Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Increase Over Quran by Khabar Wahid: Not Permissible but Obligates Action
Explaining the Hanafi ruling that ahad hadith cannot add to Quran but still obligates practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding khabar wahid and the Quran, and apply it to distinguish between fard and wajib in prayer recitation.

Core Idea
A khabar wahid cannot make a fard, but it can make a wajib — acting on it is required, but it never rivals the Quran's certainty.

This lesson explores a key usul al-fiqh principle that directly affects how we pray. The Hidayah author uses the dispute over recitation in prayer to illustrate that a single-narrator hadith (khabar wahid) cannot add a new pillar (rukn) to the Quran, but it can create an obligation (wajib). The Hanafi school reconciles both the Quranic text and the prophetic hadith without overstepping their evidentiary weight.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the usul principle
Understand the rule: increasing on the Quran via khabar wahid is not permissible for establishing a fard, but it obligates action (wajib). Note the key terms: al-ziyada 'ala al-kitab and khabar al-wahid.
This principle stems from the epistemological gap between qat'i and zanni evidence.
2
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider recitation of Fatiha and/or surah as rukn (pillar) based on ahad hadith. Their evidence is the same hadith that Hanafis use.
The dispute is not about the existence of the hadith but about its evidentiary weight.
3
Follow the Hanafi application
See how the Hanafi school applies the principle: absolute recitation of any Quranic verse is fard (from the Quranic command 'faqra'u ma tayassara'). The recitation of Fatiha and an additional surah are wajib (from ahad hadith).
This allows acting on both the Quran and the hadith without contradiction.
4
Work out the thamarah
Understand the practical result: deliberate omission of a wajib is sinful and requires sajdat al-sahw if forgetful; omission of the fard (rukn) invalidates the prayer. In Shafi'i and Maliki schools, omission of Fatiha (or surah for Maliki) invalidates the prayer.
The thamarah al-khilaf shows the real-world difference in prayer validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الزِيَادَةَ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ لَا يَجُوزُ لَكِنَّهُ يُوجِبُ الْعَمَلَ . . ترجمہ: قرآن کریم پر خبر واحد کے ساتھ زیادتی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے لیکن خبر واحد عمل کو واجب کرتی ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس اصول سے اس مسئلہ کی وضاحت کر رہے ہیں کہ نماز میں قرات قرآن کی کتنی مقدار فرض اور رکن ہے، احناف کے نزدیک مطلقاً قرات قرآن فرض ہے، لہذا کسی ایک آیت کو پڑھنے سے بھی رکن ادا ہو جائے گا سورہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا اور اس کے ساتھ سورت کا ملانا یہ دونوں احناف کے نزدیک واجبات میں سے ہیں، امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک سورہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنار کن ہے اور امام مالک رحمہ اللہ کے ہاں فاتحہ اور سورت ملانا دونوں رکن ہیں ۔ امام شافعی اور امام مالک رحمہما اللہ نے مسئلہ مذکورہ پر دلیل کے طور پر جو روایات پیش کی ہے ( جو کتاب میں موجود ہیں ) موصوف اس اصول سے ان دونوں حضرات کی پیش کردہ روایات کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ یہ روایات اخبار آحاد ہیں اور اخبار آحادظنی ہوتی ہیں اور اصول فقہ میں یہ بات مذکور ہے کہ رکن دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتا ہے نہ کہ دلیل ظنی سے، البتہ دلیل ظنی عمل کو واجب کرتی ہے اس لئے احناف کے ہاں یہ دونوں واجب ہیں۔ اگر کوئی عمد ا چھوڑے گا تو گناہ گار ہوگا اور سہوا چھوٹ جائیں تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہو گا۔ چونکہ اصول ہے کہ خبر واحد کے ذریعہ کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے ان حضرات کی پیش کردہ روایات اور احادیث سے کتاب اللہ فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ " پر زیادتی کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۰۴، ط: رحمانیہ
لكنه يوجب العمل أى لكن الحديث المذكور يوجب العمل به وبين ذلك بقوله: (فقلنا بوجوبهما) أى قلنا بوجوب قراءة الفاتحة وضم السورة حتى يأثم تاركهما إذا عمد ويلزمه سجود السهو إذا سها ، والحاصل أنما نحن عملنا بالعدل باستعمالنا بالقرآن والحديث، وأثبتنا فريضة مطلق القواءة بالنص ووجوبية قراءة الفاتحة وضم السورة بالحديث، وهذا هو العدل فى باب إعمال الأخبار ، وليس من العدل أن يعمل بأحدهما ويهمل الآخر.
البناية: كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۲ ص ۲۱۳، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
Indeed, increasing upon the Book (Quran) by a khabar wahid (single-narrator report) is not permissible, but it obligates action. Translation: Increasing upon the Quran by a khabar wahid is not permissible, but a khabar wahid obligates action.
Explanation: The author of Hidayah is explaining through this principle the issue of how much Quran recitation is fard and rukn in prayer. According to the Hanafis, reciting Quran in an absolute sense is fard, so reciting even one verse fulfills the rukn. Reciting Surat al-Fatiha and adding a surah are both wajib according to the Hanafis. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, reciting Surat al-Fatiha is a rukn, and according to Imam Malik, both Fatiha and adding a surah are rukn. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik presented as evidence certain narrations (which are in the book). The author responds to the narrations of these two scholars with this principle: that these narrations are akhbar ahad, and akhbar ahad are zanni (probable). And in usul al-fiqh it is mentioned that a rukn is established by a qat'i (definitive) proof, not by a zanni proof. However, a zanni proof obligates action. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, both are wajib. If one deliberately leaves them, he sins, and if he leaves them forgetfully, sajdat al-sahw becomes necessary. Since the principle is that increasing upon the Book of Allah through khabar wahid is not permissible, therefore the narrations and ahadith presented by these scholars cannot increase upon the Quranic verse: 'So recite whatever is easy from the Quran.'
Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sifat al-Salah, vol. 1 p. 104, Rahmaniyya: But it obligates action, i.e., but the mentioned hadith obligates action based on it. And he clarified that by saying: 'So we said that both are wajib.' That is, we said it is wajib to recite Fatiha and add a surah, such that the one who leaves them deliberately sins, and sajdat al-sahw becomes necessary if he leaves them forgetfully. The summary is that we have acted justly by using both the Quran and the hadith. We established the fard of absolute recitation by the text, and the wujub of reciting Fatiha and adding a surah by the hadith. This is justice in the chapter of implementing reports. It is not justice to act on one and neglect the other.
Al-Binaya: Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sifat al-Salah, vol. 2 p. 213, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof that addresses a foundational usul al-fiqh principle and its application to prayer recitation. The principle is that a khabar wahid (a hadith with a single narrator chain) cannot be used to add an obligation to the Quran (increase upon the Book), but it does obligate action in terms of wujub (necessary). The commentator applies this to the dispute about recitation in prayer: the Hanafi position is that absolute recitation of any Quranic verse is fard (based on the general command 'faqra'u ma tayassara'), while reciting Surat al-Fatiha and an additional surah are wajib (based on ahad hadith). The Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider these to be rukn (pillars). The Hanafi response uses the usul principle: since the proofs for Fatiha and surah are ahad hadith (zanni), they cannot create a rukn (which requires qat'i proof). Instead, they create wujub, which means deliberate omission is sinful and forgetful omission requires sajdat al-sahw. The passage quotes the Hidayah and al-Binaya to show that this is the just middle path: using both the Quran and the hadith without elevating ahad reports to the level of Quranic certainty.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith that does not reach the level of tawatur; it is narrated by one or a few chains and yields zanni knowledge.
الزيادة على الكتاب (al-ziyada 'ala al-kitab): Adding an additional obligation or ruling that is not explicitly in the Quran, based on a khabar wahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle discussed, why is reciting Surat al-Fatiha not considered fard (pillar) in prayer?
A) Because the Quran does not mention Fatiha at all
B) Because the evidence for Fatiha is from ahad hadith, which is zanni and cannot establish a rukn
C) Because prayer is valid without any recitation
D) Because the Hanafi school follows the Quran only

Key Takeaway
A khabar wahid can obligate action (wajib) but cannot establish a pillar (fard) that requires qat'i proof from Quran or tawatur.

Salah — Prayer

Khabar Wahid Cannot Add to the Qur'an: The Hanafi Ruling on Recitation in Salah
Explains that khabar wahid cannot add to Qur'an but mandates practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the status of reciting Surah al-Fatihah in prayer and explain why it is considered wajib rather than rukn, using the principle that khabar wahid cannot increase upon the Book.

Core Idea
A rukn requires qati proof; khabar wahid can only establish wujub, not fard.

This lesson examines a key usul principle from al-Hidayah: a khabar wahid (solitary hadith) cannot add to the Qur'an's ruling, but it can make an action obligatory (wajib). The principle is applied to a famous inter-madhhab dispute: is reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah in prayer a rukn (pillar) or a wajib (obligation)? Understanding this distinction is essential for knowing when a prayer must be repeated and when it can be corrected with sajdah sahw.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding qira'ah in salah: absolute recitation of any Qur'anic verse is fard/rukn; reciting al-Fatihah and adding a surah are wajib.
Absolute qira'ah is proven by the Qur'an itself (dalil qati).
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds al-Fatihah alone as rukn, and Imam Malik holds both al-Fatihah and an additional surah as rukn.
Their evidence comes from ahad hadith.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school rebuts: ahad hadith are zanni al-thubut and cannot establish a rukn, which requires qati proof (Quran, mutawatir sunnah, or ijma). Therefore, these ahad hadith establish wujub only.
This is based on the principle that khabar wahid cannot increase upon the Book.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical difference: in the Hanafi school, leaving Fatihah deliberately is a sin and requires sajdah sahw if forgotten, but the prayer remains valid. In the Shafi'i school, leaving Fatihah intentionally invalidates the prayer.
This illustrates how a difference in usul leads to different fiqh outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۱) إِنَّ الزِيَادَةَ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ لَا يَجُوزُ لَكِنَّهُ يُوجِبُ الْعَمَلَ . . ترجمہ: قرآن کریم پر خبر واحد کے ساتھ زیادتی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے لیکن خبر واحد عمل کو واجب کرتی ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس اصول سے اس مسئلہ کی وضاحت کر رہے ہیں کہ نماز میں قرات قرآن کی کتنی مقدار فرض اور رکن ہے، احناف کے نزدیک مطلقاً قرات قرآن فرض ہے، لہذا کسی ایک آیت کو پڑھنے سے بھی رکن ادا ہو جائے گا سورہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا اور اس کے ساتھ سورت کا ملانا یہ دونوں احناف کے نزدیک واجبات میں سے ہیں، امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک سورہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنار کن ہے اور امام مالک رحمہ اللہ کے ہاں فاتحہ اور سورت ملانا دونوں رکن ہیں ۔ امام شافعی اور امام مالک رحمہما اللہ نے مسئلہ مذکورہ پر دلیل کے طور پر جو روایات پیش کی ہے ( جو کتاب میں موجود ہیں ) موصوف اس اصول سے ان دونوں حضرات کی پیش کردہ روایات کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ یہ روایات اخبار آحاد ہیں اور اخبار آحادظنی ہوتی ہیں اور اصول فقہ میں یہ بات مذکور ہے کہ رکن دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتا ہے نہ کہ دلیل ظنی سے، البتہ دلیل ظنی عمل کو واجب کرتی ہے اس لئے احناف کے ہاں یہ دونوں واجب ہیں۔ اگر کوئی عمد ا چھوڑے گا تو گناہ گار ہوگا اور سہوا چھوٹ جائیں تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہو گا۔ چونکہ اصول ہے کہ خبر واحد کے ذریعہ کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے ان حضرات کی پیش کردہ روایات اور احادیث سے کتاب اللہ فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ " پر زیادتی کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۰۴، ط: رحمانیہ
لكنه يوجب العمل أى لكن الحديث المذكور يوجب العمل به وبين ذلك بقوله: (فقلنا بوجوبهما) أى قلنا بوجوب قراءة الفاتحة وضم السورة حتى يأثم تاركهما إذا عمد ويلزمه سجود السهو إذا سها ، والحاصل أنما نحن عملنا بالعدل باستعمالنا بالقرآن والحديث، وأثبتنا فريضة مطلق القواءة بالنص ووجوبية قراءة الفاتحة وضم السورة بالحديث، وهذا هو العدل فى باب إعمال الأخبار ، وليس من العدل أن يعمل بأحدهما ويهمل الآخر.
البناية: كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۲ ص ۲۱۳، ط: دار الكتب العلمية

وَمِثْلُ هَذِهِ الزِّيَادَةِ لَا تَثْبُتُ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ وَلَا بِالْقِيَاسِ، لِأَنَّ الرُّكْنِيَّةَ لَا تَثْبُتُ إِلَّا بِالنَّصَّ فَأَمَّا الْوُجُوبُ فَيَثْبُتُ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ يُوجِبُ الْعَمَلَ وَلَا يُوجِبُ عِلْمَ الْيَقِينِ، وَالرُّكْنِيَّةُ إِنَّمَا تَثْبُتُ بِمَا يُوجِبُ عِلْمَ الْيَقِينِ فَأَصْلُ الطَّوَافِ رُكُنَّ ثَابِتٌ بِالنَّيِّ، وَالطَّهَارَةُ فِيهِ تَثْبُتُ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ فَيَكُونُ مُوجِبُ الْعَمَلِ دُونَ الْعِلْمِ فَلَمْ تَصِرُ الطَّهَارَةُ رُكْنًا، وَلَكِنَّهَا وَاجِبَةٌ. المبسوط للسرخسى : كتاب المناسک، باب الطواف، ج ۴، ص ۳۸، ط: دار المعرفة
Principle: Increasing upon the Book with khabar wahid is not permissible, but it necessitates action. Translation: It is not permissible to add to the Quran through a khabar wahid, but a khabar wahid makes action obligatory. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah clarifies this principle regarding how much qira'ah in prayer is fard and rukn. According to the Hanafis, absolute qira'ah of the Qur'an is fard, so reading even one verse fulfills the rukn. Reciting Surah al-Fatihah and adding a surah are both wajib according to the Hanafis. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that reciting al-Fatihah is rukn, and Imam Malik holds that both al-Fatihah and adding a surah are rukn. They presented narrations as proof; the author responds using this principle: these narrations are ahad and zanni, and a rukn must be proven by qati proof. Zanni proof makes action obligatory, so both are wajib for Hanafis. If one deliberately leaves them, they sin; if forgotten, sajdah sahw is required. Because it is a principle that addition to the Book via khabar wahid is not permissible, the narrations cannot add to the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an'.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the status of reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah in salah. The Hanafi position: absolute qira'ah of any Qur'anic verse is fard (obligatory) and a rukn (pillar) of prayer, established by the Quranic command (dalil qati). Reciting al-Fatihah and adding a surah are wajib, proven by ahad hadith (zanni). Imam al-Shafi'i argues that al-Fatihah itself is a rukn based on ahad hadith. Imam Malik holds both al-Fatihah and adding a surah are rukn. The Hanafi response: rukn requires qati proof (Quran or mutawatir sunnah), while ahad hadith only establishes wujub (obligation but not pillar). Thus, leaving al-Fatihah or additional surah deliberately incurs sin and requires sajdah sahw if forgotten, but salah is not invalidated. The author supports this from al-Hidayah and al-Binayah, and extends the principle to tawaf: the act of tawaf is rukn by the Quran, but purity during tawaf is wajib by khabar wahid.

Key Terms
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.
رکن (rukn): A pillar of worship; its omission invalidates the act.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act proven by zanni dalil; leaving it deliberately is sinful and requires sajdah sahw if forgotten.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting Surah al-Fatihah in prayer?
A) It is fard and a rukn; leaving it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is wajib; leaving it intentionally requires sajdah sahw but prayer is valid.
C) It is sunnah; leaving it is not sinful.
D) It is mustahab; there is no consequence for leaving it.

Key Takeaway
A khabar wahid cannot raise an act to the level of rukn (pillar); it can only establish wujub (obligation), which affects the consequences of omission but not the validity of the act itself.

Salah — Prayer

The Foundation of Du'a is Concealment: Ameen in Prayer
Establishes that du'a should be silent, used for Ameen in salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on saying Ameen in prayer, explain the proof from the principle that du'a is based on concealment, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i argument and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Ameen is a du'a, and du'a is based on concealment — therefore, it is sunnah to say Ameen silently.

This passage presents a foundational principle used by the Hanafi school to determine the ruling for Ameen in prayer. Du'a is fundamentally an act of humble supplication, and the Quran instructs believers to call upon their Lord privately. Since Ameen (meaning 'O Allah, accept') is a du'a, the sunnah is to conceal it. This directly challenges the Shafi'i position that Ameen should be said aloud. By studying this dispute, you will learn how a general Quranic principle can guide specific fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the imam, follower, and latecomer all say Ameen silently. This is the mufta bihi position.
The ruling applies to all participants in congregational prayer.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
Locate the Quranic proof (7:55) and the principle that the foundation of du'a is concealment. Understand how this dalil directly supports the ruling.
The verse commands calling upon Allah 'tadarru'an wa khufyah' — in humility and privately.
3
State the Shafi'i position and their dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that Ameen is said aloud. Their proof is based on hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) said Ameen aloud.
The Shafi'i school classifies Ameen as dhikr, not du'a, hence jahr is preferred.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that those hadith are ahad (single-narrator) and do not override the general Quranic principle. The principle of concealment for du'a takes precedence.
This reflects the Hanafi usul principle that a general Quranic command (amm) is qat'i over ahad hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: in Hanafi mosques, Ameen is silent; in Shafi'i mosques, it is audible. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school.
Both positions are valid ikhtilaf; followers of each school should adhere to their own.

Source Text

This passage presents a principle used by the Hanafi school to support saying Ameen silently in prayer. Du'a is fundamentally an act of supplication, and the Quran instructs to call upon Allah privately. Since Ameen (meaning 'O Allah, accept') is a du'a, the sunnah is to say it silently. The author cites Badai' al-Sanai' and Fatawa Qadi Khan to reinforce that the original rule in dhikr and du'a is concealment. This directly contradicts Imam al-Shafi'i's view that Ameen should be said aloud.

اخفاء (ikhfa'): Concealment or quietness, as opposed to jahr (aloud).

Salah Was Not Prescribed for Rest: Principle and Application
States a principle and its application to standing after sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that salah is not for rest and apply it to identify discouraged delays in prayer movements.

Core Idea
Salah is devotion, not a break — any delay for comfort undermines its purpose.

This lesson examines a core Hanafi principle from al-Hidayah: salah was not prescribed for rest. The author uses it to derive a ruling about standing after sajdah. Understanding this principle helps you evaluate the many small pauses we might be tempted to insert in our prayer for ease, and reminds us that every movement should serve worship, not comfort.

Guided Path
1
State the principle in Arabic and English
Begin by memorizing the phrase 'Inna al-salata ma wudi'at li al-istirahah'. This is the foundation of the ruling.
2
Identify the implication given in the source
The commentary (though cut off) explains that when the worshiper completes the second sajdah, he should stand up promptly, not linger on his toes. This is one concrete application.
The principle applies to all pauses, not just standing.
3
Derive the general rule
Any movement or pause in salah done purely for rest (istirahah) contradicts the purpose of prayer and is discouraged (makruh tanzihi).
This includes sitting between sajdahs longer than necessary, or standing idly before reciting.
4
Contrast with necessary pauses
Necessary pauses for takbir, tranquility in ruku/sajdah, or catching breath due to shortness are not for rest but for proper performance — they are allowed.
The key is intention: if the pause is for devotion or need, it is fine; if for comfort, it is discouraged.

The Basis of Du'a is Concealment (Ikhfa')
Establishes the principle of concealing du'a and applies it to Ameen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying Ameen quietly, explain the Qur'anic proof, and contrast the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Du'a is fundamentally concealed; therefore Ameen, being du'a, is said quietly.

In this lesson, we examine a key legal maxim from al-Hidayah: the basis of du'a is concealment (ikhfa'). This principle shapes the Hanafi ruling on saying Ameen in prayer, which is done quietly. We will explore the Qur'anic proof (7:55) and see how the Hanafi position differs from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal maxim
What is the maxim stated at the beginning? Write it in Arabic and understand its meaning: 'Inna mabna al-du'a 'ala al-ikhfa'.'
The maxim is from al-Hidayah.
2
Define ikhfa' as it applies to du'a
Ikhfa' means concealment, saying softly so that only the speaker hears. This is the default mode for all du'a.
3
State the Hanafi ruling on Ameen
The Hanafi school holds that Ameen is said quietly by all participants in prayer (imam, follower, latecomer). This is sunnah mu'akkadah.
Contrast with the Shafi'i position that Ameen is said loudly.
4
Examine the Qur'anic proof
Quran 7:55 commands du'a with humility and secrecy (tadarru'an wa khufyatan). How does this support ikhfa' as the default?
The word 'khufyatan' indicates concealment.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings? The Hanafi follower remains quiet; the Shafi'i follower says Ameen loudly.
Both schools consider their ruling as sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The basis of du'a is concealment. Translation: The origin in du'a is concealment. Explanation: The author of Hidayah uses this principle to prove the Hanafi position that for the imam, follower, and latecomer, saying Ameen quietly is sunnah, while Imam Shafi'i holds that saying Ameen loudly is sunnah. Ameen means 'accept', and it is du'a, and the rule is that concealment is the basis in du'a. Allah says: 'Call upon your Lord in humility and privately.' Therefore, in Ameen, concealment is sunnah. Bada'i' al-Sana'i': ... Because the origin in remembrances and du'a is concealment. Fatawa Qadi Khan: ... Hidayah: ... And because it is from the category of du'a, for its meaning is 'O Allah, accept' or 'let it be so.' Allah said: 'Your supplication has been answered.' Moses was supplicating and Aaron was saying Ameen. And the sunnah in du'a is concealment. Bada'i' al-Sana'i': ...
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a qa'idah (legal maxim) from the Hidayah: du'a is fundamentally done in concealment. The commentator explains that the Hanafi school uses this principle to support the ruling that Ameen (which is a form of du'a) should be pronounced softly by all participants in congregational prayer—imam, follower, and latecomer alike. The Shafi'i school, in contrast, considers loud Ameen as sunnah. The proof cited is the Qur'anic verse (7:55) commanding du'a with humility and secrecy (tadarru'an wa khufyatan). Additional supporting texts from Bada'i' al-Sana'i' and Fatawa Qadi Khan reiterate the maxim, and the passage from Hidayah itself explains that since Ameen is a du'a (meaning 'O Allah, respond'), the practice of prophets Musa and Harun shows that one recites and the other says Ameen softly. Thus concealment remains the established sunnah.

Key Terms
إِخْفَاء (ikhfa'): Concealment; saying du'a or Ameen in a low voice so that only the speaker hears.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because it is wajib to be silent.
D) Because the Quran commands loud du'a.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that Ameen is said quietly is rooted in the Qur'anic principle that du'a is based on concealment.

The Ruling on Jalsah al-Istirahah: A Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on jalsah al-istirahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on jalsah al-istirahah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the maxim 'prayer was not instituted for rest'.

Core Idea
Jalsah al-istirahah is not sunnah for the healthy; prayer is for worship, not rest.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: should a worshipper sit briefly after the second prostration before standing? The Hanafi school, based on a foundational maxim, argues that such sitting is only for those with an excuse. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, considers it a recommended act. We will explore both proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on jalsah al-istirahah: for a healthy person, it is makruh tanzih to sit; the worshipper should rise directly on the balls of the feet.
This is based on the maxim that prayer is not for rest.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i considers jalsah al-istirahah as mustahabb (recommended), citing the Prophet's practice of sitting briefly.
The Shafi'i proof is a hadith of the Prophet sitting.
3
Explain the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response interprets the Shafi'i hadith as applying to the Prophet's old age or weakness, and prioritizes the maxim and the Prophet's other practice of rising on the front of his feet.
The maxim 'prayer was not instituted for rest' overrides the apparent meaning of the sitting hadith.
4
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis omit the sitting for healthy persons; Shafi'is include it as a sunnah. For the excused (elderly, ill), Hanafis permit sitting.
This difference affects daily prayer practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ مَا وُضِعَتْ لِلِاسْتِرَاحَةِ.
ترجمہ: نماز استراحت کے لئے وضع نہیں کی گئی ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس اصول سے یہ بتانا چاہتے ہیں کہ جب نماز پڑھنے والا اطمینان سے سجدہ کر لے تو کھڑا ہونے کے لئے تکبیر کہے ، اور سجدہ ثانیہ سے فراغت کے بعد اپنے پنجوں کے = بل سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے، نہ بیٹھے اور نہ اپنے ہاتھوں سے زمین پر ٹیک لگائے ، کیونکہ یہ بیٹھنا استراحت کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور نماز استراحت اور آرام کے لئے وضع نہیں کی گئی جیسا کہ اصول میں مذکور ہے۔ البتہ عذر کی حالت اور معذور کی حالت اس سے مستفی ہے۔
وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ: يَجْلِسُ بَعْدَهَا جِلْسَةٌ خَفِيفَةً وَتُسَمَّى جِلْسَةَ الِاسْتِرَاحَةِ، وَيَقُومُ مُعْتَمِدًا، لأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فَعَلَ كَذَا، وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يَنْهَضُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى صَدْرٍ قَدَمَيْهِ وَلَانَّ الصَّلَاةَ مَا وُضِعَتْ لِلاسْتِرَاحَةِ، وَمَا رَوَاهُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى حَالَةِ الضُّعْفِ وَالْكِبَر.
Prayer was not instituted for rest. Translation: Prayer was not prescribed for rest. Explanation: The author of Hidayah wants to explain with this principle that when the praying person performs sajdah with tranquility, he should say takbir for standing, and after the second sajdah he should stand up straight on the balls of his feet, not sit and not lean on his hands, because such sitting is for rest, and prayer was not instituted for rest and comfort, as mentioned in the principle. However, the state of excuse and the state of the excused are exempt from this. Al-Shafi'i said: He sits briefly after it, called jalsah al-istirahah, and stands leaning, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so. And our (Hanafi) proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to rise in prayer on the front of his feet, and because prayer was not instituted for rest. And what he narrated is interpreted as the case of weakness and old age.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling-based maxim: salat was not designed for rest. The commentator applies it to the issue of jalsah al-istirahah—the brief sitting after the second sajdah before standing for the next rak'ah. The Hanafi position is that a healthy person should not sit; rather, he should rise directly onto the balls of his feet, supporting himself on his hands only if needed. The Shafi'i school, however, considers this brief sitting (jalsah al-istirahah) as sunnah based on the Prophet's practice. The Hanafi response distinguishes that the Prophet's action in that regard was due to old age or weakness, not the general norm. The maxim 'prayer was not instituted for rest' serves as the foundational evidence for the Hanafi preference.

Key Terms
جِلْسَةُ الِاسْتِرَاحَة (jalsah al-istirahah): A brief sitting after the second sajdah before standing for the next rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is sunnah in every prayer.
B) It is only for those who are weak or elderly.
C) It is wajib.
D) It is never allowed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school omits jalsah al-istirahah for the healthy, based on the maxim that prayer is for worship, not rest.

The Virtue of Difficulty in Worship: The Iftirash Posture
Establishes virtue of difficulty in worship, applied to sitting posture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preferred sitting posture in prayer and explain how the principle 'what is more difficult on the body is more virtuous' supports it.

Core Idea
Physical difficulty in worship amplifies reward; thus the more demanding posture (iftirash) is preferred.

The Hanafi school holds that the worshipper should sit in the same posture for both the first and final tashahhud: laying the left foot and raising the right foot upright. This posture, called iftirash, is slightly more demanding on the body. The Hidayah author invokes a powerful qa'idah: difficulty in worship increases virtue. In this lesson, we unpack the evidence from the hadith of Aisha and the principle that ties difficulty to reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qa'idah and its immediate application
The passage opens with the maxim 'What is more difficult on the body is more virtuous.' The commentator then applies this to the sitting posture: the worshipper should sit in the same way as in the first sitting (iftirash) because it is more difficult than alternative postures.
This qa'idah is a recurring principle in Hanafi fiqh, used to prefer the heavier option among permissible choices in worship.
2
Locate the Hanafi position on the sitting posture
The Hanafi position is that the worshipper sits with the left foot laid flat and the right foot upright in both the first and final sittings. This is declared mustahabb (recommended).
Some other schools use a different posture (tawarruk) for the final sitting, but Hanafis maintain consistency.
3
Examine the primary dalil: the hadith of Aisha
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's sitting: he laid his left foot and sat on it, and raised the right foot upright. This is taken as the normative practice.
The Arabic verb 'iftarasha' means to spread, hence the term iftirash.
4
Understand how the qa'idah supports the preference
The passage argues that iftirash is more difficult on the body than alternative postures (like resting on both feet). Since difficulty in worship is virtuous, iftirash is preferred. Reports of the Prophet sitting differently in old age are interpreted as exceptions due to excuse.
This shows that the qa'idah is used as a tarjih (preference) tool, not to create obligation.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) consider tawarruk (sitting on the buttocks with both feet tucked under) for the final sitting as sunnah. Hanafis respond that the Prophet's alternative posture was due to old age, so the original practice is iftirash.
The difference is rooted in how each school interprets the conflicting narrations and the weight given to the 'difficulty' principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ مَا كَانَ عَلَى الْبَدَن أَشَقُّ أَوْلَى.
ترجمہ: جو بدن پر زیادہ شاق ہو وہ افضل ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس اصول سے یہ بتلانا چاہتے ہیں کہ مصلی قعدہ اخیرہ میں کس ہیئت پر بیٹھے ؟ تو فرمایا کہ مصلی جس ہیئت پر قعدہ اولی میں بیٹھا تھا اُسی ہیئت پر قعدہ ثانیہ میں بیٹھے یعنی بائیں پاؤں کو بچھا کر اس پر بیٹھ جائے اور دائیں پاؤں کو کھڑا رکھے ، اس ہیئت کے ساتھ بیٹھنا بدن پر زیادہ شاق ہے اور عبادت میں نفس پر جو زیادہ شاق ہو وہ افضل ہے، اس لئے اس ہیئت کے ساتھ بیٹھنا افضل ہے۔

وَإِنْ شَاء أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ التَّرْوِيَةِ وَمَا قَدَّمَ إحْرَامُهُ بِالْحَجِّ فَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ لأَنَّ فِيهِ إِظْهَارَ الْمُسَارَعَةِ وَالرَّغْبَةِ فِي الْعِبَادَةِ، وَلِأَنَّهُ أَشَقُّ عَلَى الْبَدَن
المبسوط للسرخسی کتاب المناسک ج۴ ص ۳۲، ط: دار المعرفة وَأَمَّا صَوْمُ يَوْمٍ وَإِفْطَارُ يَوْمٍ فَهُوَ مُسْتَحَتْ، وَهُوَ صَوْمُ سَيِّدِنَا دَاوُد عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يَصُومُ يَوْمًا وَيُفْطِرُ يَوْمًا، وَلَأَنَّهُ أَشَقُّ عَلَى الْبَدَن.
بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الصوم، فصل أنواع الصيام، ج ۲ ص ۷۹، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
What is more difficult on the body is more virtuous. Translation: What is more burdensome on the body is superior. Explanation: The author of Hidayah wants to explain with this principle what posture the worshipper should sit in during the final sitting. He said that the worshipper should sit in the same posture as in the first sitting: laying the left foot and sitting on it, and raising the right foot upright. This posture is more difficult on the body, and in worship, what is more difficult on oneself is more virtuous, so sitting in this posture is more virtuous. And our (Hanafi) proof is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that she described the sitting of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in prayer: when he sat, he would lay his left foot and sit on it, and raise his right foot upright. And what is narrated contrary to this is interpreted as the case of excuse due to old age, and because sitting in the manner we described is more difficult on the body. And if one wishes, he may enter ihram for Hajj before the day of Tarwiyah, and what is earlier is better, because it shows haste and desire in worship, and because it is more difficult on the body. Al-Mabsut: ... As for fasting one day and breaking one day, it is mustahabb, and it is the fast of our master Dawud (peace be upon him); he used to fast one day and break one day, and because it is more difficult on the body. Bada'i' al-Sana'i': ...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents the qa'idah that physical difficulty in worship increases reward. The commentator applies it to the sitting posture in the final tashahhud (qa'dah akheerah). The Hanafi position is that the worshipper sits with the left foot laid flat and the right foot upright (iftirash), the same posture as the first sitting. This is more difficult than resting on both feet, hence more virtuous. The hadith of Aisha is cited as evidence, while reports suggesting alternative postures are interpreted as due to the Prophet's old age. The principle is further illustrated with examples from Hajj (earlier ihram is better) and fasting (fast of Dawud, alternate-day fasting, is mustahabb because of difficulty). Thus, the maxim is a general usul applied across different acts of worship.

Key Terms
افْتِرَاش (iftirash): Sitting on the left foot with the right foot upright.
أَشَقُّ (ashaqqu): More difficult, more burdensome (superlative of shaqq).
مُسْتَحَبّ (mustahabb): Recommended, preferred (legal category between sunnah and mubah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it is easier.

C) Because the Quran commands it.
D) Because it is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The more difficult a permissible act of worship is on the body, the greater its reward, as exemplified by the iftirash sitting posture in salah.

The Principle: Harder Acts Are More Virtuous in Worship
Establishes the principle that what is harder on the body is more virtuous in worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that harder acts are more virtuous in worship, apply it to the sitting posture (iftrash), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In worship, what is harder on the body is more virtuous — the iftrash posture is preferred because it is more taxing.

This lesson explores a foundational Hanafi principle: the more physically demanding action in worship is more meritorious. The immediate application is the sitting posture (iftrash) in both tashahhuds, which is harder on the body than alternative postures. We will examine the evidence and the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sitting in tashahhud. The Hanafi ruling is that a man should sit in the iftrash posture (left foot spread, right foot erect) in both the first and final sittings. This is sunnah muakkadah.
The ruling is not fard or wajib; the prayer is valid with any sitting posture.
2
Understand the governing principle
The principle is: 'Whatever is harder on the body is more virtuous' (إِنَّ مَا كَانَ عَلَى الْبَدَن أَشَقُّ أَوْلَىٰ). This is derived from the hadith and applied to worship.
Worship is not prescribed for rest or ease.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is the hadith of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) describing the Prophet's sitting posture: 'When he sat, he laid his left foot flat and sat on it, and erected his right foot.'
This is a sahih hadith (ahad), zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
The Shafi'i school holds that after the second prostration, one should sit briefly (jalsat al-istirahah) and then stand with support from the hands.
They cite a hadith that the Prophet did this.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the Shafi'i hadith as applying only to the elderly or weak due to old age or illness. The general rule is that prayer is not for rest, and the iftrash posture is harder and therefore more virtuous.
The hadith of Aisha is given priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۷۴) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ عَلَى الْبَدَن أَشَقُّ أَوْلَى.

وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ: يَجْلِسُ بَعْدَهَا جِلْسَةٌ خَفِيفَةً وَتُسَمَّى جِلْسَةَ الِاسْتِرَاحَةِ، وَيَقُومُ مُعْتَمِدًا، لأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فَعَلَ كَذَا، وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يَنْهَضُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى صَدْرٍ قَدَمَيْهِ وَلَانَّ الصَّلَاةَ مَا وُضِعَتْ لِلاسْتِرَاحَةِ، وَمَا رَوَاهُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى حَالَةِ الضُّعْفِ وَالْكِبَر. مجمع الأنهر : كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۹۹، ط: دار إحياء التراث] الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۱۴ ، ۱۱۴، ط: رحمانیہ وَلَنَا حَدِيثُ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهَا أَنَّهَا وَصَفَتْ قُعُودَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ فَذَكَرَتْ أَنَّهُ كَانَ إِذَا قَعَدَ افْتَرَضَ رَجُلَهُ الْيُسْرَى وَيَقْعُدُ عَلَيْهَا وَيَنْصِبُ الْيُمْنَى نَصَبًا وَمَا رُوِيَ بِخِلَافِهِ فَهُوَ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى حَالَةِ الْعُذْرِ لِلْكِبَرِ وَلِأَنَّ الْقُعُودَ عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي بَيَّنَّا أَشُقُّ عَلَى الْبَدَنِ.
المبسوط للسرخسی کتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ا ص ۲۵، ط: دار المعرفة وَإِنْ شَاء أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ التَّرْوِيَةِ وَمَا قَدَّمَ إحْرَامُهُ بِالْحَجِّ فَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ لأَنَّ فِيهِ إِظْهَارَ الْمُسَارَعَةِ وَالرَّغْبَةِ فِي الْعِبَادَةِ، وَلِأَنَّهُ أَشَقُّ عَلَى الْبَدَن.
المبسوط للسرخسی کتاب المناسک ج۴ ص ۳۲، ط: دار المعرفة وَأَمَّا صَوْمُ يَوْمٍ وَإِفْطَارُ يَوْمٍ فَهُوَ مُسْتَحْسَنٌ، وَهُوَ صَوْمُ سَيِّدِنَا دَاوُد عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يَصُومُ يَوْمًا وَيُفْطِرُ يَوْمًا، وَلَأَنَّهُ أَشَقُّ عَلَى الْبَدَن.

Rather, he should stand up straight, not sit, and not support himself with his hands on the ground, because this sitting is for rest, and prayer was not prescribed for rest and comfort, as mentioned in the principles. However, the state of excuse and the disabled are exempt from this. (74) Verily, whatever is harder on the body is more virtuous. Translation: That which is more taxing on the body is more excellent. Explanation: The author of Al-Hidayah intends by this principle to clarify how the worshipper should sit in the final sitting. He says: The worshipper should sit in the final sitting in the same posture as the first sitting, i.e., spread the left foot and sit on it, and keep the right foot upright. Sitting in this manner is harder on the body, and in worship, what is more taxing on oneself is more virtuous. Therefore, sitting in this manner is more virtuous. Al-Shafi'i said: After the second prostration, he sits lightly, called the sitting of rest, and stands up relying on his hands, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so. Our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to rise in prayer on the fronts of his feet, and that prayer was not prescribed for rest, and what he narrated is interpreted as due to weakness and old age. [Majma' al-Anhur: Book of Prayer, Chapter on Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 99] Al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter on Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 114, Rahmaniyyah edition. And our proof is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that she described the sitting of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in prayer, and she mentioned that when he sat, he would lay his left foot flat and sit on it, and erect his right foot upright. And what is reported contrary to this is interpreted as due to excuse of old age. And because sitting in the manner we described is harder on the body. Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi: Book of Prayer, Chapter on Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 25, Dar al-Ma'rifah. And if he wishes, he may assume ihram for Hajj before the day of Tarwiyah, and advancing his ihram for Hajj is better, because it shows haste and desire in worship, and because it is harder on the body. Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi: Book of Rituals, vol. 4 p. 32, Dar al-Ma'rifah. As for fasting one day and breaking fast one day, it is recommended, and it is the fast of our master Dawud (peace be upon him) who used to fast one day and break fast one day, and because it is harder on the body. Bada'i' al-Sana'i': Book of Fasting, Chapter on Types of Fasting, vol. 2 p. 79, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyyah.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that establishes a key Hanafi principle: in worship, the more physically demanding action is more meritorious. The context is the sitting posture in prayer. The Hanafi school holds that in both the first and final sittings (tashahhud), the worshipper should sit in the same manner: spread the left foot under the buttocks and sit on it, with the right foot erect (iftrash). This is because it is harder on the body, and worship is not intended for rest. The author contrasts this with the Shafi'i view that after the second prostration, one should sit briefly (jalsat al-istirahah) and then stand up using the hands. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's sitting, and the principle that prayer is not for rest. The Shafi'i narration is interpreted as applying only to the elderly or weak. The principle is then applied to other acts: performing Hajj before the day of Tarwiyah is better because it shows haste and is harder, and the fast of Dawud (alternate days) is recommended because it is harder on the body than continuous fasting.

Key Terms
افتراش (iftrāsh): In this text, it means to spread the left foot flat on the ground and sit on it, keeping the right foot erect.
جلسة الاستراحة (jalsat al-istirāḥah): A brief sitting after the second prostration before standing for the next rak'ah, resting on the hands.
أشق (ashaqq): More difficult, more taxing, harder on the body.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers actions that are harder on the body in worship, exemplified by the iftrash sitting posture in both tashahhuds.

Du'a in Prayer: Avoid Human-Like Requests
Distinguishes permissible du'a from human speech in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion to distinguish permissible du'a from impermissible human-like speech in prayer, using the Quranic proof from Surah Al-i-Imran 3:135.

Core Idea
In prayer, du'a must be for what only Allah can grant; worldly requests resemble human speech and are disliked.

Du'a in prayer is a profound act of worship, but the Hanafi school teaches that not every request is appropriate. The key is whether the request could be made to another human. If yes, it resembles ordinary speech and detracts from the sanctity of prayer. This lesson unpacks the criterion and its Quranic foundation, ensuring your du'a remains in harmony with the spirit of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making du'a after tashahhud in prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that du'a should avoid words that resemble ordinary human speech (kalām al-nās).
This is a rule about the content of du'a, not its permissibility overall.
2
Understand the criterion
The criterion is whether the request is impossible (muḥāl) to ask from a human being. If it is impossible (e.g., forgiveness of sins), the du'a is appropriate. If it is possible (e.g., marriage, employment), it resembles human speech and is disliked.
The test is based on logical possibility, not custom.
3
Apply the criterion to examples
Examples: 'O Allah, forgive me' is permissible because forgiveness can only come from Allah. 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so' is disliked because marriage can be arranged by humans.
Note that the disliked nature applies to the prayer context; outside prayer, such du'a is fine.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
The proof is the verse 'وَمَنْ يَغْفِرُ الذُّنُوبَ إِلَّا الله' (And who forgives sins except Allah?). This shows forgiveness is exclusive to Allah, making such requests suitable for prayer.
The verse is from Surah Al-i-Imran 3:135, but the lesson uses it as a general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۵) إِنَّ مَا لَا يَسْتَحِيلُ سُؤَالُهُ مِنَ الْعِبَادِ يَشْبَهُ كَلَامَ النَّاسِ وَيَسْتَحِيلُ لَيْسَ مِنْ كَلامِهم.
ترجمہ: جس چیز کا مانگنا بندوں سے محال نہ ہو تو یہ کلام الناس کے مشابہ ہے، اور جس چیز کا مانگنا بندوں سے محال ہو تو یہ کلام الناس کے مشابہ نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس بات کی وضاحت فرمارہے ہیں کہ کن الفاظ میں دعا کرنی چاہئے اور کن میں نہیں ؟ تو فرمایا کہ درود کے بعد ایسے الفاظ کے ساتھ دعا نہ کی جائے جو لوگوں کے کلام کے مشابہ ہو ، پھر کون سی دعا کلام الناس سے مشابہت رکھتی ہے اور کون سی نہیں ، تو اس کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ جن چیزوں کا بندوں سے مانگنا محال نہ ہو جیسے اللَّهُمَّ زَوِّجْنِي فُلَانَةً (اے الله ! فلاں عورت سے میری شادی کرادیجئے) ، مجھے نوکری دلا دیجئے وغیرہ ، اور اس طرح کے سوالات چونکہ بندوں سے کئے جاسکتے ہیں اس لئے یہ کلام الناس کے مشابہ ہوں گے اور ان کلمات کے ذریعے دعا مانگنا مناسب نہیں ہے، البتہ وہ سوالات جن کا تعلق صرف اللہ کی ذات سے ہے، جیسے اے اللہ ! میری مغفرت فرمادیجئے، میرے گناہوں کو معاف فرمادیجئے ، یہ اور اس طرح کی دعاؤں کا قبول کرنا چونکہ بندوں کی طرف سے محال ہے، اس لئے یہ کلام خداوندی کے مشابہ ہوں گے اور ان کے ذریعے دعا کرنا بھی صحیح ہوگا۔
الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۱۵، ط: رحمانیه مَا يُشْبِهُ كَلَامَ النَّاسِ هُوَ مَا لَا يَسْتَحِيلُ سُؤَالُهُ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ تَعَالَى كَقَوْلِهِ أَعْطِنِي كَذَا أَوْ زَوِّجْنِي امْرَأَةً، وَمَا لَا يُشْبِهُ كَلَامَ النَّاسِ هُوَ مَا يَسْتَحِيلُ سُؤَالُهُ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ كَقَوْلِهِ: اللَّهُمَّ اغْفِرُ لِي وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الصلاة، فصل بيان من يجب عليه تكبير التشريق، ج ۱ ص ۲۱۳، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
وَفَسَّرُوهُ بِمَا لَا يَسْتَحِيلُ سُؤَالُهُ مِنَ الْعِبَادِ نَحْوَ أَعْطِنِي كَذَا وَزَوِّجْنِي امْرَأَةً وَمَا لَا يُشْبِهُ كَلَامَهُمُ مَا يَسْتَحِيلُ سُؤَالُهُ مِنْهُمْ نَحْوَ اغْفِرْ لِي ، لأَنَّهُ يَخْتَصُّ بِهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى وَمَنْ يَغْفِرُ الذُّنُوبَ إِلَّا الله).
البحر الرائق: كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة ، ج ۱ ص ۳۵۰، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي]
(75) Verily, what is not impossible to ask from the servants resembles the speech of people, and what is impossible is not from their speech. Translation: A thing whose asking from servants is not impossible resembles human speech, and a thing whose asking from servants is impossible does not resemble human speech. Explanation: The author of Al-Hidayah is clarifying which words one should make du'a with and which not. He said that after the salutation (durud), one should not make du'a with words that resemble human speech. Then, which du'a resembles human speech and which does not? He said: Things whose asking from servants is not impossible, such as 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so,' 'Give me a job,' etc. Because such requests can be made from servants, they resemble human speech, and it is not appropriate to make du'a with these words. However, those requests that pertain only to Allah, such as 'O Allah, forgive me,' 'Forgive my sins' — since acceptance of these from servants is impossible, they resemble divine speech, and making du'a with them is correct. Al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter on Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 115, Rahmaniyyah. 'What resembles the speech of people is what is not impossible to ask from other than Him, like saying give me such-and-such or marry me to a woman. And what does not resemble the speech of people is what is impossible to ask from other than Him, like saying O Allah forgive me and the like.' Bada'i' al-Sana'i': Book of Prayer, Chapter on Explanation of Who Must Recite Takbir al-Tashriq, vol. 1 p. 213, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyyah. And they interpreted it as that which is not impossible to ask from servants, like 'give me such-and-such' and 'marry me to a woman'; and that which does not resemble their speech is that which is impossible to ask from them, like 'forgive me', because it is exclusive to Him, the Exalted. Allah said: 'And who forgives sins except Allah?' Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Book of Prayer, Chapter on Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 350, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that provides a criterion for permissible du'a during prayer. The Hanafi school holds that after the tashahhud and salawat (durud), one may make du'a, but only with words that do not resemble ordinary human speech. The test is: if the request could be made from a human being (like asking for marriage or employment), it is considered 'kalam al-nas' and is inappropriate in prayer. However, if the request is something only Allah can grant (like forgiveness of sins), it is suitable. The proof is derived from the Quranic verse 'Who forgives sins except Allah?' and the understanding that prayer is a sacred act not intended for worldly requests that could be made from people. This principle ensures that the sanctity of prayer is maintained by avoiding speech that is mundane.

Key Terms
کلام الناس (kalām al-nās): In this context, it refers to speech that is ordinary human talk, such as requesting worldly matters that can be asked from other humans.
محال (muḥāl): Impossible; here it means impossible to be fulfilled by a human being, like forgiveness of sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following du'as is considered inappropriate (resembling human speech) in Hanafi prayer?
A) اللَّهُمَّ اغْفِرْ لِي (O Allah, forgive me)
B) اللَّهُمَّ ارْحَمْنِي (O Allah, have mercy on me)
C) اللَّهُمَّ زَوِّجْنِي فُلَانَةً (O Allah, marry me to so-and-so)
D) اللَّهُمَّ اهْدِنِي (O Allah, guide me)

Key Takeaway
Du'a in prayer must be limited to requests exclusive to Allah to preserve its sacred character.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Salam Address is for Those Present in Prayer
Definition of a principle with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the principle 'إن الخطاب حظ الحاضرين' and apply it to determine who should be intended when saying salam in prayer, including the intra-Hanafi exception for women.

Core Idea
The salam in prayer addresses only those present and participating in the prayer, not all Muslims.

This lesson introduces a key principle from Al-Hidayah about the intention during the salam in prayer. The author explains that the greeting 'al-salamu alaykum' is specifically for those who are present and share in the prayer—men, women, and angels. However, a later ruling within the Hanafi school excludes women due to the discontinuation of their attendance in congregation. Understanding this principle helps you correctly form the intention and appreciate how rulings adapt to changing circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle and Its Legal Context
First, recognize that the passage defines a legal principle: the address (خطاب) in salam is the portion (حظ) of those present (حاضرين). This is a rule about intention (niyyah) during the salam. Note that the salam is a wajib element of the prayer, and its validity depends on correct intention.
The principle is quoted in Arabic and then expanded with commentary.
2
Determine Who Qualifies as ‘Present’ (Hadirun)
The text specifies that 'present' includes (1) men and women who are participating in the prayer, (2) the guardian angels (حفظة) who are also present. This excludes anyone not involved in the prayer, even if they are in the mosque but not praying.
The term ‘sharika fi salatihi’ (share in his prayer) is key.
3
Apply the Principle to the Intention in Salam
When turning the head to the right, intend those on the right side (men, women, angels) who have a share in your prayer. Similarly for the left. This is based on the hadith: ‘Actions are by intentions.’
The intention is made for each salam separately.
4
Recognise the Intra-Hanafi Ijtihad Regarding Women
The author notes that in his time (and per later scholars), women should not be intended because their presence in congregation has been abandoned and is considered makruh. This is a ruling based on ‘urf (custom) and prevents fitna, not a change in the principle itself.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school based on changed circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۶) إِنَّ الْخِطَابَ حَظِّ الْحَاضِرِينَ.
ترجمہ: خطاب حاضرین کا حصہ ہے۔
تشریح: اس اصول سے صاحب ہدایہ اس بات کی وضاحت فرمارہے ہیں کہ مصلی تشہد، درود اور دعا کے بعد دونوں طرف سلام پھیرے، پہلے دائیں جانب پھر بائیں جانب ، اور پہلا سلام پھیرتے ہوئے ان لوگوں کی نیت کرے جو اس کے دائیں جانب ہیں خواہ مرد ہوں یا عورتیں ، اور ملائکہ حفظہ کی نیت کرے، اور اسی طرح بائیں جانب سلام پھیر تے وقت ان لوگوں کی نیت کرے جو اس کی بائیں طرف ہیں کیونکہ اعمال کا دارومدار نیت پر ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارے زمانے میں عورتوں کی نیت نہ کرے کیونکہ اس زمانہ میں عورتوں کا جماعت میں حاضر ہونا با جماع متاخرین متروک ہے، اور جو مسلمان نماز میں شریک نہیں ان کی بھی نیت نہ کرے، اس لئے کہ السلام علیکم میں جو خطاب ہے وہ حاضرین کے لئے ہے، اور اصول ہے کہ خطاب حاضرین کا حصہ ہے، اس لئے جو لوگ نماز میں شریک ہیں ان کو سلام شامل ہوگا اور جولوگ شریک نہیں ان کو یہ شامل نہیں ہو گا۔
(لأن الخطاب حظ الحاضرين هذا التعليل يتأتى فى النساء لأنهن منعن عن الحضور في هذا الزمان، ولا يتأتى فيمن لا شركة له فى الصلاة، لأن عدم الشركة في الصلاة لا يستلزم الغيبة. [البناية: كتاب الصلاة، صفة الصلاة، ج ۲ ص ۲۸۶، ط: دار الكتب العلمية وَأَمَّا النِّيَّةُ فَيَنْوِى بِكُلِّ تَسْلِيمَةٍ مَنْ فِي تِلْكَ الْجِهَةِ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ وَالنِّسَاءِ وَالْحَفَظَةِ الْحَاضِرِينَ الَّذِينَ لَهُمُ شَرِكَةً فِي صَلَاتِهِ، لِأَنَّ الْأَعْمَالَ بِالنِّيَّاتِ وَهُوَ لَمَّا اشْتَغَلَ بِمُنَاجَاةِ رَبِّهِ صَارَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْغَائِبِ عَنْهُمْ فَيُسَلِّمُ عَلَيْهِمْ عِندَ التَّحَلَّل، لأنَّهُ صَارَ حَاضِرًا وَقَالُوا لَا يَنُوى النِّسَاءَ فِي زَمَانِنَا لِعَدَمِ حُضُورِهِنَّ الْجَمَاعَةَ وَلِكَرَاهِيَتِهِ وَإِنَّمَا حُصَّ الْحَاضِرُونَ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَصْلُحُ خِطَابًا لِلْغَائِبَيْنِ. تبيين الحقائق كتاب الصلاة، صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۲۶ ، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۱۷، ط: رحمانیہ
Translation: The address is the portion of those present. Explanation: Through this principle, the author of Hidayah explains that the one praying, after tashahhud, darud, and supplication, should turn salam to both sides, first to the right then to the left. While turning the first salam, he should intend those who are on his right side, whether men or women, and intend the guardian angels. Similarly, when turning salam to the left, he should intend those on his left side because actions are by intentions. The author of Hidayah says: In our time, he should not intend women because in this time women's presence in congregation is abandoned by the later scholars. And he should not intend those Muslims who did not participate in the prayer, because the address in 'al-salamu alaykum' is for those present, and the principle is that the address is the portion of those present. Therefore, those who participated in the prayer are included in the salam, and those who did not are not included. (Because the address is for those present – this reasoning applies to women because they are prevented from attending in this time, and does not apply to those who have no share in the prayer because the lack of share in prayer does not necessitate absence. [Al-Binayah: Book of Prayer, Description of Prayer, vol. 2 p. 286] And as for intention: he intends with each salam those in that direction from men, women, and the guardian angels who are present and have a share in his prayer, because actions are by intentions. And when he engages in invoking his Lord, he becomes as if absent from them, so he greets them upon concluding because he became present. And they said: He should not intend women in our time due to their lack of attending the congregation and its dislike. And only those present are specified because the address is not suitable for the absent. [Tabyin al-Haqaiq: Book of Prayer, Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 126] Al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Section on Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 117)
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage explains the first principle (usul) from Al-Hidayah regarding the salam in prayer. The principle 'إن الخطاب حظ الحاضرين' means that the address (salam) is only for those who are present, i.e., those participating in the prayer. The ruling is that one should intend with each salam the people (men, women, and angels) who are present on that side. However, due to a change in practice, later scholars said that women should not be intended because they no longer attend the congregational prayer. Also, those not participating in the prayer are not included. This is supported by the principle that the address is for the present. The commentary cites various Hanafi sources: Al-Binayah and Tabyin al-Haqaiq, showing the continuity of the school's position.

Key Terms
الخطاب (al-khitab): The address or speech directed to someone; here it refers to the salam greeting 'al-salamu alaykum'.
حظ (hazz): Portion, share, or lot; the address is assigned to those present.
حاضرين (hadirin): Those present; here specifically those who are participating in the prayer (including angels).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'إن الخطاب حظ الحاضرين', who should be intended when saying the first salam to the right?
A) All Muslims everywhere
B) Only men present in the prayer
C) Those present on the right side including men, women, and angels
D) Only the angels

Key Takeaway
The salam in prayer is exclusively for those who are present and participating in the prayer, including angels, with an intra-Hanafi exception for women when their attendance is abandoned by custom.

Salah — Prayer

Giving a Choice Contradicts Obligation in Prayer
Proves salam is wajib not fard via the principle that choice negates obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the salam in prayer is wajib not fard, using the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the principle that giving a choice contradicts obligation, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Giving a choice in an act negates its obligation; the salam is wajib not fard because the Prophet gave a choice after tashahhud.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi usul principle: 'Giving a choice contradicts obligation.' The author of Al-Hidayah applies this to the salam in prayer, distinguishing between fard (pillar) and wajib (necessary). We will trace the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, see how it counters the Shafi'i position, and understand the epistemological weight of the evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on salam
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding the salam in prayer: it is wajib, not fard or rukn. The prayer is complete before salam according to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
Remember: fard requires qat'i proof, wajib requires zanni proof.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that salam is a rukn and fard. This is the opposing position.
The Shafi'i proof is the hadith 'tahrimatuha al-takbir'.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
Analyze the hadith: after tashahhud, the Prophet said the prayer is complete and gave Ibn Mas'ud a choice to stand or sit. This indicates that no further obligatory act (including salam) is fard.
The principle: giving a choice (takhayyur) negates both fardiyyah and wujub.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafis accept the other hadith but classify it as khabar wahid. Since khabar wahid provides zanni knowledge, it can only establish wujub, not fardiyyah, because fardiyyah requires qat'i proof.
This shows the Hanafi usul distinction between fard and wajib based on certainty.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, omitting salam intentionally: Hanafis require sajdah sahw (or the prayer is valid but deficient), while Shafi'is invalidate the prayer. Also, the distinction affects other rulings where fard/wajib differ.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۷) إِنَّ التَّخْسِيرَ يُنَافِى الْفَرْضِيَّةَ وَالْوُجُوبَ .
الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة ، ج ا ص ۱۱۶، ط: رحمانیه
ترجمہ کسی چیز کا اختیار دینا یہ فرضیت اور وجوب کے منافی ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اصول مذکورہ سے حضرات احناف کے مسلک کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ احناف کے نزدیک مصلی جب سلام پھیرتا ہے تو اُسے لفظ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمُ ادا کرنا واجب ہے فرض نہیں ، امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک لفظ سلام کہنا رکن اور فرض ہے نہ کہ واجب، وجوب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے جب حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی تو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا " إِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا أَوْ فَعَلْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُكَ فَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقُومَ فَقُمْ وَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقْعُدَ فَاقْعُدُ " اس میں آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے سلام سے نماز پوری ہونے کا حکم لگایا ہے اور اس کو بیٹھنے اور کھڑے ہونے کے درمیان اختیار دیا ہے اور اصول ہے کہ اختیار دینا کسی چیز کے فرض اور واجب ہونے کے منافی ہے، لہذ ا مقدار تشہد کے بعد سلام وغیرہ کوئی چیز فرض نہیں ہے۔ ہم نے وجوب کو احتیاطاً اس حدیث کی وجہ سے ثابت کیا ہے جس کو امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ نے بطور دلیل ذکر کیا ہے، یعنی تَحْرِيمُهَا التَّكْبِيرُ ، تو یہ حدیث خبر واحد ہے اور خبر واحد سے وجوب تو ثابت ہو جاتا ہے مگر فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ، اس لئے کہ ثبوتِ فرضیت کے لئے قطعی الدلالت نص کی ضرورت ہوتی ہے۔
وَلَنَا مَا رَوَيْنَا مِنْ حَدِيثِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: لَمَّا عَلَّمَهُ العَشَهدَ قَالَ لَهُ: إِذَا قُلْت هَذَا أَوْ فَعَلْت هَذَا فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُكَ، فَإِنْ شِئت أَن تَقُومَ فَقُمْ وَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقْعُدَ فَاقْعُدُ. وَجُهُ التَّمَسُّكِ بِهِ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ حَكَمَ بِتَمَامِ الصَّلَاةِ قَبْلَ السَّلَامِ وَخَيْرَهُ بَيْنَ الْقُعُودِ وَالْقِيَامِ، وَهَذَا يُنَا فِي فَرْضِيَّةَ أَمْرِ آخَرَ وَوُجُوبَهُ، إِلَّا أَنَّا أَثْبَتْنَا الْوُجُوبَ بِمَا رَوَاهُ احْتِيَاطًا دُونَ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ، لِأَنَّهُ خَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ، وَبِمِثْلِهِ لَا تَثْبُتُ الْفَرْضِيَّةُ.
العناية: كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۳۲۲، ط: دار الفكر
Giving a choice contradicts obligation and necessity. Al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Section on Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 116. Translation: Giving a choice in something contradicts its being obligatory and necessary. Explanation: Through this mentioned principle, the author of Hidayah is proving the position of the Hanafis: according to the Hanafis, when the one praying says salam, uttering the words 'al-salamu alaykum' is wajib, not fard. According to Imam Shafi'i, saying the salam is a rukn and fard, not wajib. The proof for wujub is that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) taught Ibn Mas'ud the tashahhud, he said: 'When you have said this or done this, your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand; if you wish to sit, sit.' In this, the Prophet made the completion of prayer conditional before salam and gave him a choice between sitting and standing. The principle is that giving a choice contradicts something being fard or wajib. Therefore, after the extent of tashahhud, the salam and other things are not fard. We have established wujub precautionarily due to the hadith that Imam Shafi'i cited as proof, namely 'tahrimatuha al-takbir'. This hadith is khabar wahid, and khabar wahid establishes wujub but not fardiyyah, because to establish fardiyyah, a text with definitive indication is needed. Our proof is what we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet when teaching him the tashahhud said to him: 'If you say this or do this, your prayer is complete; if you wish to stand, stand; if you wish to sit, sit.' The argument from it is that the Prophet judged the completion of prayer before the salam and gave him a choice between sitting and standing, and this contradicts the obligation of another matter; except we established wujub due to what he narrated precautionarily, not fardiyyah, because he is a single narrator, and by such fardiyyah is not established. Al-Inayah: Book of Prayer, Description of Prayer, vol. 1 p. 322.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage explains the second principle: 'إن التخيير ينافي الفرضية والوجوب' (Giving a choice contradicts obligatory and necessary status). The author uses this principle to prove that the salam (greeting) in prayer is wajib (necessary) and not fard (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, contrary to Imam Shafi'i who considers it a rukn and fard. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet gave him a choice after reciting tashahhud to either stand or sit, indicating that the prayer is complete before salam. This shows that salam is not fard. However, the Hanafis still consider it wajib due to the hadith 'tahrimatuha al-takbir' reported by Shafi'i, but since it is a khabar wahid (single-narrator hadith), it only establishes wujub, not fardiyyah, which requires definitive proof. The Hanafi position is that the salam is wajib, not fard, and the prayer is valid without it but requires sajdah sahw if omitted intentionally? Actually the text doesn't go that far. But the key point is the distinction in authority between fard and wajib.

Key Terms
تخيير (takhayyur): Giving a choice; here it means the Prophet gave Ibn Mas'ud a choice after tashahhud.
فرضية (fardiyyah): The quality of being fard (obligatory with qat'i proof).
وجوب (wujub): The quality of being wajib (necessary but with zanni proof).
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur; it establishes zanni knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the salam in prayer considered wajib rather than fard?
A) Because the Prophet explicitly said it is wajib
B) Because the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud gives a choice, contradicting fardiyyah, and the opposing hadith is khabar wahid which only establishes wujub
C) Because it is a pillar of prayer like bowing
D) Because the Shafi'i school says it is fard

Key Takeaway
The salam in prayer is wajib, not fard, because the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud gives a choice after tashahhud, and the opposing evidence is khabar wahid which only establishes wujub.

Salah — Prayer

Salam in Prayer: Wajib, Not Fard – The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Proving Hanafi view that Salam is wajib using Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that salam is wajib not fard, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi usul principle regarding khabar wahid.

Core Idea
Salam is wajib because its proof (khabar wahid) establishes obligation but not the certainty of fard.

In Hanafi fiqh, a key distinction exists between fard (definitive obligation) and wajib (probable obligation). This distinction matters practically: omitting a fard invalidates the act, while omitting a wajib requires compensation but does not nullify it. One of the most cited examples is the salam at the end of prayer. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that salam is wajib, not fard, and examines the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud alongside the Shafi'i reliance on 'tahrimuha al-takbir'.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafis rule regarding salam: wajib, not fard. Clarify the practical consequence: omission requires sajdah sahw, not repetition of the prayer.
This distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i who consider it a rukn.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds salam to be fard (rukn) based on his interpretation of the hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir wa tahliluha al-taslim'.
Note that Shafi'i does not distinguish fard and wajib terminologically.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Present the Shafi'i proof: the hadith indicates that salam makes the prayer permissible to exit, implying it is an integral part.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain the Hanafi rebuttal using the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet gave choice after tashahhud, negating any obligatory act after it. Also, the Shafi'i hadith is khabar wahid, which can only establish wujub, not fard.
The Hanafis still accept the hadith as evidence for wujub out of precaution.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Compare the practical difference: if salam is forgotten, Hanafi says prayer valid with sajdah sahw; Shafi'i says prayer invalid.
This highlights the real-world impact of the usul distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ کسی چیز کا اختیار دینا یہ فرضیت اور وجوب کے منافی ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اصول مذکورہ سے حضرات احناف کے مسلک کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ احناف کے نزدیک مصلی جب سلام پھیرتا ہے تو اُسے لفظ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمُ ادا کرنا واجب ہے فرض نہیں ، امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک لفظ سلام کہنا رکن اور فرض ہے نہ کہ واجب، وجوب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے جب حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی تو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا " إِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا أَوْ فَعَلْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُكَ فَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقُومَ فَقُمْ وَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقْعُدَ فَاقْعُدُ " اس میں آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے سلام سے نماز پوری ہونے کا حکم لگایا ہے اور اس کو بیٹھنے اور کھڑے ہونے کے درمیان اختیار دیا ہے اور اصول ہے کہ اختیار دینا کسی چیز کے فرض اور واجب ہونے کے منافی ہے، لہذ امقدار تشہد کے بعد سلام وغیرہ کوئی چیز فرض نہیں ہے۔ ہم نے وجوب کو احتیاطاً اس حدیث کی وجہ سے ثابت کیا ہے جس کو امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ نے بطور دلیل ذکر کیا ہے، یعنی تَحْرِيمُهَا التَّكْبِيرُ ، تو یہ حدیث خبر واحد ہے اور خبر واحد سے وجوب تو ثابت ہو جاتا ہے مگر فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ، اس لئے کہ ثبوتِ فرضیت کے لئے قطعی الدلالت نص کی ضرورت ہوتی ہے۔ وَلَنَا مَا رَوَيْنَا مِنْ حَدِيثِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: لَمَّا عَلَّمَهُ التَّشَهُّدَ قَالَ لَهُ: إِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا أَوْ فَعَلْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُكَ، فَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَن تَقُومَ فَقُمْ وَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقْعُدَ فَاقْعُدُ. وَجْهُ التَّمَسُّكِ بِهِ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ حَكَمَ بِتَمَامِ الصَّلَاةِ قَبْلَ السَّلَامِ وَخَيَّرَهُ بَيْنَ الْقُعُودِ وَالْقِيَامِ، وَهَذَا يُنَافِي فَرْضِيَّةَ أَمْرٍ آخَرَ وَوُجُوبَهُ، إِلَّا أَنَّا أَثْبَتْنَا الْوُجُوبَ بِمَا رَوَاهُ احْتِيَاطًا دُونَ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ، لِأَنَّهُ خَبَرُ وَاحِدٍ، وَبِمِثْلِهِ لَا تَثْبُتُ الْفَرْضِيَّةُ.
Translation: Giving choice regarding something contradicts its being fard or wajib. Explanation: The author of Hidayah is using the mentioned principle to prove the position of the Hanafis: According to the Hanafis, when the worshiper says salam, saying the words 'al-salamu alaykum' is wajib, not fard. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that saying salam is a rukn and fard, not wajib. The evidence for wujub is that when the Prophet taught Abdullah ibn Mas'ud the tashahhud, he said: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' In this, the Prophet linked completion of prayer to salam and gave him choice between sitting and standing. The principle is that giving choice is contrary to an action being fard or wajib. Therefore, after the tashahhud, nothing including salam is fard. We have established wujub as a precaution based on the hadith cited by al-Shafi'i, i.e., 'Its prohibition is the takbir.' That hadith is khabar wahid, and wujub can be established by khabar wahid, but fardiyyah cannot, because establishing fardiyyah requires a text that is qat'i al-dalalah. Our proof is what we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: When the Prophet taught him the tashahhud, he said to him: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' The point of reliance is that the Prophet ruled the prayer complete before salam and gave him the choice between sitting and standing, and this contradicts the fardiyyah or wujub of another action. However, we have established wujub from what he narrated as a precaution, not fardiyyah, because it is khabar wahid, and with such a report fardiyyah is not established.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a classic inter-madhhab dispute presented in the Hidayah. The author states the Hanafi position: saying salam is wajib, not fard. The Shafi'i position is that it is fard/rukn. The author then provides the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet said that when you say the tashahhud (and by extension complete the prayer with salam), the prayer is complete, and gave the choice to stand or sit after that. Choice negates obligation (both fard and wajib). Therefore, salam cannot be fard or wajib. However, the Hanafis still say it is wajib, not fard, out of precaution based on the hadith used by Shafi'i (tahrimuha al-takbir) which is a khabar wahid. Since khabar wahid can establish wujub but not fardiyyah (which requires qat'i dalalah), the Hanafis conclude wajib. The passage illustrates the usul principle that khabar wahid suffices for wujub but not fard.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): A divinely commanded obligation established by definitive evidence (qat'i al-thubut wa al-dalalah); its omission invalidates the act.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory action established by a zanni evidence (khabar wahid or qiyas); its omission requires compensation (like sajdah sahw) but does not invalidate the act.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few chains that does not reach the level of tawatur; it yields probable knowledge (zann).
قطعی الدلالت (qat'i al-dalalah): A text with unequivocal meaning, leaving no room for interpretation; required for establishing fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is salam considered wajib rather than fard?
A) Because the Prophet explicitly said salam is wajib.
B) Because the evidence for its obligation is khabar wahid, which can establish wujub but not fardiyyah.
C) Because salam is mentioned in the Quran as fard.
D) Because the Hanafis follow a different hadith that declares it obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Salam is wajib in Hanafi fiqh because its proof is zanni, highlighting the school's nuanced approach to obligation levels based on certainty of evidence.
