Principle of Tabaiyyah: Voluntary Prayer Follows Obligatory in Recitation Rulings
Establishing a legal maxim and its application to nafl prayer rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'that which completes something is subordinate to it' to derive the rulings of jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfa' (silent recitation) for voluntary (nafl) prayers.

Core Idea
The completing act follows the completed act: daytime nafl requires silent recitation just like daytime farz.

This passage from Al-Hidayah introduces a key legal maxim that governs the relationship between voluntary and obligatory prayers in matters of recitation. By understanding this principle of tabaiyyah (subordination), you will see how the Hanafi school derives consistent rules for nafl prayers without needing separate textual evidence for every detail. The passage also clarifies the limits of this followership, especially regarding validity and invalidity.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and identify its components
First, identify the Arabic maxim: 'إن ما كان مكملا لشيء فهو تابع له' (That which completes something is subordinate to it). Recognize that 'mukammil' (completer) and 'tabi' (follower) are the key terms.
The maxim is not a Quranic verse but a legal principle derived by the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the asl (original case) and far' (new case) in the qiyas
The asl is the munfarid (individual) in obligatory prayer (farz). The far' is the munfarid in voluntary prayer (nafl). The original ruling: daytime farz requires ikhfa', night farz gives choice. This ruling is transferred to nafl.
The analogy is based on the fact that nafl completes farz, just as a soldier's residence follows his commander's.
3
Determine the illa (effective cause) and its applicability
The illa is that nafl completes farz (mukammil li al-fard). Since the completing act is subordinate, the rulings suitable for followership (like jahr and ikhfa') transfer. The passage emphasizes 'فيما يصلح تبعا له' (in matters suitable for followership).
Suitability excludes matters like validity/invalidity, as clarified by the exception of independent takbirs.
4
Apply the ruling to daytime and night nafl
Daytime farz for munfarid requires ikhfa', so daytime nafl requires ikhfa' (wajib). Night farz for munfarid allows choice between jahr and ikhfa', so night nafl also allows choice. This is the mufta bihi position.
This applies only when praying alone; the imam's jahr in congregation has its own rules.
5
Note the limitation: followership does not extend to validity
If a person prays sunnah before zuhr and then invalidates the zuhr, the sunnah remains valid because each has its own opening takbir (tahrimah mubtada'ah). The exception is the muqtadi (follower) whose prayer depends on the imam.
This prevents an unintended extension of the maxim in invalidativeness.

فصل في القراءة (۷۸) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ مُكَمِّلا لِشَيْءٍ فَهُوَ تَابِع لَهُ. • ترجمہ: جو چیز کسی دوسری چیز کو مکمل کرنے والی ہو وہ اس کے تابع ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس اصول سے اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ دن کے نفل میں اخفاء واجب ہے اور رات کے نفل میں اختیار ہے جہر کرے یا اخفاء کرے، اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفل پڑھنے والے کو قیاس کیا گیا ہے تنہا فرض ادا کرنے والے پر، یعنی جیسے فرض میں منفرد شخص کو حکم ہے کہ دن کے فرائض میں وجو با اخفاء کرے گا اور رات کی نمازوں میں اس کو اختیار ہے چاہے جہر کرے یا اخفاء کرے، وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ نفل فرض کی تکمیل کرنے والا ہوتا ہے، اور اصول ہے کہ جو چیز کسی چیز کو مکمل کرنے والی ہو وہ اس کے تابع ہوتی ہے، لہذ انفل بھی فرض کے تابع ہوگا، اور رات کے فرضوں میں منفرد کو اختیار ہے کہ جہر کرے یا اختفاء ، اسی طرح رات کی نفلوں میں بھی اختیار ہے، چونکہ دن کے فرضوں میں اخفاء متعین ہے لہذا دن کی نفلوں میں بھی اخفاء متعین ہوگا۔ (۷۹) إِنَّ الْجَهْرَ يَخْتَصُّ إِمَّا بِالْجَمَاعَةِ حَتْمًا أَوْ بِالْوَقْتِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُنْفَرِدِ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّخْسِيرِ. ويكون تبعا له أى إذا كان التطوع مكملا للفرض، فيكون التطوع تبعا للفرض، والتبعية تستدعى أن يكون الحكم فى النابع كالحكم فى المتبوع فيما يصلح تبعا له، كالجندى يصير مقيما في المفازة لإقامة إمامه فى المصر، وإنما قيدنا بقولنا فيما يصلح تبعا له احترازا عن حكم الجواز والفساد، فإنه إذا صلى الأربع قبل الظهر ثم شرع في الظهر وأفسدها لا يرى ذلك إلى فساد السنة قبلها، وإن كانت شرعيتها لتكميل القرض أيضا لما كان لكل واحدة منهما تحريمة مبتدأة غير مبنية أحدهما على الأخرى. وقولنا غير مبنية احترازا عن صلاة المقتدى حيث تفسد بفساد صلاة الإمام وإن كانت لصلاة كل واحد منهما تحريمة مبتدأة.
Chapter on Recitation. (78) Indeed, that which completes something is a follower of it. Translation: Something that completes another thing is subordinate to it. Explanation: The author of Hidayah is proving by this principle that in daytime voluntary prayer, lowering the voice (ikhfa') is wajib, and in night voluntary prayer, there is choice: one may recite aloud or silently. Its evidence is that the one praying voluntarily is analogized to the one performing obligatory prayer alone: just as for the individual in obligatory prayer, the command is that in daytime obligatory prayers he must lower his voice, and in night prayers he has choice, whether to recite aloud or silently. The reason is that voluntary prayer completes obligatory prayer, and the principle is that something which completes something else is subordinate to it. Therefore, voluntary prayer will also be subordinate to obligatory prayer. In night obligatory prayers, the individual has choice between jahr and ikhfa', thus in night voluntary prayers also there is choice. Since in daytime obligatory prayers, ikhfa' is determined, so in daytime voluntary prayers, ikhfa' will also be determined. (79) Indeed, jahr (loud recitation) is specific either to congregation necessarily, or to time in the case of the individual by way of restriction. And it (the voluntary) is a follower of it, i.e., when the voluntary is complementary to the obligatory, the voluntary becomes a follower of the obligatory. This followership requires that the ruling for the follower be like the ruling for the followed in matters that are suitable for followership, like a soldier becomes a resident in the desert due to his imam's residence in the city. We restricted by our saying 'in matters that are suitable for followership' to exclude the ruling of validity and invalidity: if one prays four rak'ahs before zuhr, then begins zuhr and invalidates it, that does not lead to the invalidity of the earlier sunnah, even though its legislation was to complete the obligatory prayer, because each of them has an independent opening takbir, not built upon the other. Our saying 'not built upon one another' excludes the prayer of a follower (muqtadi), which is invalidated by the invalidity of the imam's prayer, even though each has its own opening takbir.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage from the 'Chapter on Recitation' in Al-Hidayah introduces a key legal maxim: 'What completes something is subordinate to it.' The author applies this to voluntary (nafl) prayers: since nafl prayers complete obligatory (farz) prayers, the rulings of jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfa' (silent recitation) in nafl follow those in farz. For a munfarid (individual praying alone), daytime farz requires ikhfa', so daytime nafl also requires ikhfa'. Night farz allows choice, so night nafl allows choice. The commentary from Al-Binayah clarifies the scope: followership applies in matters suitable for it, like rulings on recitation, but not in matters of validity/invalidity. For example, if one prays the sunnah before zuhr and then invalidates the farz, the sunnah remains valid because each has its own takbirat al-ihram; they are not linked in that way. The exception is the muqtadi (follower in congregation) whose prayer is dependent on the imam. This passage demonstrates how a general principle (qawida) is derived and applied to specific cases (furu').

Key Terms
مكمِّل (mukammil): That which completes or perfects another thing; here, nafl prayer completes farz prayer by making up for deficiencies.
تابع (tabi'): Subordinate/follower; something that follows the ruling of another in matters suitable for followership.
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer; specifically for night prayers and for imam in congregation.
اخفاء (ikhfa'): Silent recitation; required for daytime prayers (both farz and nafl for munfarid).
تحريمة مبتدأة (tahrimah mubtada'ah): An independent opening takbir; each prayer has its own, so one prayer's invalidity does not affect another (except muqtadi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in this passage, what is the ruling on recitation in daytime voluntary prayer for a person praying alone?
A) Jahr (loud recitation) is wajib.
B) Ikhfa' (silent recitation) is wajib.
C) He has a choice between jahr and ikhfa'.
D) Recitation is not required in nafl.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that a completing act is subordinate to the completed act allows the school to derive recitation rulings for voluntary prayers from obligatory ones, with the important limitation that followership does not extend to validity due to independent opening takbirs.

The Principle of Subordination: Nafl Follows Fard in Recitation Rules
Establishes subordination principle for nafl prayer recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of subordination (tābi'iyyah) to determine the recitation ruling for nafl prayers and distinguish between rulings suitable for subordination (e.g., recitation) and those not (e.g., validity).

Core Idea
What completes another is subordinate to it: daytime nafl must be quiet, nighttime nafl allows choice.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi legal maxim: whatever completes something else is subordinate to it in ruling. The author of al-Hidayah uses this to settle the recitation rules for supererogatory (nafl) prayers. By understanding the scope and boundaries of subordination, you will be able to correctly apply the day/night distinction to nafl and avoid common errors regarding validity.

Guided Path
1
State the legal maxim
Identify the maxim: 'Whatever completes something else is subordinate to it.' This is the foundation of the ruling.
The maxim is not absolute; it applies only in matters suitable for subordination.
2
Identify the asl (original case) and far' (new case) in the qiyas
The asl is fard prayer offered alone; its recitation ruling is known: daytime ikhfā' wajib, nighttime choice. The far' is nafl prayer. The analogy transfers the ruling because nafl completes fard.
The asl's ruling is based on Sunnah and practice.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause) – subordination
The illa is that nafl is a completion (takaamil) for fard. This is a shabahah-type illa based on the maxim.
The 'illa is extracted by tahrīr al-manāt: since nafl is meant to complete fard, it is subordinate.
4
Apply the restriction: matters suitable for subordination
The commentary from al-Binayah clarifies that subordination applies to rulings like recitation but not to validity/invalidity. Each prayer has its own takbīr and can stand independently.
Exception: the follower's prayer is built on the imam's prayer, so it invalidates if the imam's does.
5
Derive the ruling for nafl recitation
Since daytime fard requires ikhfā', daytime nafl requires ikhfā' (wajib). Nighttime fard allows choice, so nighttime nafl also allows choice.
This is the muftā bihi position in the Hanafi school.

دن کے فرضوں میں اخفاء متعین ہے لہذا دن کی نفلوں میں بھی اخفاء متعین ہوگا۔
الهداية : كتاب الصلاة، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۱۸، ط: رحمانیه
فيكون تبعا له أى إذا كان التطوع مكملا للفرض، فيكون التطوع تبعا للفرض، والتبعية تستدعى أن يكون الحكم فى النابع كالحكم فى المتبوع فيما يصلح تبعا له، كالجندى يصير مقيما في المفازة لإقامة إمامه فى المصر، وإنما قيدنا بقولنا فيما يصلح تبعا له احترازا عن حكم الجواز والفساد، فإنه إذا صلى الأربع قبل الظهر ثم شرع في الظهر وأفسدها لا يرى ذلك إلى فساد السنة قبلها، وإن كانت شرعيتها لتكميل القرض أيضا لما كان لكل واحدة منهما تحريمة مبتدأة غير مبنية أحدهما على الأخرى. وقولنا غير مبنية احترازا عن صلاة المقتدى حيث تفسد بفساد صلاة الإمام وإن كانت لصلاة كل واحد منهما تحريمة مبتدأة.

Section on Recitation
(78) Indeed, whatever is a completion for something is subordinate to it.
Translation: Whatever completes another thing is subordinate to it.
Explanation: The author of Al-Hidayah uses this principle to prove that in daytime nafl prayers, lowering the voice is obligatory, and in nighttime nafl, there is choice to recite aloud or quietly. Its proof is that the one praying nafl is analogized to the one praying fard alone. Just as in fard, an individual is commanded: in daytime fard prayers he must lower his voice, and in nighttime prayers he has a choice whether to recite aloud or quietly. The reason is that nafl is a completion for fard, and the principle is that whatever completes something is subordinate to it. Thus nafl is subordinate to fard. Since in nighttime fard the individual has a choice to recite aloud or quietly, similarly in nighttime nafl there is a choice. Because in daytime fard lowering the voice is determined, so in daytime nafl lowering the voice is determined.
Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 1, p. 118, Rahmaniyyah ed.
So it becomes subordinate to it: i.e., when the supererogatory act completes the obligatory act, then the supererogatory is subordinate to the obligatory. Subordination requires that the ruling for the subordinate be like the ruling for the principal in matters suitable for subordination. For example, a soldier becomes a resident in the desert due to the residence of his commander in the city. We restricted our statement 'in matters suitable for subordination' to exclude the ruling of validity and invalidity. For if one prays four rak'ahs before Zuhr, then begins Zuhr and invalidates it, this does not lead to the invalidity of the preceding sunnah, even though its legislation is for completing the fard as well, because each has its own separate initiating Takbir not built upon the other. And our statement 'not built upon' excludes the prayer of the follower, as it becomes invalid due to the invalidity of the Imam's prayer, even though each has its own initiating Takbir.
[Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 2, p. 292, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyyah ed.]
Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 1, p. 118, Rahmaniyyah ed.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim (qā'idah) concerning subordination: that which completes another is subordinate to it in ruling. The commentator applies this to the recitation rules for nafl (supererogatory) prayers. In the Hanafi school, a person praying fard alone must recite quietly during daytime prayers (Zuhr, 'Asr) and has a choice between loud and quiet during nighttime prayers (Maghrib, 'Isha, Fajr). Since nafl prayers are considered completions of the fard prayers, they are subordinate to the fard in rulings that are suitable for subordination. Thus, daytime nafl must be recited quietly, while nighttime nafl allows choice. The Arabic commentary from Al-Binayah refines the scope of subordination: it applies to matters like recitation but not to validity/invalidity. For example, if one prays a sunnah then fard and the fard becomes invalid, the sunnah remains valid because each has its own independent opening takbir. However, the follower's prayer is an exception: if the imam's prayer becomes invalid, the follower's also becomes invalid, as it is built upon the imam's prayer. This shows the precise boundaries of the subordination principle.

Key Terms
تابع (tābi'): Subordinate, following another in legal ruling
اختفاء (ikhfā'): Lowering the voice in recitation, as opposed to jahr (loud)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle of subordination in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for recitation in a daytime nafl prayer?
A) Loud recitation is obligatory
B) Quiet recitation is obligatory
C) There is a choice between loud and quiet
D) Recitation is not required

Key Takeaway
Nafl recitation rules mirror fard's day/night distinction because nafl completes fard and is subordinate in suitable matters, but validity is not a matter of subordination.

When to Recite Loudly in Qada' of 'Isha: The Principle of Jahr
Explains when loud recitation is obligatory vs optional for qada' of a missed prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for loud recitation (jahr) in qada' of 'Isha and apply the Hanafi ruling to determine whether an individual must recite loudly or quietly.

Core Idea
Loud recitation in qada' depends on congregation or time; without both, quiet is wajib.

This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses a key principle: loud recitation (jahr) in prayer is tied to two factors—congregation (where it is obligatory) and time (where it is optional for the individual). Understanding these conditions is crucial when making up a missed prayer (qada'). In this lesson, we will analyze the ruling for qada' of 'Isha after sunrise and see why the Hanafi school mandates quiet recitation for the individual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two scenarios
The act is qada' of 'Isha after sunrise. Consider two scenarios: praying with congregation or alone. Determine the ruling for each based on the principle.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
With congregation, jahr is wajib; alone, ikhfa' is wajib with no choice. This is from the passage: 'If he leads, he recites aloud; if alone, he recites quietly obligatorily.'
3
Extract the underlying principle
The principle: jahr is specifically either for congregation (obligatory) or for the time in the case of the individual (optional). This is from the Arabic: 'إِنَّ الْجَهْرَ يَخْتَصُّ إِمَّا بِالْجَمَاعَةِ حَتْمًا أَوْ بِالْوَقْتِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُنْفَرِدِ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّخْسِيرِ'.
4
Apply the principle to the qada' case
In qada' alone after time, neither congregation nor the original time exists. Therefore, jahr is not permissible; ikhfa' becomes wajib. The passage states: 'لَمْ يُوجَدُ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمَا' (neither of them exists).
This analysis shows the logical deduction, not personal opinion.
5
Note the authority
This is the sahih (correct) view in the Hanafi school, as stated in Al-Hidayah and supported by Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and Al-Binayah.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۹) إِنَّ الْجَهْرَ يَخْتَصُّ إِمَّا بِالْجَمَاعَةِ حَتْمًا أَوْ بِالْوَقْتِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُنْفَرِدِ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّخْسِيرِ.
ترجمہ: جہر یا تو جماعت کے ساتھ واجب ہے، یا منفرد کے حق میں بطور تخییر واجب ہے۔
تشریح : مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کی عشاء کی نماز فوت ہوگئی ، تو اس نے اس نماز کو آفتاب طلوع ہونے کے بعد قضا کیا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو با جماعت قضا کرے گایا تنہا، اگر جماعت کے ساتھ قضا کی ہے تو جہر کرے، لیکن اگر مذکورہ قضا نماز تنہا پڑھے تو اخفاء واجب ہے اور اس کو جہر اور اخفا کے درمیان اختیار نہیں ۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ جہر کرنا دوصورتوں میں مختص ہے، ایک یہ کہ نماز با جماعت ہو، دوم یہ کہ نماز وقت کے اندر ہو ، پہلی صورت میں جہر واجب ہے ، اور دوسری صورت میں منفرد کے حق میں بطور اختیار کے ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ جہر اور اخفا شرعی تو قیف پر موقوف ہے، اور شریعت میں جہر دو طریقوں سے پایا جاتا ہے، ایک تو جہر واجب ہے، یہ اس وقت ہے کہ جماعت سے جہری نماز پڑھی جائے خواہ ادا ہو یا قضا ہو، اور دوم جہر مخیر ، یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ منفر دوقت کے اندر جہری نماز پڑھے، اور چونکہ یہاں جب کہ منفر دطلوع آفتاب کے بعد جہری نمازی پڑھتا ہے تو دونوں باتوں میں سے کوئی بات نہیں پائی گئی یعنی نہ جماعت ہے اور نہ وقت،
اس لئے اس صورت میں نہ جہر واجب ہو گا اور نہ جہر مخیر ، بلکہ اخفا واجب ہوگا۔
وَمَنْ فَاتَتُهُ الْعِشَاءُ فَصَلَّاهَا بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ إِنْ أَمَّ فِيهَا جَهَرَ وَإِنْ صَلَّى وَحْدَهُ خَافَتَ حَتْمًا وَلَا يَتَخَيَّرُ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّ الْجَهْرَ يَخْتَصُّ إِمَّا بِالْجَمَاعَةِ حَتْمًا أَوْ بِالْوَقْتِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُنْفَرِدِ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّخْسِيرِ وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمَا.
الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة ، ج ۱ ص ۵۷، ط: المطبعة الخيرية (لأن الجهر يختص إما بالجماعة (حتما أى لأن الجهر بالقراءة مخصوص أما في الصلاة بالجماعة على سبيل الحتم أى الوجوب (أو) بالوقت أى وإما أن يختص بوقت الصلاة في حق المنفرد وعلى وجه التخيير بين الجهر والإخفاء ولم يوجد أحدهما) أى أحد المذكورين وهما أى الجماعة والوقت فى حق المنفرد وحاصله أن سبب الجهر إما الجماعة وذلك حتم، وإما الوقت وذلك فيه خيار للمنفرد بين الأمرين الجهر والمخافتة، والمنفرد القاضي لا يوجد فى حقه لا الجماعة ولا الوقت فلا يجهر.
[البناية: كتاب الصلاة، فصل فى القراءة ، ج ۲ ص ۲۹۷، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ]
(79) Indeed, loud recitation is specifically either for the congregation necessarily, or for the time in the case of the individual as a choice.
Translation: Loud recitation is either obligatory with congregation, or optional for the individual in the time.
Explanation: The issue is that if a person misses the 'Ishā' prayer and makes it up after sunrise, there are two scenarios: he prays it with congregation or alone. If he prays it with congregation, he recites aloud. But if he prays the mentioned qada' prayer alone, then quiet recitation is obligatory, and he has no choice between loud and quiet. The reason is that loud recitation is specific to two situations: first, the prayer is with congregation; second, the prayer is within its time. In the first case, loud recitation is obligatory; in the second, for the individual it is optional. The conclusion is that loud and quiet recitation are based on legal prescription. And in the Shari'ah, loud recitation is found in two ways: obligatory loud recitation, which is when a loud prayer is prayed with congregation, whether on time or qada'; and optional loud recitation, which is when an individual prays a loud prayer within its time. Since here the individual is praying a loud prayer after sunrise, neither of the two conditions exists—neither congregation nor time. Therefore, in this case, loud recitation is not obligatory nor optional; rather quiet recitation is obligatory.

And whoever misses 'Ishā' and prays it after sunrise: if he leads in it, he recites aloud; if he prays alone, he recites quietly obligatorily, and he does not have a choice. This is the correct view, because loud recitation is specific either to the congregation necessarily, or to the time in the case of the individual as a choice, and neither of them exists.
Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah: Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sifat al-Salah, vol. 1, p. 57, Al-Khayriyyah ed. (Because loud recitation is specific either to the congregation necessarily, i.e., because loud recitation is specifically in congregational prayer by way of necessity i.e. obligation, or to the time, i.e., it may be specific to the time of prayer for the individual by way of choice between loud and quiet, and neither of them exists) i.e., not one of the mentioned two exists, and they are congregation and time for the individual. Essentially, the cause for loud recitation is either congregation, which is obligatory, or time, which gives the individual a choice between loud and quiet. The individual making up the prayer does not have in his case either congregation or time, so he does not recite aloud.
[Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 2, p. 297, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyyah ed.]
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents a legal principle (qā'idah) regarding loud recitation (jahr) in prayer, specifically in the context of qada' (making up) a missed prayer. The principle states that loud recitation is either obligatory (when praying with congregation) or optional (for an individual praying within the prayer's proper time). The commentator applies this to the case of a person who misses 'Ishā' (a loud prayer) and makes it up after sunrise. If he leads a congregation in the qada', he must recite aloud (jahr becomes obligatory due to congregation). However, if he prays alone, he must recite quietly (ikhfā') because neither condition for jahr is met: there is no congregation and the prayer is outside its time. The passage emphasizes that the individual has no choice in this scenario; quiet recitation is obligatory (ḥatman). The Arabic sources (Al-Jawharah and Al-Binayah) clarify the reasoning: the cause for jahr is either congregation (which imposes obligation) or the time (which grants a choice). Since both are absent, the individual must recite quietly. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and is the ṣaḥīḥ (correct) position as stated in Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer
اخفاء (ikhfā'): Quiet recitation in prayer, opposite of jahr
تخسير (takhsīr): Choice between two options (loud and quiet)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person misses 'Isha and makes it up alone after sunrise, what is the Hanafi ruling for recitation?
A) He must recite aloud
B) He must recite quietly
C) He has a choice between loud and quiet
D) Recitation is not required

Key Takeaway
The mode of recitation in qada' is determined by the presence of congregation or the original time, not by the nature of the missed prayer itself.

Qada of Isha After Sunrise: Jahr vs Ikhfa
Explains ruling on reciting aloud or silently in qada of Isha after sunrise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in qada of Isha after sunrise and explain the legal reasoning linking jahr to the presence of either congregation or the prescribed time.

Core Idea
In qada of Isha after sunrise, jahr is for the imam only; the individual must recite silently.

When you miss the Isha prayer and make it up after sunrise, does the rule of reciting aloud still apply? The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction: if you lead a congregation, you must recite aloud; if you pray alone, you must recite silently. This lesson unpacks the logical proof behind that ruling, grounded in the causes (asbab) that trigger jahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two scenarios
The passage rules on qada of Isha after sunrise. It distinguishes two cases: the person leads a congregation (imam), or prays alone (munfarid). For each, state the ruling on recitation.
The ruling is categorical: jahr for imam, ikhfa for munfarid, with no choice for the latter.
2
List the two causes for jahr
The proof states that jahr is tied to either (1) praying in congregation (obligatory jahr) or (2) being within the prescribed time of a jahri prayer (optional jahr for the individual). Identify these two causes.
Time applies only to the prescribed time, not to qada. Congregation applies to any congregational prayer.
3
Check the presence of each cause in the qada scenario
Since the prayer is qada after sunrise, it is no longer within the Isha time. Also, the munfarid is not in congregation. Both causes are absent. Therefore, jahr is not justified.
The absence of both causes makes ikhfa necessary (wajib) – there is no basis for jahr.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The text explicitly says 'wa huwa al-sahih' (this is the correct view). This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school for fatwa.
No intra-madhhab difference is recorded in this passage; it is the settled view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ فَاتَتُهُ الْعِشَاءُ فَصَلَّاهَا بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ إِنْ أَمَّ فِيهَا جَهَرَ وَإِنْ صَلَّى وَحْدَهُ خَافَتَ حَتْمًا وَلَا يَتَخَيَّرُ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّ الْجَهْرَ يَخْتَصُّ إِمَّا بِالْجَمَاعَةِ حَتْمًا أَوْ بِالْوَقْتِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُنْفَرِدِ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّخْيِيرِ وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمَا. (الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج1 ص57، ط: المطبعة الخيرية). (لأن الجهر يختص إما بالجماعة (حتما أى لأن الجهر بالقراءة مخصوص أما في الصلاة بالجماعة على سبيل الحتم أى الوجوب (أو) بالوقت أى وإما أن يختص بوقت الصلاة في حق المنفرد وعلى وجه التخيير بين الجهر والإخفاء ولم يوجد أحدهما) أى أحد المذكورين وهما أى الجماعة والوقت فى حق المنفرد وحاصله أن سبب الجهر إما الجماعة وذلك حتم، وإما الوقت وذلك فيه خيار للمنفرد بين الأمرين الجهر والمخافتة، والمنفرد القاضي لا يوجد فى حقه لا الجماعة ولا الوقت فلا يجهر. (البناية: كتاب الصلاة، فصل فى القراءة، ج2 ص297، ط: دار الكتب العلمية).
Whoever misses Isha and prays it after sunrise: if he leads therein, he recites aloud; and if he prays alone, he recites silently necessarily and he does not have a choice. This is the correct view because Jahr is specific either to the congregation necessarily or to the time in the right of the individual on the basis of choice, and neither of them is found. (Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira...) (Because Jahr is specific either to the congregation necessarily, meaning because loud recitation is specifically for prayer with congregation by way of necessity i.e. obligation, or to the time, meaning it is specific to the time of prayer in the right of the individual and he has a choice between loud and silent recitation, and neither of the two is found) i.e. one of the mentioned two, which are congregation and time, in the right of the individual. The conclusion is that the cause of Jahr is either congregation, which is obligatory, or time, which gives the individual a choice between loud and silent recitation. The individual performing qada has neither congregation nor time, so he does not recite aloud. (Al-Binaya...)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the qada of Isha after sunrise. The base text from Al-Jawhara states that if a person misses Isha and prays it after sunrise, then if he leads a congregation, he must recite aloud (jahr), and if he prays alone, he must recite silently (ikhfa) necessarily, without choice. The proof is that loud recitation (jahr) is either obligatory due to congregation or optional due to being within the time for an individual. Since the qada is after the time and alone, neither condition exists, so jahr is not permissible; rather ikhfa is obligatory. The commentator from Al-Binaya explains that the cause of jahr is either congregation (obligatory jahr) or time (optional jahr). The individual performing qada has neither, so he must recite silently.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation in prayer, specifically in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr, and in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers.
الإخفاء (al-ikhfā'): Silent recitation, where the reciter only hears himself.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must recite aloud because Isha is a jahri prayer.
B) He may choose between loud and silent recitation.
C) He must recite silently necessarily.
D) He must recite silently only if he is not leading, but aloud if he leads.

Key Takeaway
For qada of Isha after sunrise, the individual praying alone must recite silently; loud recitation is only for an imam leading a congregation.

Missed Wajib in Prayer: Qada or Sajda al-Sahw?
States the usul principle and its application to a specific prayer omission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul principle 'al-wajib idha fata 'an waqtihi la yuqda illa bi dalil' and apply it to determine whether a missed wajib recitation in prayer should be made up or compensated by sajda al-sahw.

Core Idea
A missed wajib in its proper time is not made up later without a specific proof.

This lesson introduces a fundamental usul principle that governs the qada of wajibat in prayer. We will examine an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) regarding whether a forgotten recitation (Surah al-Fatiha or an additional surah) in the first two rak'ahs of Isha prayer should be repeated in the last two rak'ahs. Abu Yusuf argues that no qada is required because the principle dictates that a wajib missed from its time is not made up except with a specific dalil, which is absent here. The author of Al-Hidayah supports this view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usul principle
State the principle: الواجب إذا فات عن وقته لا يقضى إلا بدليل (A wajib missed from its time is not made up except with a proof). Understand that this limits qada to cases where a specific proof exists.
This is a rational (aqli) principle, not derived from text.
2
Understand the prayer scenario
Consider a person praying Isha who forgets to recite Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs but recites another surah, or vice versa. The question is whether he should recite the missing part in the last two rak'ahs.
Fatiha and an additional surah are both wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer.
3
Compare the two Hanafi positions
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say: make up the missed recitation in the last two rak'ahs, and also perform sajda al-sahw. Abu Yusuf says: do not make up any missed recitation; just perform sajda al-sahw.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, both within the school.
4
Apply the principle to Abu Yusuf's argument
Abu Yusuf argues: since the missed recitation is wajib and its time (the first two rak'ahs) has passed, it cannot be made up without a specific proof. No proof exists for qada of Fatiha in later rak'ahs, because recitation in the last two rak'ahs is not prescribed for that purpose.
The author of Al-Hidayah uses this principle to support Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْوَاجِبَ إِذَا فَاتَ عَنْ وَقْتِهِ لَا يُقْضَى إِلَّا بِدَلِيْلٍ . ترجمہ: واجب جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہو جائے تو بغیر دلیل کے اس کی قضا نہیں کی جاتی۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا سمجھنا موقوف ہے ایک مسئلہ پر، مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے عشاء کی پہلی دو رکعت میں سورت پڑھی مگر سورہ فاتحہ نہیں پڑھی، تو یہ شخص آخری دور کعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ کی قضا نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اگر پہلی دو رکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ کے بعد کچھ اور نہیں پڑھا تو آخری دو رکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت دونوں پڑھے گا، اور دونوں کے ساتھ جہر کرے، یہ حضرات طرفین کے نزدیک ہے، اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت دونوں میں سے کسی کی قضاء نہ کرے، بلکہ علی حالہ نماز پڑھے گا اور اخیر میں سجدہ سہو کرے گا۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک واجب ہے، اور اصول ہے کہ واجب جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہو جائے تو اس کی قضاء نہیں کی جاتی الا یہ کہ کوئی دلیل قضاء پائی جائے، اور یہاں پر دلیل قضاء موجود نہیں، اس لئے ان دونوں کی قضاء بھی نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ سے امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے مسلک کو ثابت کیا ہے۔ (الهداية كتاب الصلاة، فصل فى القراءة، ج1 ص118، ط: رحمانية) (وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ: لَا يَقْضِى وَاحِدَةً مِنْهُمَا لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا وَاجِبٌ، وَلِهَذَا لَوْ تَرَكَ إحْدَاهُمَا سَاهِيًا وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ سَجْدَةُ السَّهُو وَقَضَاهَا فِى الشَّفْع الثَّانِي أَوْ لَمُ يَقْضِ، وَالْوَاجِبُ إِذَا فَاتَ عَنْ وَقْتِهِ لَا يُقْضَى إِلَّا بِدَلِيلِ، وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِمَوْجُودٍ لَّانَّ الدَّلِيلَ هُوَ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَا لَهُ مَشْرُوعًا لِيُصْرَفَ إِلَى مَا عَلَيْهِ، وَالسُّورَةُ فِي الْأُخْرَيَيْنِ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعَةٍ. (العناية: كتاب الصلاة، فصل فى القراءة، ج1 ص329، ط: دار الفكر) وقال أبو يوسف لا تقضى السورة أصلا لأن الواجب إذا فات عن محله لا يقضى إلا بدليل وهو مفقود هنا قوله: وهو الأشبه، لأن السورة شرعت مرتبة على الفاتحة دون العكس. (حاشية الطحطاوي على مراقي الفلاح كتاب الصلاة، فصل في بيان واجب الصلاة، ص255، ط: دار الكتب العلمية)
Indeed, the obligatory when it is missed from its time is not made up except with a proof. Urdu: The obligatory when it is missed from its time, its qada is not made without a proof. Explanation: Understanding the mentioned principle depends on an issue: The issue is that a person recited a Surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha but did not recite Surah al-Fatiha, then this person will not make up Surah al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs. And if in the first two rak'ahs after Surah al-Fatiha he did not recite anything else, then in the last two rak'ahs he will recite both Surah al-Fatiha and a Surah, and he will recite aloud with both. This is according to the respected scholars (i.e., the majority). And Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) says that he should not make up any of them (Surah al-Fatiha and the additional Surah), but rather he should pray the prayer as it is and perform sajda al-sahw at the end. The reason is that both Surah al-Fatiha and the additional Surah are wajib, and the principle is that the wajib when missed from its time is not made up except with a proof, and here a proof for qada does not exist. Therefore, the qada of both will not be made. The author of Al-Hidayah established the view of Imam Abu Yusuf using the mentioned principle. (Al-Hidayah...) (Abu Yusuf said: He does not make up any one of them because each one of them is wajib, and for this reason if he left one of them forgetfully, sajda al-sahw becomes obligatory upon him, and whether he makes it up in the second shaf' or not, the wajib when missed from its time is not made up except with a proof, and it (the proof) is not present, because the proof is that what is prescribed for it should be turned to what is upon it, and reciting a Surah in the last two rak'ahs is not prescribed.) (Al-Inayah...) And Abu Yusuf said: He does not make up the Surah at all, because the wajib when missed from its place is not made up except with a proof, and it is absent here. He said: And it is more appropriate, because the Surah is prescribed as dependent on the Fatiha, not the opposite. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi...)
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute centered on a usul principle. The principle: 'A wajib missed from its time is not made up except with a dalil.' The issue: In Isha prayer, if a person forgetfully omits Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs but recites a Surah, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say he should make up the Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs, and if he omitted the Surah after Fatiha, he makes up both. But Abu Yusuf argues that both recitations are wajib; since the time for the first two rak'ahs has passed, they cannot be made up without a specific proof, which is absent. He thus says no qada, only sajda al-sahw. The author of Al-Hidayah supports Abu Yusuf's view using this principle. The later commentary from Al-Inayah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi reinforce that the Surah is prescribed to follow Fatiha in the same rak'ah, so it cannot be transferred to later rak'ahs.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wājib): An obligatory act proven by zanni (speculative) evidence, distinct from fard.
القضاء (al-qaḍā'): Performing a missed obligatory act after its prescribed time.
سجدة السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or addition in prayer, without invalidating it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle discussed, why does Abu Yusuf argue that a missed wajib recitation in the first two rak'ahs should not be made up in the last two?
A) Because the prayer would become invalid.
B) Because making up is only allowed if there is a specific proof, and here there is none.
C) Because the recitation in the last two rak'ahs is not wajib.
D) Because sajda al-sahw replaces the need for qada.

Key Takeaway
A missed wajib in prayer is not made up later without a specific proof; its omission is compensated by sajda al-sahw.

Qada of Missed Wajib Requires a Dalil: Principle and Application
States a usul principle and applies it to a specific case in prayer, including an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a missed wajib is not made up without evidence, and apply it to the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding recitation in prayer.

Core Idea
A missed wajib is not repeated without explicit proof — the principle disciplines compensation and resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute.

In Hanafi fiqh, the category of 'wajib' sits between fard and sunnah. When a wajib act is missed in prayer, it is generally not made up (qada) unless there is a specific dalil. This lesson presents that principle and its application to a classic case: recitation of Surah al-Fatiha and an additional surah in the first two rak'ahs, and whether to make them up in the last two. The case reveals an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Yusuf and the majority.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Recite the Arabic: 'إن الواجب إذا فات عن وقته لا يقضى إلا بدليل'. Understand that this is a legal maxim (qa'ida) that limits qada of wajib to cases with evidence.
2
Define Wajib and Qada
In Hanafi, wajib is less than fard; its omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the act. Qada means performing the missed act later.
The principle applies to missed wajib, not fard.
3
Apply to the Prayer Case
Consider the case: a person prays Isha and forgets to recite Surah al-Fatiha or the surah in the first two rak'ahs. Abu Yusuf says: do not make up either, only do sajdah al-sahw, because no dalil for qada exists. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) say: if the surah was missed, make up both Fatiha and surah with jahr in the last two; if Fatiha was missed, no qada.
The differing views stem from whether the last two rak'ahs can be a place for qada.
4
Analyze the Dalil
Abu Yusuf's dalil: the principle itself, and the fact that reciting a surah in the last two is not prescribed (ghayr mashru'a) originally. The majority rely on the need to complete recitation and some prophetic practice.
The author of al-Hidayah supports Abu Yusuf.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Yusuf's view, no qada; under the majority, qada of surah (and Fatiha if surah was missed) in the last two rak'ahs with jahr.

(۸۰) إِنَّ الْوَاجِبَ إِذَا فَاتَ عَنْ وَقْتِهِ لَا يُقْضَى إِلَّا بِدَلِيْلٍ . ترجمہ: واجب جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہو جائے تو بغیر دلیل کے اس کی قضا نہیں کی جاتی۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا سمجھنا موقوف ہے ایک مسئلہ پر ، مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے عشاء کی پہلی دو رکعت میں سورت پڑھی مگر سورہ فاتحہ نہیں پڑھی ، تو یہ شخص آخری دور کعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ کی قضا نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اگر پہلی دو رکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ کے بعد کچھ اور نہیں پڑھا تو آخری دو رکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت دونوں پڑھے گا ، اور دونوں کے ساتھ جہر کرے، یہ حضرات طرفین کے نزدیک ہے، اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت دونوں میں سے کسی کی قضاء نہ کرے، بلکہ علی حالہ نماز پڑھے گا اور اخیر میں سجدہ سہو کرے گا۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک واجب ہے، اور اصول ہے کہ واجب جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہو جائے تو اس کی قضاء نہیں کی جاتی الا یہ کہ کوئی دلیل قضاء پائی جائے ، اور یہاں پر دلیل قضاء موجود نہیں ، اس لئے ان دونوں کی قضاء بھی نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ سے امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے مسلک کو ثابت کیا ہے۔ الهداية كتاب الصلاة، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۱۸، ط: رحمانیه (وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ : لَا يَقْضِى وَاحِدَةً مِنْهُمَا لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا وَاجِبٌ، وَلِهَذَا لَوْ تَرَكَ إحْدَاهُمَا سَاهِيًا وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ سَجْدَةُ السَّهُو وَقَضَاهَا فِى الشَّفْع الثَّانِي أَوْ لَمُ يَقْضِ، وَالْوَاجِبُ إِذَا فَاتَ عَنْ وَقْتِهِ لَا يُقْضَى إِلَّا بِدَلِيلِ، وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِمَوْجُودٍ لَّانَّ الدَّلِيلَ هُوَ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَا لَهُ مَشْرُوعًا لِيُصْرَفَ إِلَى مَا عَلَيْهِ، وَالسُّورَةُ فِي الْأُخْرَيَيْنِ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعَةٍ. العناية: كتاب الصلاة، فصل فى القراءة ، ج ا ص ۳۲۹، ط: دار الفکر ] وقال أبو يوسف لا تقضى السورة أصلا لأن الواجب إذا فات عن محله لا يقضى إلا بدليل وهو مفقود هنا قوله : وهو الأشبه، لأن السورة شرعت مرتبة على الفاتحة دون العكس. حاشية الطحطاوي على مراقي الفلاح كتاب الصلاة، فصل في بيان واجب الصلاة، ص ۲۵۵، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
80. Indeed, when the obligatory (act) misses its time, it is not made up except with a proof. Translation: When a wajib is missed from its time, its qada is not performed without a proof. Explanation: Understanding the mentioned principle depends on a case. The case is that a person recited a surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha but did not recite Surah al-Fatiha. This person will not make up (qada) Surah al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs. If he did not recite anything after Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, then in the last two rak'ahs he will recite both Surah al-Fatiha and a surah, and recite both aloud (jahr). This is according to the two parties. Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) says: He should not make up either of them (Surah al-Fatiha or the surah), but instead pray as is and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end. The reason is that each of Surah al-Fatiha and the surah is wajib, and the principle is: 'When a wajib misses its time, it is not made up unless there is a proof for qada.' Here, there is no proof for qada, so neither is made up. The author of al-Hidayah has established the position of Imam Abu Yusuf from the mentioned principle. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 1, p. 118, Rahmaniyyah: 'And Abu Yusuf said: he should not make up either of them because each of them is wajib. For this, if one leaves one of them forgetfully, sajdah al-sahw becomes obligatory upon him, and he makes it up in the second pair or not, and the wajib when it misses its time is not made up except with a proof, and it does not exist because the proof would be that what is prescribed for it be diverted to what is due, and the surah in the last two is not prescribed.' Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 1, p. 329, Dar al-Fikr: 'And Abu Yusuf said: the surah is not made up at all because the wajib when it misses its place is not made up except with a proof, and it is absent here. His statement: and it is more similar, because the surah is prescribed in order after al-Fatiha, not the opposite.' Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 'ala Maraqi al-Falah, Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi Bayan Wajibat al-Salah, p. 255, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul (principle) of Hanafi fiqh: a missed wajib (obligatory act) is not made up (qada) unless there is specific evidence (dalil) indicating that it should be made up. The author states this principle and then shows its application in a specific issue from prayer. The issue: in the first two rak'ahs of a silent prayer (like Isha), recitation of Surah al-Fatiha and an additional surah is wajib. If a person forgets to recite Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, the majority view (attributed to 'the two parties' - likely Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) says that he should not make it up in the last two rak'ahs, because the place for qada of Fatiha is not established. However, if he recited Fatiha but missed the additional surah, then he should make up both Fatiha and the surah in the last two rak'ahs, reciting them aloud (since jahr is also a requirement for the first two rak'ahs). Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: he says that neither Fatiha nor the surah should be made up in the last two rak'ahs, because both are wajib, and according to the principle, a missed wajib is not made up without a dalil. Since there is no explicit evidence allowing qada of these recitations in the latter part of the prayer, the prayer is valid as is, and only sajdah al-sahw is required to compensate for the omission. The author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) uses this principle to support Abu Yusuf's view. The reference clarifies that the surah in the last two rak'ahs is not prescribed (mashru'a) in the same way as in the first two, so qada is not justified. Thus, the principle serves as a tool to determine whether compensation is required: if no dalil exists for qada, the act is not repeated.

Key Terms
الْوَاجِبُ (al-wajib): An obligatory act that is less than fard; its omission in prayer requires sajdah al-sahw.
قَضَى / يَقْضِي (qada / yaqdi): To make up a missed obligatory act after its time has passed.
دَلِيْلٌ (dalil): A legal proof or evidence from Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas that establishes a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person misses reciting Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha, what does Imam Abu Yusuf say should be done?
A) He should recite both Fatiha and a surah in the last two rak'ahs with jahr.
B) He should not make up either, but perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) He should repeat the entire prayer.
D) He should make up only the surah in the last two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle 'al-wajib idha fata 'an waqtihi la yuqda illa bi dalil' limits qada of wajib acts, and in the case of recitation, Abu Yusuf's no-qada view is the mufta bihi position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
The Two Definitions of Jahr and Mukhafatah in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines jahr and mukhafatah with two opinions and applies them to talaq, itq, etc.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of jahr and mukhafatah according to al-Hindwani and al-Karkhi, and apply each definition to determine the validity of utterances in talaq, itq, and istithna.

Core Idea
The validity of a spoken divorce depends on what 'hearing' means — and Hanafi scholars disagree on the threshold.

In Hanafi fiqh, the terms jahr (audible recitation) and mukhafatah (silent/subvocal recitation) are not just descriptive; they carry legal consequences. This lesson unpacks a classical dispute between two major Hanafi jurists — Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani and Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi — over the minimum requirements for these modes of speech. The difference is not academic: it determines whether a divorce, an emancipation, or an exception (istithna) is valid. By the end, you will see how a single definitional choice can change a family's legal status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of mukhafatah
Read the Arabic text and note that al-Hindwani defines mukhafatah as 'making oneself hear' (the sound reaches one's own ears), while al-Karkhi defines its minimum as 'correct pronunciation of letters' (tashih al-huruf) without necessarily hearing oneself.
Al-Karkhi's definition is a lower threshold.
2
Identify the corresponding definitions of jahr
For al-Hindwani, jahr means 'making others hear'. For al-Karkhi, the minimum of jahr is 'making oneself hear' (the same as al-Hindwani's mukhafatah).
Notice the reversal: what is mukhafatah for one is jahr for the other.
3
Apply the definitions to talaq and itq
Apply the definitions to a concrete scenario: a man says 'anti taliq' or 'anta hurr' but does not hear himself. Under al-Karkhi, the utterance is valid (pronunciation correct); under al-Hindwani, it is not (did not hear himself). The divorce or emancipation takes effect only under al-Karkhi.
4
Apply the same logic to istithna (exception)
Consider a divorce with an exception: 'You are divorced except if you enter the house.' If the speaker utters the exception so quietly that he does not hear it, al-Karkhi accepts the exception (so divorce does not occur immediately), while al-Hindwani does not (so divorce occurs immediately).
This shows the broad impact of the definitional choice.
5
Note the tarjih and the scope
The majority of later Mashayikh (including the author of al-Hidayah) adopt al-Hindwani's view as the relied-upon (mu'tamad) position. However, al-Bada'i' states that al-Karkhi's view is 'more analogous' (aqyas). The same dispute applies to tasmiyah over the slaughter animal and the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah.
Thus, the definitions govern all speech acts in fiqh.

(۸۱) إِنَّ الْمُخَافَتَةَ أَن يُسْمِعَ نَفْسَهُ وَالْجَهْرَ أَن يُسْمِعَ غَيْرَهُ عِنْدَ الْفَقِيهِ أَبِي جَعْفَرَ الْهِندُوَانِي وَعِندَ الْكَرْخِي أَدْنَى الْجَهْرِ أَن يُسْمِعَ نَفْسَهُ وَأَدْنَى الْمُخَافَتَةِ تَصْحِيحُ الْحُرُوفِ. ترجمہ: اختفاء یہ ہے کہ مصلی اپنے آپ کو سنائے اور جہر یہ ہے کہ دوسرے کو سنائے ، یہ تعریف فقیہ ابو جعفر الہندوانی کے نزدیک ہے، اور امام کرخی کے نزدیک جہر کی ادنی مقدار یہ ہے کہ قاری اپنے آپ کو سنائے ،اور مخافت کی ادنی مقدار حروف کی تصیح ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ پر فقہی مسئلہ کی تفریح کی ہے، مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی بیوی سے انتِ طَالِقٌ ، یا غلام سے انتَ حُر “ کہا اور کہنے والے نے بذاتِ خود نہیں سنا، تو امام کرخی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک طلاق اور عتاق واقع ہو جائیں گے، اور امام ابو جعفر ہندوانی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک واقع نہیں ہوں گے۔ اور اسی وَأَدْنَى الْمُخَافَتَةِ تَصْحِيحُ الْحُرُوفِ، وَفِي الْبَدَائِعِ : مَا قَالَهُ الْكَرْخِيُّ أَقْيَسُ وَأَصَحُ، وَفِي كِتَابِ الصَّلَاةِ لِمُحَمَّدٍ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَيْهِ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ: إِنْ شَاءَ قَرَأَ فِي نَفْسِهِ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ جَهَرَ وَأَسْمَعَ نَفْسَهُ . وَأَكْثَرُ الْمَشَايِخِ عَلَى أَنَّ الصَّحِيحَ أَنَّ الْجَهْرَ أَنْ يُسْمِعَ غَيْرَهُ وَالْمُخَافَتَةَ أَنْ يُسْمِعَ نَفْسَهُ ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الْهِنْدُوَانِيُّ ، وَكَذَا كُلُّ مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالنُّطْقِ كَالتَّسْمِيَةِ عَلَى النَّبِيحَةِ وَوُجُوبِ السَّجْدَةِ بِالتَّلَاوَةِ وَالْعَتَاقِ وَالطَّلَاقِ وَالاسْتِثْنَاءِ حَتَّى لَوْ طَلَّقَ وَلَمْ يُسْمِعُ نَفْسَهُ لَا يَقَعُ، وَإِنْ صَحْحَ الْحُرُوقَ، وَفِي الْخُلاصَةِ الْإِمَامُ إِذَا قَرَأَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْمُخَافَتَةِ بِحَيْتُ سَمِعَ رَجُلٌ أَوْ رَجُلَانِ لَا يَكُونُ جَهْرًا وَالْجَهْرُ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ الْكُلُّ. البحر الرائق: كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۳۵۶، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
81. Indeed, mukhafatah is that he makes himself hear, and jahr is that he makes others hear, according to Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani. And according to al-Karkhi, the minimum of jahr is that he makes himself hear, and the minimum of mukhafatah is the correct pronunciation of letters. Translation: Mukhafatah is that the worshiper makes himself hear, and jahr is that he makes another hear. This definition is according to Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani. According to Imam al-Karkhi, the minimum of jahr is that the reciter makes himself hear, and the minimum of mukhafatah is the correct pronunciation of letters. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah has derived a fiqhi issue from this principle. The issue: if a person says to his wife 'Anti taliq' or to his slave 'Anta hurr' and the speaker himself did not hear it, then according to Imam al-Karkhi, divorce and emancipation occur. According to Imam Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, they do not occur. Similarly, if he spoke aloud and made an exception (istithna) in such a way that he himself could not hear it, then according to Imam al-Karkhi, divorce and emancipation do not occur and the exception is valid. According to Imam Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, both occur immediately and the exception is not valid. The same difference applies to reciting tasmiyah over a slaughtered animal and the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 1, p. 119, Rahmaniyyah: 'The author did not specify the limit of jahr and israr (mukhafatah) due to difference of opinion along with the variation of what is correct. So al-Karkhi held that the minimum of jahr is that he makes himself hear, and the minimum of mukhafatah is correct pronunciation of letters. In al-Bada'i': what al-Karkhi said is more analogous and sound. In Kitab al-Salah of Muhammad, there is an indication towards it, for he said: If he wishes, he may recite to himself, and if he wishes, he may recite aloud and make himself hear. The majority of mashayikh hold that the correct view is that jahr is that he makes others hear, and mukhafatah is that he makes himself hear; this is the statement of al-Hindwani. And similarly, everything related to utterance, such as tasmiyah over the slaughtered animal, the obligation of sajdah by recitation, emancipation, divorce, and exception, to the extent that if he divorces and does not make himself hear, it does not occur, even if he correctly pronounces the letters. In al-Khulasah: The imam when he recites in the silent prayer such that one or two men hear him, it is not jahr; jahr is that everyone hears.' Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sifat al-Salah, vol. 1, p. 356, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage defines two key terms in Hanafi fiqh related to recitation and utterance: jahr (audible recitation) and mukhafatah (subvocal recitation). There is a dispute between two Hanafi scholars: Imam Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani defines mukhafatah as making oneself hear (i.e., the sound is audible to the reciter) and jahr as making others hear. Imam al-Karkhi defines the minimum of jahr as making oneself hear (so a lower threshold) and the minimum of mukhafatah as simply pronouncing the letters correctly without necessarily hearing oneself. The commentary explains that the author of al-Hidayah applies this difference to various fiqh issues. For example, in divorce (talaq) and emancipation (itq), if a person utters the words but does not hear himself, according to al-Karkhi, the utterance is considered valid (since he pronounced the letters correctly) and the divorce/emancipation takes effect. According to al-Hindwani, it does not take effect because the speaker did not hear himself, so it is not considered proper speech. Similarly, if a person makes an exception (istithna) in a divorce statement but does not hear himself, the same difference applies. The same disagreement applies to reciting tasmiyah (Bismillah) over an animal before slaughter and the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) — i.e., whether the recitation is considered audible enough for the rulings. The reference from al-Hidayah notes that the majority of mashayikh (later scholars) hold the view of al-Hindwani as the correct one (sahih), although al-Bada'i' states that al-Karkhi's view is more analogous (aqyas) and sound. The text also cites Kitab al-Salah of Imam Muhammad, where he says one may recite to himself or aloud and make himself hear, which supports al-Karkhi's view. The application is broad: everything related to speech acts follows this definition.

Key Terms
الْجَهْرُ (al-jahr): Audible recitation; according to al-Hindwani, making others hear; according to al-Karkhi, making oneself hear (minimum).
الْمُخَافَتَة (al-mukhafatah): Subvocal or quiet recitation; according to al-Hindwani, making oneself hear; according to al-Karkhi, correct pronunciation of letters.
تَصْحِيحُ الْحُرُوفِ (tashih al-huruf): Correct pronunciation of letters, even if not audible to the speaker; the minimum for mukhafatah according to al-Karkhi.
الِاسْتِثْنَاءُ (al-istithna): An exception uttered in speech, e.g., in divorce: 'You are divorced except if...' The validity depends on whether it is heard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Karkhi, what is the minimum requirement for mukhafatah (silent recitation)?
A) To make others hear.
B) To make oneself hear.
C) To correctly pronounce the letters.
D) To recite with full voice.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two definitions of jahr and mukhafatah; the relied-upon view (al-Hindwani) requires the speaker to hear himself for the utterance to be valid in speech acts like talaq and istithna.

The Definitions of Jahr and Ikhfa' in Hanafi Fiqh: Al-Karkhi vs Al-Hinduwani
Explaining intra-Hanafi disagreement on jahr and ikhfa' and legal consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of jahr and ikhfa' according to al-Karkhi and al-Hinduwani, and apply each definition to determine the occurrence of talaq, itq, and istithna'.

Core Idea
Jahr and ikhfa' definitions differ: self-audible vs others-audible; this affects talaq, itq, and more.

In the Hanafi school, the thresholds for audible (jahr) and silent (ikhfa') recitation are not fixed uniformly. Two major early authorities, al-Karkhi and al-Hinduwani, offered different definitions. Their disagreement cascades into multiple fiqh areas beyond salah, including talaq, itq, and istithna'. This lesson unpacks their positions and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
List al-Karkhi's definitions: jahr = hearing oneself; ikhfa' = correct articulation. List al-Hinduwani's definitions: jahr = making others hear; ikhfa' = making oneself hear.
These definitions are about the minimum threshold.
2
Trace the evidence for each
Al-Karkhi's evidence: qiyas and a statement from Imam Muhammad in his Book of Salah. Al-Hinduwani's evidence: the view of the majority of the mashayikh and common understanding.
Al-Bada'i' considers al-Karkhi's view more analogically correct but most scholars follow al-Hinduwani.
3
Apply to talaq and itq
If a person pronounces talaq or itq such that he himself does not hear his own utterance: under al-Karkhi, talaq occurs; under al-Hinduwani, it does not.
4
Apply to istithna'
A person makes an exception (istithna') in such a low voice that he himself does not hear it. Under al-Karkhi, the exception is valid (ikhfa' is merely correct articulation). Under al-Hinduwani, the exception is invalid (ikhfa' requires self-audibility).
5
Recognize the scope
The same definitions govern tasmiyah on sacrifice, obligation of sajda tilawah, and the ruling on imam's recitation in silent prayer (if only one or two hear, it's not jahr according to al-Khulasah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جَعْفَرَ الْهِندُوَانِي وَعِندَ الْكَرْخِي أَدْنَى الْجَهْرِ أَن يُسْمِعَ نَفْسَهُ وَأَدْنَى الْمُخَافَتَةِ تَصْحِيحُ الْحُرُوفِ.
ترجمہ: اختفاء یہ ہے کہ مصلی اپنے آپ کو سنائے اور جہر یہ ہے کہ دوسرے کو سنائے ، یہ تعریف فقیہ ابو جعفر الہندوانی کے نزدیک ہے، اور امام کرخی کے نزدیک جہر کی ادنی مقدار یہ ہے کہ قاری اپنے آپ کو سنائے ،اور مخافت کی ادنی مقدار حروف کی تصیح ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ پر فقہی مسئلہ کی تفریح کی ہے، مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی بیوی سے انتِ طَالِقٌ ، یا غلام سے انتَ حُر “ کہا اور کہنے والے نے بذاتِ خود نہیں سنا، تو امام کرخی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک طلاق اور عتاق واقع ہو جائیں گے، اور امام ابو جعفر ہندوانی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک واقع نہیں ہوں گے۔ اور اسی طرح اگر ان دونوں کے ساتھ جہر کیا اور استثناء کا ایسے طور پر اخفاء کیا کہ خود بھی نہیں سن سکا تو امام کرخی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک طلاق اور عناق واقع نہیں ہوں گے اور استثناء معتبر ہوگا، اور امام ابو جعفر ہندوانی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک دونوں فی الحال واقع ہو جائیں گے اور استثناء معتبر نہیں ہو گا ، اور اسی اختلاف پر ذبیحہ پر تسمیہ پڑھنا اور وجوب سجدہ تلاوت ہے۔
الهداية كتاب الصلاة ، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۱۹، ط: رحمانيه وَلَمْ يُبَيِّنُ الْمُصَنِّفُ حَدَّ الْجَهْرِ وَالْأَخِفَّاءِ لِلاخْتِلَافِ مَعَ اخْتِلَافِ النَّصْحِيحِ فَذَهَبَ الْكَرْخِيُّ إِلَى أَنَّ أَدْنَى الْجَهْرِ أَنْ يُسْمِعَ نَفْسَهُ وَأَدْنَى الْمُخَافَتَةِ تَصْحِيحُ الْحُرُوفِ، وَفِي الْبَدَائِعِ : مَا قَالَهُ الْكَرْخِيُّ أَقْيَسُ وَأَصَحُ، وَفِي كِتَابِ الصَّلَاةِ لِمُحَمَّدٍ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَيْهِ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ: إِنْ شَاءَ قَرَأَ فِي نَفْسِهِ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ جَهَرَ وَأَسْمَعَ نَفْسَهُ . وَأَكْثَرُ الْمَشَايِخِ عَلَى أَنَّ الصَّحِيحَ أَنَّ الْجَهْرَ أَنْ يُسْمِعَ غَيْرَهُ وَالْمُخَافَتَةَ أَنْ يُسْمِعَ نَفْسَهُ ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الْهِنْدُوَانِيُّ ، وَكَذَا كُلُّ مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالنُّطْقِ كَالتَّسْمِيَةِ عَلَى النَّبِيحَةِ وَوُجُوبِ السَّجْدَةِ بِالتَّلَاوَةِ وَالْعَتَاقِ وَالطَّلَاقِ وَالاسْتِثْنَاءِ حَتَّى لَوْ طَلَّقَ وَلَمْ يُسْمِعُ نَفْسَهُ لَا يَقَعُ، وَإِنْ صَحْحَ الْحُرُوقَ، وَفِي الْخُلاصَةِ الْإِمَامُ إِذَا قَرَأَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْمُخَافَتَةِ بِحَيْتُ سَمِعَ رَجُلٌ أَوْ رَجُلَانِ لَا يَكُونُ جَهْرًا وَالْجَهْرُ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ الْكُلُّ.
Ja'far al-Hinduwani and according to al-Karkhi the minimum of jahr is that he makes himself hear, and the minimum of ikhfa' is the correct articulation of letters. Translation: Ikhfa' is that the worshipper makes himself hear, and jahr is that he makes another hear. This definition is according to Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani, and according to Imam al-Karkhi the minimum of jahr is that the reciter makes himself hear, and the minimum of ikhfa' is the correct articulation of letters. Explanation: The author of Hidayah has derived a fiqh ruling from the mentioned principle. The ruling is that if a person said to his wife 'anti taliq' or to his slave 'anta hurr' and the speaker himself did not hear it, then according to Imam al-Karkhi talaq and itq occur, and according to Imam Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani they do not occur. Similarly, if he said both with jahr and made istithna' in such a way that he himself could not hear it, then according to Imam al-Karkhi talaq and itq do not occur and the istithna' is valid, and according to Imam al-Hinduwani both occur immediately and the istithna' is not valid. And based on this difference is the matter of reciting tasmiyah over the sacrificial animal and the obligation of sajda tilawat. Al-Hidayah, Book of Salah, Chapter on Recitation, vol 1 p 119, Rahmaniyyah: 'And the author did not define the limit of jahr and ikhfa' due to difference with the difference of the correct [view]. So al-Karkhi held that the minimum of jahr is to make oneself hear, and the minimum of ikhfa' is the correct articulation of letters. In al-Bada'i': What al-Karkhi said is more analogical and more correct. And in the Book of Salah of Muhammad there is an indication to it, for he said: If he wishes he recites in himself, and if he wishes he recites aloud and makes himself hear. And most of the mashayikh are of the view that the correct is that jahr is to make others hear, and ikhfa' is to make oneself hear, and that is the statement of al-Hinduwani. And likewise everything that relates to speech, such as tasmiyah over the sacrifice, obligation of sajda tilawah, itq, talaq, and istithna'. So much so that if he divorces and does not make himself hear, it does not occur, even if he correctly articulates the letters. And in al-Khulasah: The imam when he recites in silent prayer such that one or two men hear it, it is not jahr, and jahr is that all hear it.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the definitions of jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfa' (silent recitation). Two prominent Hanafi scholars, al-Karkhi and al-Hinduwani, differ on the minimal threshold for each. For al-Karkhi, jahr means the reciter hears himself, and ikhfa' means correct articulation of letters even if not heard by oneself. For al-Hinduwani, jahr means making others hear, and ikhfa' means making oneself hear. The passage then applies this to several rulings: if a man says 'you are divorced' or 'you are free' without hearing himself, al-Karkhi deems it effective while al-Hinduwani does not. Similarly, if he makes an exception (istithna') inaudible to himself, al-Karkhi validates the exception while al-Hinduwani rejects it. The same principle extends to reciting tasmiyah over a sacrificial animal and the obligation of prostration of recitation (sajda tilawah). The text notes that al-Bada'i' considers al-Karkhi's definition more analogically sound, but most mashayikh prefer al-Hinduwani's view. The final reference from al-Khulasah clarifies that in silent prayer, if one or two people hear the imam, it does not constitute jahr; jahr requires all to hear.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation; al-Karkhi: hearing oneself; al-Hinduwani: making others hear.
المخافتة (al-mukhafatah): Silent recitation; al-Karkhi: correct articulation of letters; al-Hinduwani: making oneself hear.
اختفاء (al-ikhfā’): Concealing recitation; synonymous with mukhafatah in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man pronounces divorce ('anti taliq') in a voice that he himself cannot hear. According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (al-Hinduwani's view), does the divorce occur?
A) Yes, because the utterance itself is sufficient.
B) No, because the minimum of jahr according to the majority is making others hear, which was not achieved.
C) Yes, because al-Karkhi's view, which is more analogically sound, would rule occurrence.
D) No, because ikhfa' requires hearing oneself, and he did not hear.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains diverse positions on the definitions of jahr and ikhfa', and these definitions have practical consequences in talaq, itq, istithna', and ibadat.

Impermissibility of Adults Following a Child as Imam in Prayer
Two principles proving child's imamah invalid for adults

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi principles that prohibit a child leading adults in fard prayer and apply them to evaluate similar scenarios.

Core Idea
An adult cannot follow a child in fard prayer because the child's prayer is nafl and the strong cannot build upon the weak.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents two foundational Hanafi principles that establish the impermissibility of adults praying behind a child imam. The first principle prohibits a muftarid (one performing fard) from following a mutanaffil (one performing nafl). The second principle states that the strong cannot build upon the weak, with the child's prayer considered weak relative to the adult's. These principles are then applied to the specific case of child imamah and contrasted with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two principles
First principle: a person performing fard cannot follow a person performing nafl. Second principle: the strong cannot build upon the weak.
These are the core of the Hanafi proof.
2
Apply to child imam case
A child's prayer is nafl (not fard) because the child is not legally obligated. Therefore, an adult performing fard would be a muftarid following a mutanaffil, violating the first principle. The child's prayer is also weak because if invalidated, it does not require qada, whereas an adult's does, violating the second principle.
The second principle extends the prohibition even to nafl prayers.
3
Examine the Hanafi position and proof
The Hanafi school rules it impermissible (haram) and the prayer invalid. The proof is the two principles and the consensus that a child's nafl does not obligate qada.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Compare with Shafi'i and intra-Hanafi differences
Imam al-Shafi'i permits child imamah in fard, arguing the child's prayer is valid as nafl and the follower's intention suffices. Some Hanafi scholars (mashayikh of Balkh) permit it in tarawih and absolute sunan, but the mainstream view rejects it.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi, prayer behind a child is invalid; in Shafi'i, it is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإمامة
(۸۲) إِنَّ اِقْتِدَاءَ الْمُفْتَرِضِ بِالْمُتَنَقِّلِ لَا يَجُوزُ .
ترجمہ: مفترض کی اقتدا نفل پڑھنے والے کے پیچھے جائز نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس اصول سے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ بالغ حضرات کا بچے کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ مکلف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ نفل ادا کرنے والا ہے، اور اصول ہے کہ فرض پڑھنے والے کی اقتداء نفل پڑھنے والے کے پیچھے جائز نہیں ۔
(۸۳) إِنَّ الْقَوِيُّ لَا يَبْنِي عَلَى الضَّعِيْفِ.
ترجمہ: قوی کی ضعیف پر بنا نہیں ہوتی۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدا یہ اس اصول سے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ بالغ مرد کا بچہ کی اقتداء کرنا کسی بھی نماز میں جائز نہیں ہے، خواہ نفل مطلق ہو یا موقت ہو ، وجہ یہ ہے کہ بچہ کی نفل نماز بالغ کی نفل سے کمتر اور ادنی ہے، کیونکہ بالا تفاق اگر بچہ نفل نماز شروع کر کے فاسد کر دے تو اس پر اس کی قضا واجب نہیں ہوتی ، اور اگر بالغ نماز فاسد کر دے تو اس کے ذمہ قضاء کرنا واجب ہے۔ اصول یہ ہے کہ ضعیف پر قوی کی بنا درست نہیں ہے، بچے کی نماز بالغوں کی نماز کے مقابلے میں ضعیف ہے اس لئے بنا درست نہیں ہے۔
✔
الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب الإمامة، ج ۱ ص ۱۲۶، ط: رحمانیہ اقْتِدَاء الْبَالِغِينَ بِالصَّبْيَانِ فِى الْفَرَائِضِ أَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ عِنْدَنَا ، لِأَنَّ الْفِعْلَ مِنْ الصَّبِيِّ لَا يَقَعُ فَرْضًا فَكَانَ اقْتِدَاءِ الْمُفْتَرِضِ بِالْمُتَنَفِّل.
بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الصلاة، فصل شرائط أركان الصلاة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۴۳، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ] فلا تجوز إمامة الصبي في صلاة القرض، وقال الشافعي تجوز؛ لأن العمل يصح من الصبى نفلا لا فرضاً، واقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل لا يجوز عندنا. المحيط البرهاني كتاب الصلاة، الفصل السادس عشر، ج ا ص ۴۰۶، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ] الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب الإمامة، ج ۱ ص ۱۲۷، ط: رحمانيه
إِمَامَةُ الصَّبِيِّ فِي التَّرَاوِيحِ وَالسُّنَنِ الْمُطْلَقَةِ جَوَّزَهُ مَشَايِخُ بَلْخِ وَلَمْ يُجَوِّزُهُ مَشَايِخُنَا لِأَنَّ =
Chapter of Imamah (82) Indeed, the following of one performing fard by one performing nafl is not permissible. Translation: The following of a fard prayer by a nafl prayer is not permissible. Explanation: The author of Hidayah is explaining through this principle that adults following a child is not permissible, because due to not being obligated, he is performing nafl, and the principle is that a person performing fard cannot follow a person performing nafl. (83) Indeed, the strong does not build upon the weak. Translation: The strong does not build upon the weak. Explanation: The author of Hidayah is explaining through this principle that an adult man following a child is not permissible in any prayer, whether it is absolute nafl or time-bound nafl. The reason is that the child's nafl prayer is inferior and lower than the adult's nafl, because by consensus if a child starts a nafl prayer and invalidates it, making it up is not obligatory upon him, whereas if an adult invalidates a prayer, making it up is obligatory upon him. The principle is that building the strong upon the weak is not correct; the child's prayer is weak compared to the adult's prayer, so building upon it is not correct. ✓ Al-Hidayah: Book of Salah, Chapter of Imamah, vol 1 p 126, Rahmaniyyah: 'The following of adults by children in fard prayers is not permissible according to us, because the child's action does not constitute fard, so it is following of one performing fard by one performing nafl.' Bada'i' al-Sana'i': Book of Salah, Section on Conditions of Prayer Pillars, vol 1 p 143, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyyah: 'So the imamah of a child in fard prayer is not permissible, and al-Shafi'i said it is permissible, because the action is valid from the child as nafl not fard, and following of a muftarid by a mutanaffil is not permissible according to us.' Al-Muhit al-Burhani: Book of Salah, Chapter Sixteen, vol 1 p 406, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyyah. Al-Hidayah: Book of Salah, Chapter of Imamah, vol 1 p 127, Rahmaniyyah: 'The imamah of a child in tarawih and absolute sunan was permitted by the mashayikh of Balkh and not permitted by our mashayikh because ='
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage establishes two principles from the Hanafi school regarding the impermissibility of adults following a child as imam in prayer. The first principle (82) states that a person performing fard cannot follow a person performing nafl. Since a child's prayer is nafl (the child is not obligated for fard), an adult following a child would violate this principle. The second principle (83) adds that the strong cannot build upon the weak. The child's prayer is considered weak compared to the adult's, because if a child invalidates a nafl prayer, it is not obligatory to make it up, whereas an adult must make up any invalidated prayer. Therefore, an adult cannot rely on the child's prayer as a basis for his own. The passage also notes a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i, who permits a child leading adults in fard prayer, relying on the child's valid nafl. There is also an internal Hanafi disagreement regarding tarawih and absolute sunan prayers: some scholars (mashayikh of Balkh) permit a child leading adults in these, but the mainstream Hanafi view rejects it.

Key Terms
المفترض (al-muftarid): A person performing an obligatory (fard) prayer.
المتنفل (al-mutanaffil): A person performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
اقتداء (iqtidā’): Following an imam in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it impermissible for an adult to pray behind a child as imam in fard prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because a child is not held accountable for his actions.
B) Because the child's prayer is considered nafl, and an adult performing fard cannot follow a nafl prayer.
C) Because the child cannot recite properly.
D) Because the child must have reached puberty.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits adults from following a child in any prayer because the child's prayer is considered nafl and weak, based on two principles: muftarid cannot follow mutanaffil, and the strong cannot build upon the weak.
