A) He may continue his prayer because it is not invalidated.
B) He must repeat the prayer because insanity is a rare event not covered by the hadith on vomiting.
C) He should turn away and perform ablution, then continue.
D) His prayer is valid because it was not his fault.

Key Takeaway
Rare events during prayer are not analogically included in textual rulings for common events; they fall under original qiyas and thus invalidate the prayer, requiring repetition.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Exiting Prayer: Fard or Not?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on exiting prayer as fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) on whether exiting prayer by one's own action is fard, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says exiting prayer is fard; the Sahibayn say it is not—the relied-upon view is the Sahibayn's.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi difference: whether the act of ending prayer (e.g., saying salam) is obligatory (fard) or not. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it fard, while his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree. Understanding this dispute is essential because it affects the validity of prayer in twelve specific cases listed in Al-Hidayah, all occurring after sitting for tashahhud. We will clarify the positions, their practical consequences, and the later preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Recall that Abu Hanifa holds exiting prayer by a deliberate act (like salam) as fard; the Sahibayn hold it is not fard.
This is a pure intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not between madhhabs.
2
Identify the thamarah (practical consequence)
According to Abu Hanifa, if one intentionally omits the salam, the prayer is invalid. According to the Sahibayn, the prayer remains valid but is makruh (disliked).
This difference matters in cases where the worshipper must choose to exit or continue.
3
Examine the subsidiary cases
The text mentions twelve cases (e.g., finding water after tayammum, learning a surah after being ummi) where this principle applies. In each, the ruling hinges on whether exiting is fard or not.
These cases are memorization anchors for the principle.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., Al-Haskafi, Ibn Abidin) prefer the Sahibayn's view: exiting by salam is sunnah, not fard. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Therefore, if someone intentionally omits salam, their prayer is valid but makruh tanzihan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۹) إِنَّ الْخُرُوجَ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ بِصُنْعِ الْمُصَلَّى فَرَضْ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لَيْسَ بِفَرْضِ عِنْدَهُمَا. ترجمہ: امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مصلی کا اختیاری فعل کے ساتھ نماز سے نکلنا فرض ہے اور حضرات صاحبین کے نزدیک فرض نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ پر متفرع ان بارہ مسائل کا ذکر کیا ہے جو تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد پیش آئیں: تقسیم کرنے والے مصلی نے مقدار تشہد بیٹھنے کے بعد پانی دیکھا۔ موزوں پر مسح کرنے والے کے مقدار تشہد بیٹھنے کے بعد مدت مسح پوری ہوگئی۔ مقدار تشہد کے بعد عمل قلیل کے ساتھ دونوں موزے نکالے، یا دونوں موزوں میں سے کوئی ایک نکالا۔ .... مصلی امی تھا پھر تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد اس نے کوئی قرآن کی سورت سیکھ لی۔ مصلی بر ہنہ تھا اس نے مقدار تشہد کے بعد کپڑا پا لیا۔ ... مصلی اشارے سے رکوع اور سجدہ کرنے والا تھا پھر وہ مقدار تشہد کے بعد رکوع اور سجدہ پر قادر ہو گیا۔ ... مصلی کو مقدار تشہد کے بعض قضاء نماز یاد آ گئی جو اس پر اس نماز سے پہلے واجب القضاء ہے۔ مقدار تشہد کے بعد امام قاری کو حدث ہوا اس نے امی کو خلیفہ بنایا۔ مقدار تشہد کے بعد فجر کی نماز میں آفتاب طلوع ہو گیا۔
Principle 89: Indeed, exiting from prayer by the action of the worshipper is fard according to Abu Hanifa, but not fard according to them (the two disciples). Translation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the worshipper's exiting from prayer by his own voluntary action is fard (obligatory), and according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is not fard. Explanation: The author of Al-Hidayah has mentioned, based on this principle, twelve cases that occur after sitting for the amount of tashahhud: The worshipper who was performing tayammum sees water after sitting for tashahhud. The one who was wiping over socks finds his wiping period has expired after sitting for tashahhud. After tashahhud, he removes both socks with a minor action, or removes one of them. ... The worshipper was ummi (unlettered) then after sitting for tashahhud he learned a surah of the Quran. The worshipper was naked then after tashahhud he found clothing. ... The worshipper was performing ruku and sujud by gesture, then after tashahhud he became able to perform them physically. ... The worshipper remembered some qada prayer that was obligatory upon him before this prayer, after tashahhud. After tashahhud, the imam (who was a qari) had a hadath and he appointed an ummi as his deputy. After tashahhud, the sun rose during Fajr prayer.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute presenting a key difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding the ruling of exiting prayer by one's own action. Abu Hanifa holds that it is fard (obligatory) to exit prayer by a deliberate action, meaning the worshipper must perform a specific act (like saying salam) to end the prayer. The Sahibayn consider it not fard; the prayer ends by intention alone or the act is not a binding requirement. The text then lists twelve subsidiary cases where this principle applies, all occurring after sitting for the amount of tashahhud. These include situations where a condition changes (e.g., finding water after tayammum, expiry of wiping period, learning a surah, etc.) The common thread is that the worshipper must decide whether to exit the prayer or continue, and the ruling depends on whether exiting is considered fard. Abu Hanifa's view would require a deliberate exit act, while the Sahibayn's view gives flexibility. The mufta bihi (relied upon) position is not explicitly stated here, but in Hanafi fiqh, the view of the Sahibayn is often preferred in later practice regarding the act of exiting being sunnah rather than fard.

Key Terms
الخروج عن الصلاة (al-khuruj 'an al-salah): Exiting the state of prayer, i.e., ending the prayer by a deliberate action like saying salam.
صنع المصلي (sun' al-musalli): The voluntary action of the worshipper, as opposed to an involuntary occurrence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle (89) in Al-Hidayah, what is the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Sahibayn) regarding exiting prayer by one's own action?
A) All agree it is fard.
B) Abu Hanifa says it is fard; the Sahibayn say it is not fard.
C) Abu Hanifa says it is not fard; the Sahibayn say it is fard.
D) They all say it is sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Exiting prayer by one's own action is not fard according to the relied-upon Hanafi position; it is sunnah, following the Sahibayn.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Dispute on Exiting Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Explains the principle and twelve applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the core dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding exiting prayer, and apply it to determine the validity of prayer in scenarios after the final sitting.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds exiting prayer by one's own action is fard; Sahibayn do not—this difference determines validity of events after final sitting.

This lesson unpacks an important intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The disagreement centers on whether the act of voluntarily exiting the prayer (e.g., saying salam) is an obligatory element (fard) of the prayer itself. While both sides agree on the basic acts of prayer, this subtle difference has major practical consequences for the validity of prayer when certain events occur after the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah). Through twelve concrete scenarios, the lesson reveals how a single legal principle ripples across diverse situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed element
The dispute is about 'al-khuruj 'an al-salah bi sun' al-musalli' – exiting the state of prayer by a deliberate action of the worshipper. Ask: what is the legal nature of this exit?
Do not confuse this with the final sitting itself; the final sitting is a different element.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa (RA) considers this exit to be fard (obligatory with definitive proof). The Sahibayn hold it is not fard; for them, the prayer is complete with the final sitting and the salam is sunnah or wajib but not fard.
This is a difference within the Hanafi school itself.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference appears when an event occurs after the final sitting but before the salam. According to Abu Hanifa, the prayer is still ongoing, so any event that would invalidate prayer during it (e.g., breaking wudu, seeing water for tayammum) also invalidates now. According to the Sahibayn, the prayer is already complete, so such events have no effect.
The key is whether the prayer is considered 'exited' or not.
4
Apply to one scenario
Take the case of a person performing tayammum who sees water after the final sitting. For Abu Hanifa, seeing water nullifies tayammum and since prayer is ongoing, the prayer becomes invalid. For the Sahibayn, the prayer is valid because it is already complete.
All twelve scenarios follow this same logic.
5
Recognize the pattern
The twelve scenarios cover various situations (tayammum, wiping over socks, learning a surah, etc.). In each, the ruling hinges on the same principle. Mastering this principle allows you to derive rulings for new cases that may arise.
This demonstrates how a foundational usuli difference generates specific fiqh results.

ترجمہ: امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مصلی کا اختیاری فعل کے ساتھ نماز سے نکلنا فرض ہے اور حضرات صاحبین کے نزدیک فرض نہیں ہے۔

اور حضرات صاحبین کے نزدیک قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کا پیش آنا ایسا ہے جیسے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد پیش آنا ، اور ظاہر ہے کہ سلام پھیرنے کے بعد کوئی عارض نماز کو فاسد نہیں کرتا، اس لئے قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کے پیش آنے سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ۔
(89) Indeed, exiting from prayer by the action of the worshipper is fard according to Abu Hanifa, not fard according to them (the two Sahibayn). Translation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, exiting the prayer with the voluntary action of the worshipper is fard, and according to the respected Sahibayn, it is not fard. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah has mentioned twelve issues derived from the aforementioned principle, which occur after sitting for the amount of tashahhud: - The worshipper performing tayammum saw water after sitting for the amount of tashahhud. - The one wiping over leather socks had his period of wiping expire after sitting for the amount of tashahhud. - After the amount of tashahhud, he removed both socks with a small action, or removed one of the two socks. - The worshipper was ummi (illiterate) then after sitting for the amount of tashahhud he learned a surah of the Quran. - The worshipper was naked and after the amount of tashahhud he found clothing. - The worshipper was making ruku and sujud by gesture, then after the amount of tashahhud he became able to do actual ruku and sujud. - The worshipper remembered some missed prayers (qada) that were obligatory upon him before this prayer, after the amount of tashahhud. - After the amount of tashahhud, the imam who was a qari (one who recites properly) had an hadath (ritual impurity), so he appointed an ummi as khalifah (substitute). - After the amount of tashahhud, the sun rose during Fajr prayer. = And as for its invalidation by the mentioned (causes) of insanity, fainting, and nocturnal emission, because the occurrence of these incidents is rare, so they are not within the meaning of what has come in the text regarding vomiting and nosebleed. [References] Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Salah, Bab al-Hadath fi al-Salah, vol. 1 p. 395, Dar al-Kutub al-Islami. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Salah, Bab al-Hadath fi al-Salah, vol. 1 p. 133, Rahmaniyyah. Usool-e-Hidayah Vol 1 ... after the amount of tashahhud the time of Asr entered while this person is in Jumu'ah prayer. The bandage fell off. ... The worshipper was wiping over a jabirain (splint/bandage), then after the amount of tashahhud due to the wound healing... ... The worshipper was a ma'dhur (excused person, e.g., with chronic incontinence) but after the amount of tashahhud his excuse ended, like a mustahadah (woman with chronic uterine bleeding) and others like silsal al-bawl (dribbling urine) etc. In these twelve issues, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer becomes invalid, and according to the respected Sahibayn, in all cases the prayer is completed. In all these issues, the principle and basis is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, exiting from prayer by the worshipper's voluntary action is fard, and according to the Sahibayn, it is not fard. Therefore, based on this principle, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the occurrence of these incidental events after the final sitting is like their occurrence during the prayer, and since during the prayer their occurrence invalidates the prayer, so if these events occur after the final sitting, the prayer becomes invalid. And according to the Sahibayn, the occurrence of these events after the final sitting is like their occurrence after saying the salam, and it is obvious that after saying the salam, no event invalidates the prayer. Therefore, the occurrence of these events after the final sitting does not invalidate the prayer.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the nature of exiting prayer by the worshipper's own voluntary action. The core issue is whether this exit (al-khuruj bi sun' al-musalli) is a fard (obligatory) element of the prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is fard, while the Sahibayn consider it not fard. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) manifests in twelve scenarios where an event occurs after the final sitting (qad'ah akhirah) but before the salam. These include situations involving tayammum, wiping over socks, learning a Quranic surah, covering nakedness, ability to perform actual ruku/sujud, remembering qada prayers, imam's hadath and substitution, sunrise during Fajr, time change in Jumu'ah, bandage fall, wound healing, and end of chronic excuse. According to Abu Hanifa, since the prayer is not yet exited, these events invalidate the prayer as if they occurred during it. According to the Sahibayn, the prayer is already complete after the final sitting, so these events do not affect validity. The passage also includes a marginal note from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq distinguishing invalidation due to insanity etc., which is rare, from vomiting and nosebleed which have textual basis.

Key Terms
الخُرُوجَ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ بِصُنْعِ الْمُصَلَّى (al-khurūj ‘ani al-ṣalāti bi-ṣun‘i al-muṣallī): The act of exiting the state of prayer by a deliberate action of the worshipper, such as saying the salam or committing an invalidating action.
فرض (farḍ): An obligation established by a definitive proof; omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in the twelve scenarios, what is the ruling according to the Sahibayn?
A) The prayer is invalid in all cases.
B) The prayer is valid in all cases.
C) The ruling depends on the specific scenario.
D) The passage does not specify.

Key Takeaway
The dispute on whether exiting prayer by one's own action is fard has practical consequences in many post-final sitting events, determining whether the prayer remains valid or becomes invalid.

The Principle of Exiting Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on a foundational principle about exiting prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on whether exiting prayer is fard and state the mufta bihi position with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: exiting prayer is fard; Sahibayn: it is not. The final sitting does not automatically end prayer.

This passage introduces a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh that affects many rulings after the final sitting. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ on whether the act of exiting prayer (khuruj) is a fard obligation. This difference leads to twelve specific cases where the validity of prayer hinges on this principle.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Clear state the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether exiting prayer (khuruj) is fard.
Abu Hanifa holds it is fard; Sahibayn hold it is not.
2
Identify the core proof for each
What evidence does each side provide? Abu Hanifa uses a rational argument; Sahibayn rely on the completeness of the final sitting.
Abu Hanifa's argument: the second prayer is fard, and you cannot perform it without exiting the first; thus exiting is fard.
3
Analyse the practical difference
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf: how does this difference affect real prayer scenarios?
Any event after final sitting but before salam: Abu Hanifa invalidates, Sahibayn uphold.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa in the Hanafi school?
The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn, as stated in authoritative works like Al-Hidayah.
5
Apply to an example case
Take a specific scenario from the hidayah (e.g., time of 'Asr entering during Jumu'ah after final sitting) and apply both positions.
This solidifies the practical impact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذه المسائل تبنى على أصل وهو أن الخروج من الصلاة بصنع المصلي فرض عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وعندهما ليس بفرض.
المحيط البرهاني كتاب الطهارة، الفصل الخامس، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۲، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
الهداية : كتاب الصلاة، باب الحدث في الصلاة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۳۳، ط: رحمانیه
These cases are based on a principle: exiting prayer by the action of the one praying is obligatory (fard) according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage. The text establishes a fundamental principle: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, exiting the state of prayer (tahrimah) is a fard act that must be performed by the worshipper's own choice (bisan' al-musalli). The Sahibayn hold that it is not fard. This difference affects twelve specific scenarios where an event occurs after the final sitting (qadah akhirah) but before salam. For instance, if the time of 'Asr enters during Jumu'ah prayer, or a wound heals under a bandage, etc. According to Abu Hanifa, since exiting is fard and has not occurred, the prayer is invalidated. According to the Sahibayn, the final sitting itself completes the prayer; subsequent events are like post-salam events and do not invalidate. The text provides the ruling with reasons but does not list all twelve cases individually.

Key Terms
الخروج بصنع المصلي (al-khuruj bisan' al-musalli): Exiting the state of prayer by an intentional action of the worshipper, specifically the salam.
القعدة الأخيرة (al-qa'dah al-akhirah): The final sitting in prayer after the last prostration, during which the tashahhud is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi of the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on exiting prayer?
A) Exiting prayer is fard.
B) Exiting prayer is not fard; the prayer ends with the final sitting.
C) Exiting prayer is sunnah.
D) Exiting prayer is only required for fard prayers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds that exiting prayer is not fard; the final sitting completes the prayer, and salam is wajib. This principle governs numerous cases after the final sitting.

The Principle of Mawquf 'Alayhi: Means to a Fard are Fard
States a legal principle and applies it to exiting prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that means to a fard become fard and apply it to the case of exiting prayer, identifying the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
If a fard cannot be performed without a prerequisite, that prerequisite becomes fard.

One of the foundational rules in Hanafi usul is that the means to an obligation is itself obligatory. This principle, known as mawquf 'alayhi, was used by Imam Abu Hanifa to argue that exiting a prayer (by saying salam) is a fard, because performing the next fard prayer depends on it. In this lesson, we explore the principle, its rational proof, and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Read the Arabic text: 'Innama yutawakkalu ila al-fard illa bihi yakunu fardan'. Recognize that this is a general legal maxim stating that whatever is necessary to fulfill an obligation is itself obligatory.
This is a rational principle, not directly from Quran or Sunnah.
2
Understand the Rational Proof
The principle is based on logical necessity: if a fard act cannot be performed without a prior act, that prior act becomes fard. Otherwise, the original fard would be impossible to fulfill.
This is a form of aqli dalil.
3
Apply to Exiting Prayer
Consider the scenario: a person is praying the current prayer, and the time for the next fard prayer begins. To perform the next fard, the person must exit the current prayer. Thus, exiting becomes fard.
This supports Imam Abu Hanifa's view that khuruj bisan'ihi is fard.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Disagreement
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) did not consider exiting as fard, limiting the application of this principle. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows the Sahibayn.
This shows that principles are not absolute; they can be overridden by other considerations like istihsan.
5
Recognize Other Applications
The passage gives analogies: earning for maintenance, and moving from ruku to sujud for prostration. Both are means to fard acts and thus become fard.
This illustrates the broad scope of the principle in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ مَا يَتَوَكَّلُ إِلَى الْفَرْضِ إِلَّا بِهِ يَكُونُ فَرْضًا.
ترجمہ: ہر وہ چیز جس کے بغیر فرض تک رسائی نہ ہو وہ فرض ہوتی ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے اصول مذکورہ کو امام ابو حنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کے مسلک پر بطور دلیل کے ذکر کیا ہے، جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دوسری نماز اُس کے وقت میں ادا کرنا فرض ہے اور یہ ممکن نہیں ہوگا کہ جب تک اس موجودہ نماز سے نہ نکلیں، پس اس موجودہ نماز سے نکلنا دوسری فرض نماز ادا کرنے کا ذریعہ ہے، یعنی دوسری فرض نماز ادا کرنا اس موجودہ نماز سے نکلنے پر موقوف ہے، اور چونکہ فرض کا موقوف علیہ بھی فرض ہوتا ہے، اس لئے موجودہ نماز سے نکلنا بھی فرض ہوگا، یہی وجہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک خروج بصنعہ فرض ہے ۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص پر نفقہ لازم ہے اور وہ بغیر کمائی کے حاصل نہیں ہوسکتا تو اس پر کمائی بھی لازم ہوگی ۔سجدہ فرض ہے اور یہ اس وقت تک ممکن نہیں جب تک کہ رکوع سے منتقل نہ ہو، پس یہ انتقال بھی فرض ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ فرض کا موقوف علیہ بھی فرض ہوتا ہے۔
Indeed, whatever is relied upon for the obligatory except by it becomes obligatory. Translation: Every thing without which reaching the obligatory is not possible, that thing is obligatory. The author of Hidayah mentioned this principle as evidence for the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. The summary is: performing the second prayer in its time is obligatory, and it is not possible unless we exit the current prayer. So exiting the current prayer is a means to perform the second obligatory prayer. Since that upon which the obligatory depends is itself obligatory, therefore exiting the current prayer is also obligatory. This is why Imam Abu Hanifa holds that exiting by one's action is obligatory. An analogy: if a person is obligated to provide maintenance and it cannot be obtained without earning, then earning becomes obligatory. Prostration is obligatory, and it is not possible until one moves from bowing, so that movement becomes obligatory, because that upon which the obligatory depends is obligatory.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage presenting a foundational legal principle: 'Innama yutawakkalu ila al-fard illa bihi yakunu fardan' (Whatever leads to a fard is itself fard). The text explains that the author of Al-Hidayah uses this principle to support Imam Abu Hanifa's position that exiting prayer (khuruj) is a fard. The reasoning is that performing the second prayer (e.g., 'Asr) is fard, and it is impossible without exiting the first prayer. Therefore, the act of exiting becomes fard. The same logic applies: if earning is necessary for maintenance, earning becomes fard; if moving from bowing to prostration is necessary for prostration, that movement also becomes fard. This principle is a rational (aqli) proof used in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
موقوف علیہ (mawquf 'alayhi): That upon which something else depends; the necessary prerequisite.
خروج بصنعہ (khuruj bisan'ihi): Exiting prayer by one's own action, specifically by saying salam intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle, why did Imam Abu Hanifa consider exiting prayer as fard?
A) Because the Quran explicitly commands it.
B) Because performing the next fard prayer depends on exiting the current prayer.
C) Because the Sahibayn agreed.
D) Because the final sitting is a pillar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that the means to an obligation is obligatory is a powerful rational tool, but its application is nuanced and may be limited by istihsan or other principles.

Principle: Building on Invalid Act is Invalid
States and applies the principle that building on an invalid act is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of al-bina' ala al-fasid to determine the validity of a latecomer's prayer when the imam's prayer becomes invalid.

Core Idea
A building on an invalid foundation is itself invalid — the masbuq's prayer collapses if the imam's prayer is fasid.

This lesson examines the Hanafi legal principle that any act built upon an invalid act is itself invalid. The author of Al-Hidayah applies this to a scenario involving a latecomer (masbuq) in congregational prayer. Understanding this principle is crucial for determining the validity of dependent acts in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its scope
The principle 'al-bina' ala al-fasid fasid' means that if a legal act is based on an earlier act that has become invalid, the later act is also invalid. The passage applies it to prayer, but it is a general principle.
2
Describe the scenario from Al-Hidayah
The imam completes the prayer and sits for tashahhud, then laughs or intentionally breaks wudu. This invalidates the imam's prayer. The masbuq (latecomer) who had joined the imam is still following.
The laughter or hadath occurs after the final sitting, so the imam's prayer is invalid.
3
Apply the principle
The masbuq's prayer is built on the imam's prayer. Since the imam's prayer is invalid, the masbuq's prayer is also invalid because it is built on an invalid foundation.
4
Examine the rational proof (qiyas)
The passage draws an analogy: moving from one pillar to another in prayer is considered fard because it is a means to the next fard. Similarly, exiting the first prayer (to perform the second) is a means to the fard of 'Asr, so it is also fard. This shows that means to a fard are fard, supporting the principle that building on an invalid act is invalid.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
The passage follows Imam Abu Hanifa's view. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) may hold a different ruling, possibly that the masbuq's prayer is not invalid. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْبِنَاءَ عَلَى الْفَاسِدِ فَاسِدٌ .
ترجمہ: فاسد پر بنا کرنا بھی فاسد ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اصول مذکورہ سے اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ امام نے مکمل نماز پڑھائی اور تشہد کی مقدار بھی بیٹھ گیا، پھر اس نے قہقہہ مارا ، یا عمد أحدث لاحق ہوا، تو امام ابوحنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک مسبوق کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی، وجہ یہ ہے کہ امام کی نماز میں سے جس جزء وصورة هذا التوسل أنه إذا تحرم للظهر مثلا فلم يخرج منها حتى دخل وقت العصر لزمه أداء العصر مثلا ولا عليه أداؤها إلا بعد الخروج عن تحريمة الظهر ، لأن العصر لا يتأدى بهذه التحريمة، فيكون الخروج عن تحريمة الظهر سببا يتوصل به إلى أداء العصر وأداء العصر فرض، وما لا يتوصل إلى الفرض إلا به يكون فرضا كالانتقال من ركن إلى ركن في باب الصلاة عد من الأركتان، وإن لم يكن ركنا فى نفسه كذا هذا لأنه لم يبق الأولى على الصحة لا يمكنه أداء الثانية لأن الترتيب عندنا فرض، ولا يخرج عن الأولى على وجه يبقى صحيحا إلا بصنع يوجد منه فكان فرضا، وهذه النكتة منقولة عن الشيخ الإمام أبي منصور الماتريدى رَحِمَهُ اللهُ. [البناية: كتاب الصلاة، باب الحدث في الصلاة، ج ۲ ص ۳۹۵، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ]
الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب الحدث في الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۳۵، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed, building on an invalid (act) is invalid. Translation: Building on an invalid thing is invalid. Explanation: The author of Hidayah is proving through this principle that if the imam completed the prayer and sat for the measure of tashahhud, then he laughed or intentionally committed a hadath, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer of the latecomer (masbuq) becomes invalid. The reason is that the part of the imam's prayer that the masbuq built upon is invalid. This principle is applied as follows: if a person enters prayer for Dhuhr and does not exit until the time of 'Asr enters, he is obligated to perform 'Asr, and he can only do so by exiting the tahrimah of Dhuhr, because 'Asr cannot be performed with that tahrimah. Thus exiting the tahrimah of Dhuhr is a means to perform 'Asr, and performing 'Asr is fard. Whatever leads to a fard is fard, like moving from one pillar to another in prayer is considered part of the pillars, even if not a pillar in itself. This is so because when the first prayer is no longer valid, he cannot perform the second since sequence (tartib) is fard according to us, and he cannot exit the first in a way that keeps it valid except by an action from him, so it is fard. This subtle point is transmitted from the great scholar Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may Allah have mercy on him).
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage explaining the principle 'al-bina' ala al-fasid fasid' (building on an invalid act is invalid). The author of Al-Hidayah applies it to a scenario: the imam completes the prayer, sits for tashahhud, but then laughs or intentionally breaks his wudu. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this invalidates the imam's prayer, and consequently the prayer of the masbuq (latecomer) who had joined is also invalid because his prayer was built on the imam's prayer. The reasoning is that the masbuq's prayer is connected to the imam's; if the imam's becomes invalid, the masbuq's prayer cannot stand alone validly. The text also includes a longer argument from Al-Binayah emphasizing that exiting the first prayer is a means to the second fard prayer, and that means become fard. This is linked to the principle from the previous lesson. The subtle point is attributed to Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi.

Key Terms
البناء على الفاسد (al-bina' ala al-fasid): Constructing a legal act upon a previous act that has become invalid.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer to congregational prayer who joins the imam after the first rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because the time for the prayer ended.
D) Because the masbuq should not follow an imam after the first rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that building on an invalid act is invalid means that if an imam's prayer becomes invalid, the prayer of a latecomer who followed him is also invalid.

Salah — Prayer

Principle: Building on the Corrupt is Corrupt
Establishes that a masbuq's prayer is invalid if the imam laughs in the final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle 'al-bina' 'ala al-fasid fasid' to determine the validity of a masbuq's congregational prayer when the imam's prayer is partially corrupted.

Core Idea
Building a valid act on a corrupted part is invalid — the masbuq's prayer fails because it rests on the imam's corrupted portion.

In this lesson, we explore a key Hanafi principle — building on the corrupt is corrupt — as it applies to a specific scenario in congregational prayer. When the imam laughs in the final sitting after tashahhud, his own prayer and that of those who prayed fully (mudrik) are complete. But the prayer of a latecomer (masbuq) becomes invalid. Understanding why requires grasping how the masbuq's prayer is structurally dependent on the imam's, and what happens when that foundation is corrupted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
We examine the ruling on a masbuq's prayer when the imam laughs after sitting for tashahhud. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the masbuq's prayer is invalid (fasid).
The imam's own prayer and the mudrik's prayer are valid because they are complete.
2
Understand the masbuq's dependency
The masbuq still owes parts of the prayer. After the imam says salam, the masbuq stands to complete his missed rak'at. His remaining prayer is 'built' upon the part of the imam's prayer that he caught.
This building (bina') is a key concept; the masbuq is not starting fresh.
3
Apply the principle
The imam's laughter corrupts the part of his prayer that the masbuq was building on. Since that part is corrupted, building on it is also corrupted.
The principle 'al-bina' 'ala al-fasid fasid' directly applies.
4
Distinguish the imam and mudrik
The imam and mudrik do not need to build on any part because their prayer is complete. Therefore, the corruption does not affect them.
This key distinction shows the principle's scope.
5
State the conclusion
Thus, the masbuq's prayer is invalid, and he must repeat it from the beginning after renewing his wudu if necessary.
The source does not specify repetition, but it follows from invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ: فاسد پر بنا کرنا بھی فاسد ہے۔

تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اصول مذکورہ سے اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ امام نے مکمل نماز پڑھائی اور تشہد کی مقدار بھی بیٹھ گیا، پھر اس نے قہقہہ مارا ، یا عمد أحدث لاحق ہوا، تو امام ابوحنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک مسبوق کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، وجہ یہ ہے کہ امام کی نماز میں سے جس جزء وصورة هذا التوسل أنه إذا تحرم للظهر مثلا فلم يخرج منها حتى دخل وقت العصر لزمه أداء العصر مثلا ولا عليه أداؤها إلا بعد الخروج عن تحريمة الظهر ، لأن العصر لا يتأدى بهذه التحريمة، فيكون الخروج عن تحريمة الظهر سببا يتوصل به إلى أداء العصر وأداء العصر فرض، وما لا يتوصل إلى الفرض إلا به يكون فرضا كالانتقال من ركن إلى ركن في باب الصلاة عد من الأركتان، وإن لم يكن ركنا فى نفسه كذا هذا لأنه لم يبق الأولى على الصحة لا يمكنه أداء الثانية لأن الترتيب عندنا فرض، ولا يخرج عن الأولى على وجه يبقى صحيحا إلا بصنع يوجد منه فكان فرضا، وهذه النكتة منقولة عن الشيخ الإمام أبي منصور الماتريدى رَحِمَهُ اللهُ. [البناية: كتاب الصلاة، باب الحدث في الصلاة، ج ۲ ص ۳۹۵، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ] الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب الحدث في الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۳۵، ط: رحمانيه

سے متصل قہقہہ واقع ہوا اس جزء کو اس نے فاسد کر دیا، لہذا اس جزء کے مثل مسبوق کی نماز بھی فاسد ہوگی، کیونکہ مقتدی کی نماز امام کی نماز پر مبنی ہوتی ہے، اور جب مسبوق کی نماز کا ایک جزء فاسد ہو گیا تو اب باقی نماز کی اس پر بنا نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ اصول ہے کہ فاسد جزء پر بناء کرنا فاسد ہوتا ہے۔ برخلاف امام اور مدرک مقتدیوں کی نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی اس لئے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ میں مقدار تشہد بیٹھنے کی وجہ سے ان کی نماز مکمل ہو گئی ۔

وَأَمَّا الْقَهْقَهَةُ وَالْحَدَتُ الْعَمْدُ فَصَلَاةُ الْإِمَامِ وَمَنْ هُوَ بِمِثْلِ حَالِهِ تَامَّةٌ وَأَمَّا صَلَاةُ الْمَسْبُوقِينَ فَفَاسِدَةٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، لِأَنَّ الْقَهْقَهَةَ مُفْسِدَةٌ لِلْجُزْءِ الَّذِى تُلاقِيهِ مِنْ صَلَاةِ الْإِمَامِ فَيَفْسُدُ مِثْلُهُ مِنْ صَلَاةِ الْمُقْتَدِى غَيْرَ أَنَّ الْإِمَامَ لَا يَحْتَاجُ إلَى الْبَنَاءِ وَالْمَسْبُوقُ مُحْتَاجٌ إِلَيْهِ وَالْبِنَاء عَلَى الْفَاسِدِ فَاسِدٌ.

الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الصلاة، باب صفة الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۲۵، ط: المطبعة الخيرية] أَنَّ الْقَهْقَهَةَ وَالْحَدَثَ الْعَمَّدَ مُفْسِدَانِ لِلْجُزْء الَّذِي يُلاقِيَانِهِ مِنْ صَلَاةِ الْإِمَامِ فَيُفْسِدَانِ مِثْلَهُ مِنْ صَلَاةِ الْمَأْمُورِ غَيْرَ أَنَّ الْإِمَامَ وَالْمُدْرِكَ لَا يَحْتَاجَانِ إِلَى الْبَنَاءِ وَالْمَسْبُوقَ وَمَنْ حَالُهُ مِثْلُ حَالِهِ يَحْتَاجُ إلَيْهِ وَالْبَنَاءِ عَلَى الْفَاسِدِ فَاسِدٌ.

تبيين الحقائق كتاب الصلاة، باب الإمامة، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۲، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي]

الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب الحدث فى الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۱۳۵، ط: رحمانیه
Building on the corrupt is corrupt. Translation: Building on the corrupt is also corrupt. Explanation: The author of Hidayah is proving from the mentioned principle that the imam performed the complete prayer and sat for the measure of tashahhud, then he laughed or had an intentional hadath. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer of the masbuq becomes invalid. The reason is that the part of the imam's prayer that he encountered, he corrupted it, so the like of that part from the prayer of the masbuq is corrupted because the prayer of the muqtadi is based on the imam's prayer. And when a part of the masbuq's prayer became corrupt, he cannot build the rest of his prayer upon it because the principle is: building on the corrupt is corrupt. Unlike the imam and the mudrik, their prayer is not invalid because by sitting for the measure of tashahhud in the final sitting, their prayer is complete.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling regarding the effect of laughter (qahqaha) or intentional hadath by the imam during the final sitting of prayer. The key distinction is between the imam himself and those who caught the full prayer (mudrik) versus those who joined late (masbuq). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the imam laughs or has an intentional hadath after having sat for the duration of tashahhud in the final sitting, the imam's prayer and the mudrik's prayer are complete and valid. However, the masbuq's prayer is invalid. The reasoning is that the masbuq still owes a portion of prayer and needs to build his remaining prayer upon the imam's. Since the imam's prayer contained a corrupted part (the part where he laughed), the masbuq's corresponding part is also corrupted. And building upon a corrupt foundation is itself corrupt. Various sources (Al-Binaya, Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq) are cited to support this usul-based ruling. The passage also includes a tangential discussion of the principle that what is necessary to fulfill an obligation becomes obligatory, using examples from prayer transitions and earning for nafaqah.

Key Terms
بناء على الفاسد (bina' 'ala al-fasid): The principle that building one's prayer (or any act) upon a corrupted part renders the whole construction invalid.
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late and does not catch the entire prayer with the imam.
قہقہہ (qahqaha): Loud laughter that nullifies prayer according to the majority of scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the imam laughs after sitting for tashahhud in the final sitting, what happens to the masbuq's prayer?
A) The masbuq's prayer is valid and he completes as usual.
B) The masbuq's prayer is invalid because building on a corrupt part is corrupt.
C) The masbuq's prayer is valid but he must repeat the part where the imam laughed.
D) The imam's prayer becomes invalid, so everyone must repeat.

Key Takeaway
The principle 'building on the corrupt is corrupt' means that a masbuq's prayer is invalid if the imam's prayer contains a corrupted part, even if the imam's own prayer is complete.

Completion of a Pillar is by Transition
Explains a principle and its application to hadath in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle of tamam al-rukn bi al-intiqal, apply it to a case of hadath during prayer, and identify the hukm level of the transition.

Core Idea
A pillar in prayer is incomplete until you deliberately move to the next.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a subtle but critical principle: a pillar (rukn) of prayer is not considered fully performed until the worshipper transitions to the next pillar. This principle has direct practical implications, especially when an event like hadath (loss of wudu) interrupts the prayer. Understanding this principle clarifies why certain parts of prayer must be repeated and how the school defines the completion of ritual acts.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Identify the exact wording of the principle: 'The completion of a pillar is by transition.' Understand its literal meaning: a pillar is complete only after moving to the next one.
This is a legal maxim (qa'idah fiqhiyyah) specific to prayer.
2
Identify the case study
The author applies the principle to a person who experiences hadath while in ruku or sujud. Note the roles: munfarid (alone), imam, or muqtadi. The rule applies to all.
3
Analyse the required action
The person must: (1) perform wudu to remove the hadath, (2) resume the prayer from where they left off (build upon), (3) NOT count the pillar in which hadath occurred.
The prayer is not nullified entirely; only the incomplete pillar is discarded.
4
Explain the logic
Because the transition from that pillar to the next is obligatory (fard/wajib), and hadath prevented the transition, the pillar itself was never completed. Without completion, it cannot be counted.
The transition is itself a wajib; its omission due to hadath renders the preceding pillar void.
5
Derive the hukm level
The transition (intiqal) is a wajib in Hanafi prayer. Its omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) if forgetful, but here due to hadath it is not performed, so the pillar must be repeated.
The principle distinguishes between the rukn (pillar) itself and the wajibat (obligations) like the transition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۲) إِنَّ تَمَامَ الرُّكُن بِالْاِنْتِقَال .

ترجمہ: ایک رکن کا اتمام دوسرے رکن کی طرف منتقل ہونے کے بعد ہوتا ہے۔

تشریح: صاحب ہدایہ اس اصول سے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی کو رکوع یا سجدہ کی حالت میں حدث ہوا، خواہ وہ منفرد ہو یا امام یا مقتدی، تو اس کو چاہئے کہ وضو کر کے بناء کرے اور جس رکن میں حدث پیش آیا ہے اس کو شمار نہ کرے، کیونکہ اصول ہے کہ ایک رکن اس وقت مکمل ہوتا ہے جب کہ اس سے دوسرے رکن کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے اور یہ انتقال فرض ہے اور حدث کے ساتھ انتقال متحقق نہیں ہوتا، کیونکہ منتقل الیہ (جس کی طرف منتقل ہوگا) نماز کا ایک جزء ہے اور حدث پیش آنے [؟]
The completion of a pillar is by the transition. Translation: The completion of a pillar occurs after transitioning to the next pillar. Explanation: The author of Hidayah is telling from this principle that if someone experiences hadath in the state of ruku or sujud, whether he is alone or imam or muqtadi, he should perform wudu and build upon (his prayer) and not count the pillar in which the hadath occurred, because the principle is that a pillar is complete only when he transitions from it to the next pillar, and this transition is obligatory (fard). And with hadath, the transition is not realized, because that to which he would transition is a part of the prayer and hadath occurred...
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage presents another Hanafi usul principle: a pillar (rukn) of prayer is not considered complete until one actually transitions to the next pillar. This principle is applied to a case where a person experiences hadath (invalidates wudu) while in ruku or sujud. Regardless of whether the person is praying alone, as an imam, or as a follower, they must: (1) resolve the hadath by performing wudu, (2) build upon the prayer by continuing from the point they left, and (3) not count the pillar in which the hadath occurred, since that pillar was not properly completed because the transition to the next pillar (which is itself a wajib/fard in Hanafi) was not performed. The principle underscores the importance of the sequential flow in prayer: a pillar is effectively exited only by initiating the next pillar, and if the process is interrupted by a nullifier, the previous pillar remains incomplete.

Key Terms
تمام الركن بالانتقال (tamam al-rukn bi al-intiqal): A legal maxim stating that a pillar in prayer is considered fully performed only when one moves to the next pillar.
انتقال (intiqal): The movement from one pillar (e.g., ruku) to the next (e.g., standing), which is an obligatory part of prayer.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, such as passing wind, urine, stool, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person experiences hadath while in ruku, what should they do according to the Hanafi school based on the principle that completion is by transition?
A) They should ignore the hadath and continue; the ruku is complete.
B) They should repeat the entire prayer because the ruku is nullified.
C) They should perform wudu and build upon the prayer, not counting the ruku.
D) They should perform wudu and start the prayer from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
A pillar of prayer is not complete until the worshipper intentionally transitions to the next pillar; thus, if hadath interrupts, the pillar must be repeated.

Repeating a Pillar After Hadath in Salah: The Hanafi Rule
Ruling on hadath during ruku/sujud with qiyas proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when hadath occurs during ruku or sujud and explain the rationale based on the transition (intiqal).

Core Idea
A hadath during a pillar does not invalidate the entire prayer; only that pillar must be repeated after wudu because its completion requires a valid transition.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Bahr al-Raiq: what to do if you experience hadath while in ruku or sujud. The Hanafi school holds that you can still save the prayer by performing wudu and repeating only the affected pillar. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that a pillar is only fully completed with a valid transition (intiqal) out of it, and hadath prevents that validity. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi approach to continuity (bina') in prayer and the importance of intention in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and its ruling
The scenario is hadath occurring during ruku or sujud. The ruling: after performing wudu, the person repeats the affected pillar (ruku or sujud) and builds upon the rest of the prayer.
This is specific to hadath during these two pillars; other scenarios have different rulings.
2
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The completion of a pillar is achieved only by the transition (intiqal) out of it. Since hadath invalidates the transition, the pillar remains incomplete, necessitating repetition.
The rationale is based on the definition of 'completion' of a rukn.
3
Apply to a concrete example
If hadath occurs during ruku, after wudu one returns to the standing position, performs ruku again, and then continues the prayer from where he left off.
Only the affected pillar is repeated; other parts remain valid.
4
Note the madhhab's uniqueness
Other schools may require restarting the entire prayer. The Hanafi school allows building upon the valid parts (bina'), reflecting its principle of leniency.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.

کے بعد نماز کا ایک جزء ادا کرنا بھی مفسد ہے اس لئے اس رکن کا اعادہ ضروری ہوگا، مثلاً اگر رکوع میں حدث ہوا تھا تو وضو کے بعد آکر رکوع کرے گا پھر بقیہ نماز ادا کرے گا۔
(قَوْلُهُ وَلَوْ أَحْدَثَ فِي رُكُوعِهِ أَوْ سُجُودِهِ تَوَضَّأَ وَبَنَى وَأَعَادَهُمَا لِأَنَّ إِثْمَامَ الرُّكْنِ بِالِانْتِقَالِ وَمَعَ الْحَدَثِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ الْإِعَادَةِ.
البحر الرائق: كتاب الصلاة، باب الحدث في الصلاة، ج ا ص ۴۰۴، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي (وَمَنْ سَبَقَهُ الْحَدَتْ فِي رُكُوعِ أَوْ سُجُودٍ أَعَادَهُمَا بَعْدَ التَّوَضُوَ (حَتْمًا) إِنْ بَنَى لِأَنَّ تَمَامَ الرُّكْنِ بِالِانْتِقَالِ وَمَعَ الْحَدَثِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ الْإِعَادَةِ.
After [the occurrence of hadath], performing a part of the prayer is also invalidating, therefore repetition of that pillar is necessary. For example, if hadath occurred during ruku, after wudu he should come and perform ruku, then perform the rest of the prayer. (His saying:) And if he has hadath during his ruku or his sujud, he performs wudu, builds upon [the prayer], and repeats them because the completion of the pillar is by the transition [out of it], and with hadath it is not realized, so repetition is necessary. al-Bahr al-Raiq: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Hadath in Prayer, vol. 1 p. 404, pub. Dar al-Kitab al-Islami: And whoever is overtaken by hadath in ruku or sujud, he repeats them after wudu (necessarily) if he builds upon [the prayer] because the completion of the pillar is by the transition, and with hadath it is not realized, so repetition is necessary.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Bahr al-Raiq explaining the Hanafi position on what to do if a person experiences a hadath (ritual impurity) during the ruku or sujud posture. The author explains that performing a part of the prayer after hadath is invalidating (mufsid), meaning that particular part is not valid, but the entire prayer is not nullified; rather, the affected pillar must be repeated. For example, if hadath occurs during ruku, the person should perform wudu, return, and perform ruku again, then complete the rest of the prayer. The legal reasoning (ta'lil) is that the completion of a pillar (such as ruku or sujud) is only realized by the transition (intiqal) out of it. If hadath occurs during the pillar, the transition with purity does not occur, so the pillar is incomplete. Therefore, its repetition is necessary. This is in accordance with the Hanafi principle that if an invalidator occurs during an obligatory act, one can build upon the valid parts after removing the invalidator.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity (minor or major) that invalidates wudu.
ركن (rukn): An essential pillar of prayer without which the prayer is invalid.
انتقال (intiqal): The act of moving from one posture to another in prayer, e.g., from ruku to sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abandon the prayer and restart from the beginning after wudu.
B) Perform wudu, return to prayer, and repeat only the sujud.
C) Perform wudu and continue from where he left off without repetition.
D) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated entirely.

Key Takeaway
Hadath during ruku or sujud does not nullify the entire prayer; the affected pillar must be repeated after wudu because its completion requires a valid transition.

Appointing an Unfit Substitute Invalidates Prayer
Ruling that appointing an unqualified person as imam substitute nullifies the imam's prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of istikhlaf when the substitute is unqualified and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) based on the imam becoming a follower.

Core Idea
Appointing an unqualified substitute turns the imam into a follower of an unfit imam, invalidating the prayer.

In congregational prayer, if the imam has to leave due to hadath, he may appoint a substitute. This ruling from Al-Hidayah clarifies a critical condition: the substitute must be qualified for imamate. If the only followers are a minor or a woman (unable to lead men), and the imam appoints one of them, both his prayer and the followers' prayers become invalid. The reasoning is that the imam becomes a follower of the substitute, and following an unfit imam invalidates prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam experiences hadath; only a minor boy or a woman are present as followers. He must appoint a substitute to continue.
2
Assess the substitute's qualification
Determine if the person is fit for imamate. In this case, a minor or a woman is not qualified to lead men in prayer.
Hanafi conditions for imamate include being adult, male, sane, and knowledgeable.
3
Apply the rule
If the substitute is unqualified, the imam's prayer becomes fasid (invalid). The followers' prayer also becomes invalid.
The passage states that both the imam's and the followers' prayers are invalidated.
4
Analyze the ta'lil (reasoning)
When the imam designates a substitute, he becomes a follower of that person. Following an unfit imam invalidates prayer.
The dalil is: 'mann iqtada biman la yasluhu lil-imamati fasadat salatuhu.'
5
Understand the effect on followers
The followers' prayer is invalid because the imam's position becomes empty (khalā') – the original imam stepped back and the substitute is invalid.
The cause for followers is: 'khuluwwu makan al-imamah 'an al-imam.'

Source Text

مجمع الأنهر : كتاب الصلاة، باب الحدث في الصلاة، ج ص ١١ ، ط: دار إحياء التراث
(93) Indeed, appointing as a substitute someone who is not fit for imamate invalidates the prayer. Translation: Appointing a person who does not possess the capability for imamate as a substitute will render the prayer invalid. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah is explaining through this mentioned principle that if the imam is overtaken by hadath and behind the imam there is only a minor boy or a woman, and he appoints one of them as substitute, then in that case the imam's prayer becomes invalid, because he appointed a person who is not qualified for imamate. And the rule is that appointing someone unqualified for imamate as a substitute invalidates the prayer. Therefore, the imam's prayer will be invalid. Al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Hadath in Prayer, vol. 1 p. 135, pub. Rahmaniyya: The appointing of one who is not fit for imamate as a substitute is a ruling, because when he is designated for imamate, the imam becomes a follower of him, and whoever follows someone not fit for imamate, his prayer is invalid. [Al-‘Inayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Hadath in Prayer, vol. 1 p. 394, pub. Dar al-Fikr] The aspect of invalidity of the imam's prayer is his appointing someone unfit for imamate, and the cause of invalidity of the follower's prayer is the emptiness of the place of imamate from the imam. Majma‘ al-Anhur: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Hadath in Prayer, vol. p. 11, pub. Dar Ihya’ al-Turath.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Hidayah that if an imam who is leading the prayer experiences hadath, he should appoint a substitute (mustakhlif) from among the followers to complete the prayer. However, if the only persons present are a minor boy or a woman (who are not qualified to lead the prayer for men), and the imam appoints one of them, then the imam's own prayer becomes invalid (fasid). The reasoning (ta'lil) is that when the imam designates someone as his substitute, that substitute effectively becomes the imam, and the original imam becomes a follower of that substitute. Since the substitute is not qualified for imamate (a minor or woman cannot lead men in prayer), the act of following an unqualified imam invalidates the prayer. Additionally, the prayer of the original followers (ma'mumun) is also invalidated because the imam's place becomes empty (when the original imam steps back and the substitute is not valid). Thus, the entire congregation's prayer is ruined. This ruling underscores the importance of proper qualification for imamate.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaf): The act of appointing a substitute for the imam to lead the rest of the prayer when the imam becomes unable (e.g., due to hadath).
مستخلف (mustakhlaf): The person appointed as substitute imam.
خلیفہ (khalifah): Substitute or deputy; here it refers to the person who takes over as imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid and the substitute leads the remaining parts.
B) The imam's prayer becomes invalid, but the followers' prayer remains valid.
C) The imam's prayer becomes invalid, and the followers' prayer also invalid because the imam's position is empty.
D) The prayer is valid if the substitute is a minor boy but not a woman.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a substitute imam must be qualified for imamate; appointing an unqualified person (minor, woman) invalidates the prayer of both the imam and the followers.

Actions Indicating Increased Khushu' Do Not Invalidate Prayer
Ruling that actions showing additional humility (khushu') are not nullifiers of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on crying and moaning in prayer due to remembrance of the afterlife, identify the dalil (qiyas), and apply the principle to distinguish between permissible and nullifying actions.

Core Idea
Any action in prayer that indicates increased khushu' does not invalidate it, because khushu' is the very purpose of prayer.

Prayer is an act of profound devotion, and the Hanafi madhhab recognizes that external expressions of humility can enhance, rather than nullify, one's prayer. This lesson unpacks a key principle from Al-Hidayah: actions that indicate increased khushu', such as crying or moaning from the remembrance of the afterlife, do not invalidate the prayer. We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling, its basis in qiyas, and its practical application in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is crying (buka') or moaning (aah) during prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that if the cause is remembrance of Paradise or Hell, the prayer remains valid (sahih); it is not invalidated.
Crying from worldly distress is treated differently and may invalidate prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites qiyas (analogical reasoning): the action is compared to tasbih (glorification) or du'a (supplication), which are permissible in prayer. The effective cause (illa) is that it indicates increased khushu'.
The dalil is not a direct textual proof from Quran or Sunnah but a rational extension.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does qiyas work here? Crying from devotion demonstrates khushu', which is the maqsud (purpose) of prayer. Since tasbih and du'a are permissible and enhance khushu', crying from devotion is analogous and therefore also permissible.
The argument is: [Crying from devotion] → [Indicates khushu'] → [Maqsud of prayer] → [Analogous to permissible acts] → [Ruling: not invalidating].
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The cross_madhhab_status is mukhtalaf_fih: some other schools may consider any loud crying as invalidating prayer because it resembles human speech. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on cause.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different understandings of what constitutes speech in prayer.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that crying from remembrance of the afterlife does not nullify prayer. This is supported by the authority of the zahir al-riwayah and the consistent reasoning of the Hanafi school.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the qiyas and the emphasis on khushu' as the essence of prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها
(۹۴) إِنَّ مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ الْخُشُوعَ لَا يُبْطِلُ الصَّلَاةَ. ترجمہ: یقینا ہر وہ فعل جو خشوع کی زیادتی پر دلالت کرے نماز کو باطل نہیں کرتا۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نماز میں ہر وہ کام جو خشوع میں اضافے پر دلالت کرے تو اس فعل سے نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی۔
اگر کوئی آدمی نماز میں آہ کرتا ہے یا نماز میں بلند آواز میں روتا ہے تو اب اگر اس شخص کا رونا جنت یا جہنم کے تذکرہ کی وجہ سے ہو تو اس سے نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ جنت یا جہنم کے تذکرہ سے رونا یہ اور زیادہ خشوع فی الصلاۃ پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور نماز میں مقصود بھی خشوع ہے، لہذا مذکورہ اصول کی رو سے اس شخص کی نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی ۔
الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكوه فيها، ج ۱ ص ۱۳۷، ط: رحمانيه وَإِنْ كَنَانَ مِنْ ذِكْرِ الْجَنَّةِ أَو النَّارِ لَا تَفْسُدُ صَلَاتُهُ، لِأَنَّهُ يَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ الْخُشُوعِ وَهُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ فَكَانَ بِمَعْنَى التَّسْبِيحِ أَو الدُّعَاءِ، وَهَذَا لَّانَّ الْأَنِينَ وَالتَّأَوَّهَ وَالْبُكَاءَ قَدْ يَنْشَأُ مِنْ مَعْرِفَةِ قُدْرَةِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَعَظَمَتِهِ وَغِنَاهُ عَنْ خَلْقِهِ وَكِبْرِيَائِهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ وَمِنْ شِدَّةِ الْخَوْفِ وَالرَّجَاءِ وَالرَّغْبَةِ فَيَكُونُ كَالتَّقْدِيسِ وَالدُّعَاءِ.
تبيين الحقائق كتاب الصلاة، باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكوه فيها، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۶، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
Chapter: What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. (94) Indeed, whatever indicates increase in humility does not nullify the prayer. Translation: Certainly, every action that indicates an increase in khushu' does not invalidate the prayer. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that any action in prayer that indicates an increase in khushu' does not invalidate the prayer. If a person moans in prayer or cries loudly in prayer, then if his crying is due to the mention of Paradise or Hell, it does not invalidate his prayer, because crying from the mention of Paradise or Hell indicates even more khushu' in prayer, and the purpose of prayer is khushu'. Therefore, according to the mentioned principle, this person's prayer will not be invalid. Al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter of What Invalidates Prayer and What is Disliked in It, vol. 1 p. 137, pub. Rahmaniyya: And if it is from the mention of Paradise or Hell, his prayer is not invalid, because it indicates increase in humility, and that is the purpose in prayer, so it is in the meaning of tasbih or supplication. And this is because moaning, sighing, and crying may arise from the recognition of the power of Allah, His might, His independence from creation, and His grandeur, and from intense fear, hope, and desire, so it becomes like glorification and supplication. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Book of Prayer, Chapter of What Invalidates Prayer and What is Disliked in It, vol. 1 p. 156, pub. Dar al-Kitab al-Islami.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a general principle: any action in prayer that demonstrates increased khushu' (humility and devotion) does not invalidate the prayer. The specific application is about a person who moans (aah) or cries aloud during prayer. If the cause is the remembrance of Paradise or Hell, it does not nullify the prayer. The reasoning is that such crying indicates a heightened state of khushu', which is the very goal of prayer. Therefore, it is analogous to saying tasbih or making du'a, which are permissible in prayer. The commentary from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq explains that moaning, sighing, and crying can stem from a deep awareness of Allah's greatness, fear, hope, and longing, and thus are akin to expressions of glorification and supplication. Hence, they are permissible. However, if the crying is due to worldly distress or pain, it may be considered human speech (kalam al-nas) and invalidate the prayer, as a separate rule (see next lesson).

Key Terms
خشوع (khushu'): Humility, submissiveness, and focus in prayer, both physical and spiritual.
آہ (aah): Moaning, sighing; an expression of distress or emotion.
بکاء (buka'): Crying, weeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, why does crying from the mention of Paradise or Hell not invalidate prayer?
A) Because crying is not a proscribed action in prayer.
B) Because it indicates increased khushu', which is the purpose of prayer.
C) Because it is a form of du'a.
D) Because the sound of crying is not considered speech.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that actions demonstrating increased khushu' in prayer, such as devotional crying, do not nullify the prayer because they fulfill the very purpose of prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Actions of Distress in Prayer as Human Speech
Ruling with proof via qiyas: worldly distress in prayer equals human speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that deliberate actions showing worldly distress in prayer invalidate it, and distinguish them from devotional expressions.

Core Idea
Worldly distress in prayer is like human speech and voids the prayer.

This lesson examines a key principle from al-Hidayah: any action in prayer that displays distress (jaza') or regret (nasuf) from worldly causes is considered akin to ordinary human speech (kalam al-nas). In Hanafi fiqh, deliberate human speech not part of the prayer nullifies it. Understanding this principle helps you distinguish between valid devotional expressions and invalid worldly complaints during salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and its cause
First, note the action in question: moaning, sighing, crying, or any expression of distress or regret. Determine whether the cause is worldly (e.g., pain, loss) or devotional (e.g., fear of Allah). The ruling depends on the cause.
The Arabic terms are jaza' (distress) and nasuf (regret/remorse).
2
Apply the principle of kalam al-nas
According to the principle in the text, any action that shows distress from worldly matters belongs to the category of 'human speech' (kalam al-nas). This means it is treated as if the person spoke ordinary words, even if no actual words are uttered.
The proof is qiyas: the action resembles speech in conveying personal feelings.
3
Determine invalidation of prayer
Since deliberate human speech invalidates prayer in the Hanafi school, this action also invalidates it if done intentionally. The underlying rule: anything resembling kalam al-nas nullifies the prayer.
Unintentional or forgetful actions may be excused; the focus is on deliberate expression.
4
Distinguish from devotional expressions
Contrast this with crying or moaning from devotion (e.g., fear of Allah, recitation of Quran). That is not considered kalam al-nas and does not invalidate prayer. The key difference is the motive and cause.
This distinction prevents confusion: not all emotions in prayer are the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۵) إِنَّ مَا فِيْهِ إِظْهَارُ الْجَزَع وَالنَّاسُفِ فَهُوَ مِنْ كَلامِ النَّاسِ . ترجمہ: بلاشبہ ہر وہ فعل جس میں جزع اور افسوس کا اظہار ہوتو یہ کلام الناس کے قبیل سے ہوگا۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ کام نماز میں جو کلام الناس کے مشابہ ہو تو ایسے کلام سے نماز باطل ہو جاتی ہے، مذکورہ اصول کو صاحب ہدایہ ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی آدمی نماز میں آہ کرتا ہے یا بلند آواز سے روتا ہے اور اس کا یہ رونا در دیا
الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكوه فيها ، ج ۱ ص ۱۳۷، ط: رحمانیه
(95) Indeed, whatever involves the display of distress and regret, it is from the category of human speech. Translation: Undoubtedly, every action that shows distress and sorrow belongs to the category of human speech (kalam al-nas). Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that any action in prayer that resembles human speech, such speech invalidates the prayer. After mentioning this principle, the author of al-Hidayah is proving that if a person moans in prayer or cries loudly and his crying is from ... al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter of What Invalidates Prayer and What is Disliked in It, vol. 1 p. 137, pub. Rahmaniyya.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents a second principle regarding actions in prayer that display distress (jaza') and regret/remorse (nasuf). Such actions, when they arise from worldly causes, are considered to be like human speech (kalam al-nas), and any speech in prayer that is not the speech of prayer (Quran, dhikr, du'a) invalidates the prayer if performed deliberately. The author of al-Hidayah uses this principle to distinguish from the previous ruling: if a person moans or cries from worldly pain or emotional distress, it is akin to ordinary human speech and thus nullifies the prayer. The cut-off text ('در دیا') likely indicates 'from pain' (dard). Therefore, the key distinction is the cause: devotion vs. worldly distress. The ruling from al-Hidayah would normally elaborate that if the crying is from a physical pain or worldly sorrow, the prayer is invalidated because it falls under kalam al-nas.

Key Terms
جزع (jaza'): Distress, agitation, lack of patience; in this context, from worldly matters.
ناسف (nasuf): Regret, remorse; possibly a variant of 'نَسَف' (to uproot) but here means sorrow.
کلام الناس (kalam al-nas): Human speech; words that are not part of the prayer (Quran, dhikr, du'a). In prayer, such speech invalidates if done deliberately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on this lesson, what is the ruling if a person moans in prayer due to a severe headache?
A) It does not invalidate the prayer because moaning is not speech.
B) It invalidates the prayer because it displays distress from a worldly cause.
C) It is permissible because it is an involuntary action.
D) It is recommended to continue the prayer without concern.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, deliberate expressions of worldly distress in prayer are treated as human speech and invalidate the salah.

Crying from Fear of Allah Does Not Invalidate Prayer
States the principle that actions increasing khushu' do not invalidate prayer and gives proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on crying in prayer due to remembrance of Paradise or Hellfire, and identify the underlying principle that actions increasing khushu' do not invalidate prayer.

Core Idea
Actions that increase khushu' in prayer do not invalidate it, even if they involve sound or movement.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi principle: actions in prayer that enhance humility (khushu') are not considered invalidating. The focus is on crying, moaning, or sighing that arises from the remembrance of Allah's power, Paradise, or Hellfire. We will examine the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, and understand how such actions are analogized to tasbih and dua.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
What is the specific action being ruled upon? It is crying, moaning (anīn), or sighing in prayer due to the mention of Jannah or Jahannam.
The act is not any crying, but that which arises from spiritual reflection.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling is that such crying does not invalidate the prayer; the prayer remains sahih (valid).
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The ruling is supported by Quran 17:109 and the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. The Quran praises those who weep in fear of Allah, and the Prophet’s weeping in prayer is recorded.
The dalil is both Quran and Sunnah (ahad).
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof applies)
The verse shows that weeping is commendable and thus not an invalidating action. The Prophet's practice confirms it. The crying is interpreted as an expression of khushu', so it becomes like tasbih or dua which are permissible in prayer.
5
Apply the principle
The principle is: 'Any action that indicates an increase in khushu' does not invalidate prayer.' Since khushu' is the purpose of prayer, actions that enhance it are analogous to glorification and supplication.
This principle distinguishes between spiritual and worldly crying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ الْخُشُوعَ لَا يُبْطِلُ الصَّلَاةَ. ترجمہ: یقینا ہر وہ فعل جو خشوع کی زیادتی پر دلالت کرے نماز کو باطل نہیں کرتا۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نماز میں ہر وہ کام جو خشوع میں اضافے پر دلالت کرے تو اس فعل سے نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ اگر کوئی آدمی نماز میں آہ کرتا ہے یا نماز میں بلند آواز میں روتا ہے تو اب اگر اس شخص کا رونا جنت یا جہنم کے تذکرہ کی وجہ سے ہو تو اس سے نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ جنت یا جہنم کے تذکرہ سے رونا یہ اور زیادہ خشوع فی الصلاۃ پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور نماز میں مقصود بھی خشوع ہے، لہذا مذکورہ اصول کی رو سے اس شخص کی نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها، ج ۱ ص ۱۳۷، ط: رحمانية وَإِنْ كَانَ مِنْ ذِكْرِ الْجَنَّةِ أَو النَّارِ لَا تَفْسُدُ صَلَاتُهُ، لِأَنَّهُ يَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ الْخُشُوعِ وَهُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ فَكَانَ بِمَعْنَى التَّسْبِيحِ أَو الدُّعَاءِ، وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْأَنِينَ وَالتَّأَوَّهَ وَالْبُكَاءَ قَدْ يَنْشَأُ مِنْ مَعْرِفَةِ قُدْرَةِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَعَظَمَتِهِ وَغِنَاهُ عَنْ خَلْقِهِ وَكِبْرِيَائِهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ وَمِنْ شِدَّةِ الْخَوْفِ وَالرَّجَاءِ وَالرَّغْبَةِ فَيَكُونُ كَالتَّقْدِيسِ وَالدُّعَاءِ.
Indeed, anything that indicates an increase in khushu' does not invalidate the prayer. Translation (Urdu): Every action that indicates an increase in khushu' does not invalidate the prayer. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that any action in prayer that indicates an increase in khushu' will not invalidate the prayer. If a person moans in prayer or cries loudly, and his crying is due to the mention of Jannah or Jahannam, then his prayer is not invalidated, because crying due to the mention of Jannah or Jahannam indicates an increase in khushu' in prayer, and the purpose in prayer is khushu'. Therefore, according to this principle, that person's prayer is not invalidated. Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Salah, Bab ma yufsidu al-salah wa ma yukrahu fiha, vol. 1, p. 137, Rahmaniyyah edition: And if it is from the mention of Jannah or the Fire, his prayer is not invalidated, because it indicates an increase in khushu', and that is the purpose in prayer, so it is like tasbih or dua. And this is because moaning, saying 'ah', and crying may arise from knowledge of the power of Allah Almighty, His greatness, His independence from creation, His majesty, and from extreme fear, hope, and desire, so it becomes like glorification and supplication.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school. The principle states that any action that increases khushu' in prayer does not invalidate it. The commentator explains that crying, moaning, or sighing in prayer, if it arises from the remembrance of Paradise or Hell, demonstrates increased khushu'. Since khushu' is the very purpose of prayer, such actions are analogous to tasbih (glorification) and dua (supplication). Therefore, they do not break the prayer. The text cites Al-Hidayah, which provides the proof: such crying arises from awareness of Allah's power and greatness, fear, and hope. This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
خُشُوع (khushūʿ): Humility and concentration in prayer, the purpose of which is increased by certain actions like weeping from fear of Allah.
أَنِين (anīn): A low moan or groan in prayer, which if arising from spiritual reflection does not invalidate.
بُكَاء (bukāʾ): Weeping in prayer; ruled according to the cause: spiritual or worldly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person cries in prayer due to the mention of Hellfire, according to the Hanafi school does his prayer become invalid?
A) Yes, because crying is a human action that breaks prayer.
B) No, because it indicates increased khushu', acting like tasbih or dua.
C) Yes, because it is similar to talking in prayer.
D) It depends on whether the crying is loud or silent.

Key Takeaway
Crying from the remembrance of Allah's power, Paradise, or Hellfire does not invalidate prayer because it increases khushu', which is the essence of prayer.

Crying from Worldly Pain Invalidates Prayer
States the principle that actions showing distress and regret are like speech of people and invalidate prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between crying that invalidates prayer (from worldly distress) and crying that does not (from fear of Allah), and state the Hanafi principle and evidence.

Core Idea
Crying from worldly pain invalidates prayer because it shows distress (jaza'), which is like human speech.

In prayer, not all crying is equal. The Hanafi school distinguishes between weeping from fear of Allah—which is praiseworthy and does not break prayer—and weeping from worldly pain or calamity, which expresses distress (jaza') and is treated like ordinary human speech. This lesson examines the evidence and reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (crying in prayer) and what the ruling is (invalidates prayer if from worldly cause).
2
Understand the principle
The principle states that any action showing jaza' (distress) or ta'assuf (regret) is like kalam al-nas (human speech), which invalidates prayer.
Hanafis treat non-verbal actions that convey meaning as equivalent to speech.
3
Locate the dalil
Identify the proof: Quran 17:109 praising weeping in fear, and the Prophet's (ﷺ) weeping. These show that crying from fear is valid. By contrast, crying from worldly pain has no such praise.
The dalil is used to establish the exception, not the rule.
4
Apply the analogy
Crying from worldly pain expresses human emotion and communicates distress, which is analogous to speaking. Therefore, it invalidates prayer.
The analogy is qiyas: worldly crying is like kalam al-nas in conveying meaning.
5
Distinguish from valid crying
Crying from fear of Allah, remembrance of Paradise or Hell, increases khushu' and is like tasbih. This does not invalidate.
The distinction hinges on the cause (sabab) of the crying.
